--- 段落 155 (462 字元) ---
- Q4: And there are a bunch of things we can talk about…  
- Marshall: Well, again, obviously we can come back to this later, but the CIA was a  complete flop on the Soviet economic things, the defense burden, which was  something I’ll come back to a little later.Also indicative of the situation was that  Kissinger was very interested in one of the products they produced, which were  these psychological profiles that Jerry Post and some people out there did.

[翻譯]
Q4：我們可以談談許多事情...
Marshall：嗯，顯然我們可以稍後再回來討論這個問題，但中央情報局對蘇聯經濟事務、防禦負擔等方面完全失敗，這是我稍後會回來討論的一點。說明當時的情況還有一點就是，基辛格對其中一個產品非常感興趣，這些產品是傑瑞·波斯特等人製作的心理分析。

--- 段落 156 (298 字元) ---
49  They were seen by the rest of the intelligence establishment as sort of very low  products, I mean not our first-line estimates.And yet Kissinger very much wanted  them, valued them, and you had to have a big fight with them to get them to  really produce them, to do more than they were doing.

[翻譯]
他們被情報機構的其他人視為非常低端的產品，我指的不是我們的第一線估計。然而基辛格非常想要它們，重視它們，你必須和他們激烈爭執才能讓他們真正製作這些資料，超出他們當時的工作範圍。

--- 段落 157 (413 字元) ---
Another thing was that we wanted to get them to attach probabilities to their  predictions, first to give alternative outcomes, not just one outcome as a forecast,  and secondly, to attach probabilities.That was a great trauma for them and you  never succeeded in dealing with it.During this period, RAND had been doing  some work on a thing that’s technically called “reproducible [reproducing] scoring  systems.

[翻譯]
另一件事是，我們想要讓他們將概率附加到他們的預測中，首先是提供替代結果，而不僅僅是一個預測結果，第二是附加概率。這對他們造成了巨大的創傷，你從未成功地應對過這個問題。在這段時間裡，蘭德公司一直在做一個叫做“可重現[再現]評分系統”的技術工作。

--- 段落 158 (472 字元) ---
”50 It’s a way of assigning a score for how close you are to the right answer  that provides an incentive for someone supplying an estimate to provide, in fact,  his best estimate, not to play games with the receiver of the thing.They had developed a really neat device of multiple-answer questions with three answers.They  had developed it, as a demonstration, for a whole series of different fields, like  Roman history or 17th-century music, or various kinds of things.

[翻譯]
這是一種方式，用來將一個分數指定給你距離正確答案有多接近的程度。這樣一來，提供估計的人就有了一個誘因，他會竭盡所能提供他最佳的估計，而不是與接收方玩弄把戲。他們開發了一個非常聰明的裝置，可以提供三個答案的多重選擇題。作為示範，他們已經為一系列不同的領域開發了這個裝置，比如羅馬歷史或17世紀音樂，或者各種不同的事物。

--- 段落 159 (434 字元) ---
The virtue of it  with the three potential answers was that with a light pen you could register your  relative probabilities among the three by the point on this triangle, the area of  this triangle that you could get.If A, if you were 100 percent sure, you put it at…  Why don’t we get back to that, I guess.Alright, maybe we just ought to take that up,  the transition of Net Assessment from the NSC staff to the Defense Department.

[翻譯]
其中的優點是，你可以用一支輕筆在這個三角形上點出你對三個可能答案之間的相對機率，你可以獲得的這個三角形的面積。如果是A，如果你確定百分之百，你就把它放在... 我們為什麼不回到這個，我想。好吧，也許我們應該討論一下，Net Assessment從NSC工作人員轉到國防部的過渡。

--- 段落 160 (375 字元) ---
The  main thing to say about the transition, I think, would be that Kissinger in the summer  of ‘73 had been appointed the Secretary of State and had the two jobs, but he was  beginning to spend more and more of his time over at the State Department.I  guess this all happened at the same time that Schlesinger came to Defense.I guess  he actually arrived on the 2nd of July.

[翻譯]
我認為關於過渡的主要事情是，基辛格在1973年夏季被任命為國務卿，並擔任兩份工作，但他開始花越來越多的時間在國務院。我猜這一切都是在舒萊辛格來到國防部的同時發生的。我想他實際上是在7月2日抵達的。

--- 段落 161 (335 字元) ---
Fairly soon afterwards, he called me, and  called me every week or two about coming over and setting up a net assessment  office in Defense.I had been somewhat hesitant about doing that.In the first place,  I wasn’t sure I was going to stay in Washington—ha, ha, ha, ha, ha.Secondly, Mary  for various reasons was against it and so on.

[翻譯]
不久之後，他打電話給我，每隔一兩個星期就打一次關於來設立一個國防網絡評估辦公室的事情。我一開始對這件事有些猶豫。首先，我不確定自己是否會留在華盛頓 - 哈哈哈哈。其次，瑪麗出於各種原因都反對這個計劃等等。

--- 段落 162 (391 字元) ---
But then what happened was really  a negotiated deal with Kissinger to transfer the whole office, not just that I would  come over and start over again, but that the whole office and responsibility for  net assessment, national net assessments would be transferred with me to Defense.- Q2: Who negotiated that?- Marshall: Schlesinger and Kissinger between themselves.So that’s what happened.

[翻譯]
但接下來發生的是真的是與基辛格進行了談判的一項協議，將整個辦公室轉移，不僅僅是我來重新開始，而是整個辦公室和對國家淨評估的責任將與我一起轉移到國防部。- Q2: 誰進行了談判？- 馬歇爾：謝爾辛格和基辛格之間進行談判。這就是所發生的事情。

--- 段落 163 (168 字元) ---
In fact, someplace around here there probably is a National Security Study Memorandum that transfers the thing.- Q2: NSSM 186?- Marshall: No, no, there’s several NSSMs.

[翻譯]
事實上，這附近可能有一份轉移該物件的國家安全研究備忘錄。- Q2: NSSM 186？- 馬歇爾：不，不，有幾個NSSM。

--- 段落 164 (474 字元) ---
There’s a NSSM that sets up the NSC net  assessment process, which probably came out in the early part of ‘73, when we  finally reached agreement about how we were going to proceed with net assessments from that point on, which was that they would be formulated through  some process at the NSC level, with consultation and so on of the departments,  and then they would be assigned to some department to carry out, depending  on the character or focus that they would have.

[翻譯]
有一個NSSM建立了NSC網絡評估過程，這可能是在73年初時提出的，當時我們終於就從那時開始如何進行網絡評估達成了協議。根據協議，這些評估將通過某種NSC層面的流程制定，並在諮詢各部門等過程後，會分配給某個部門進行執行，根據其特徵或焦點的不同。

--- 段落 165 (475 字元) ---
So there was a NSSM on that.51  Then there was a NSSM, NSSM 186—that’s where Project 186 got its number—  which was the first net assessment that was to be done, which was on ground  forces.52 It wasn’t completed until I came over to the Defense Department, when  it was conducted or headed on the government side by Pat Parker, who went to  work for, I forget the name of that fellow who was hissuperior, who…

--- 段落 167 (450 字元) ---
I sent him a letter, handwritten, so I don’t have a copy of it, telling him what I thought the problems were that he was going to face.I remember  the opening sentence or two says, “You’re taking over an organization with very  low morale that compares unfavorably with the people in the ‘50s.” I made the  point that then they were very activist, sought outside help, worked long hours;  now it’s become a routine eight-to-five job for these people.

[翻譯]
我寄了一封手寫信給他，所以我沒有信的副本，信中告訴他我認為他將面臨的問題是什麼。我記得開頭的一兩句話是："你要接手一個士氣非常低落的組織，與五十年代的人們相比，這些人的情況並不理想。"我認為那時他們非常積極主動，尋求外部幫助，工作時間很長；現在對這些人來說，這只是一份例行的朝九晚五的工作。

--- 段落 168 (490 字元) ---
They seem uninterested in anybody else’s information or knowledge, and so on.Schlesinger later  told me, “You certainly were right about that.” He said, “You could get trampled on  the stairways at 4 o’clock.I don’t know why they put lights in this building.”  The other thing about Schlesinger, that was already mentioned, was that he was  the first DCI from outside of the Agency.Well, that’s not right.McCone had been  from the outside.- Q4: McCone?- Marshall: Yes, he was a businessman.

[翻譯]
他們似乎對其他人的信息或知識都不感興趣。之後舽金格告訴我，“你當時確實是對的。”他說，“在下午4點，在樓梯上可能會被踩踏。我不知道為什麼他們在這棟樓裡裝了燈。”另一件關於舽金格的事情，就像之前提到的，他是首位來自機構外的中央情報局局長。哦，這是不對的。麥康來自外部。- 問題4：麥康？- 馬歇爾：是的，他是一名商人。

--- 段落 169 (417 字元) ---
- Q4: But no intelligence experience in the war?- Marshall: No, I don’t think so.At any rate, Schlesinger just scared them.In fact, there  were a bunch of the middle managers, including Proctor, who just hid when he  was out there.It’s hard to know exactly why he was so frightened.- Q4: Well, his personality, as I recall, would lead one to feel that way.He did not tolerate fools, to put it mildly.- Marshall: Yeah.

--- 段落 170 (437 字元) ---
He did, of course, even before he went out there… Well, in the first  place, let me just mention another part of the story.He and I had been talking for  some time because, while he took over in, I think, February of ‘73, right after the  election in ‘72, Nixon went up to Camp David, and then called the various heads  of agencies up there.He called Helms and, at least second or third hand, told him  he was not going to be continuing.

[翻譯]
當然，他在出任前就這樣做了...嗯，在第一個地方，讓我提一下故事的另一部分。他和我已經談了一段時間了，因為當他在1973年2月接手時，就在1972年選舉之後，尼克松去了戴維斯營，然後叫各個機構的負責人過去。他叫赫爾姆斯，至少是第二或第三手消息告訴他，他不會繼續做下去。

--- 段落 171 (480 字元) ---
53 When Schlesinger came up there, to talk  about the Atomic Energy Commission, which he was head of, he was told that he  was going to take over.So he and I began talking right after that; this happened  right after Thanksgiving.In December, he and I started talking about what do you  do with this place, who are the good guys, and various things.54 As I say, I wrote  him this longish letter about the situation and things I thought that needed to  be done for long-term goals.

[翻譯]

--- 段落 174 (328 字元) ---
The first thing I would say is my impression ended up that Kissinger, even going back to the initial studies he had me do  and then this monitoring of the reorganization of the intelligence community and  so on, that he fundamentally was not interested in all that.He was doing it, I think,  because Nixon wanted something done.

[翻譯]
我要說的第一件事是，我的印象最終是，基辛格即使回溯到他讓我做的最初研究，以及對情報界重新組織等方面的監控，基本上並不對這些感興趣。我認為他這樣做是因為尼克松想要完成某件事情。

--- 段落 175 (459 字元) ---
I think Kissinger thought the intelligence  products were terrible, but he is not someone who is at all focused on improving  organizations, changing organizations, making them better.His view, I think, of  the NSC was, “We can get what we want out of the intelligence organizations, for  the most part, so why do we care?” Schlesinger had a totally different view.Wherever he went he was very interested in the organization and changing or making  it better.

[翻譯]
我認為基辛格認為情報產品很糟糕，但他並不是一個專注於改善組織、改變組織、使其更好的人。我認為他對國家安全委員會的看法是，“我們可以從情報機構中得到我們想要的，所以我們為什麼要關心呢？”施萊辛格的觀點則完全不同。無論他走到哪裡，他都對組織很感興趣，並且致力於改變或使其更好。

--- 段落 176 (482 字元) ---
In fact, that may be one of the big distinctions among officials, one way of thinking about the people who come into government.That is, there are some people  who just want to do as well as they can during the couple of years they are there  and are interested in performing well, or seeming to perform well.But they are totally uninterested in the organizations or the processes.Then there’s a set of guys  who are really interested in trying to change things or make them better.

[翻譯]
事實上，這可能是官員之間的一個重要區別，一種思考進入政府的人們的方式。也就是說，有些人只是想在他們在那裡的幾年裡盡可能表現出色，對表現出色或看起來表現出色感興趣。但他們完全對組織或流程不感興趣。然後還有一群人真的很想試著改變事情或讓它們變得更好的人。

--- 段落 177 (495 字元) ---
The other thing is to look back at the performance of the intelligence community.Just really bad.Let me give you another example.I remember being called over  and going into the Situation Room.Then Carl Duckett [CIA Deputy Director for  Science and Technology] came down to break what was really bad news.In the  negotiations with the Russians, we had put a lot of emphasis with respect to the  SS-19, about what its size or volume could be and there were some specific provisions in the treaty.

[翻譯]
另一件事是回顧情報界的表現。實在很糟糕。讓我舉個例子。我記得被叫去到情勢室，然後卡爾·達克特（中央情報局科學技術副局長）下來傳達了一個真的很糟糕的消息。在與俄羅斯的談判中，我們對於SS-19洲際彈道飛彈，以及關於它的尺寸或容積都花了很多心思，條約中也有一些具體的條款。

--- 段落 178 (423 字元) ---
56 Those provisions had been guided by past Agency estimates  of what the volume or size of the SS-19 was.Duckett was there to tell us that the  calculations had been wrong.There was an error in them that had not been  detected for several years.It had been there for years.It was a simple thing of  some number had been divided by another number rather than the square root  of the number, or some damn thing of this sort.

[翻譯]
這些條款是根據過去機構對SS-19體積或大小的估算制定的。達克特在那裡告訴我們，這些計算是錯誤的。有一個錯誤在這些計算中多年來一直未被發現。這個錯誤存在多年了。這是一個簡單的事情，某個數字被另一個數字除以，而不是數字的平方根，或類似的某種東西。

--- 段落 179 (456 字元) ---
At any rate, the -19 was bigger,  very likely bigger, enough bigger that it would cross this threshold that was set  in the SALT I treaty.So if the Russians signed it as they probably did, or would, or  had—I can’t remember the date—they were already in violation of the thing, or  they were intending to violate it.I remember Haig and I and, I forget, there were a  couple of other people who were in there… I recall Haig being pretty upset about  it all.

[翻譯]
無論如何，-19更大，非常可能更大，足夠大以至於將突破SALT I條約中設定的門檻。因此，如果俄羅斯人簽署了它，他們很可能已經違反了這一條約，或者打算違反它。我記得海格和我，還有，我忘了，當時還有另外幾個人...我記得海格對此事感到非常沮喪。

--- 段落 180 (417 字元) ---
But again, it was just symptomatic that here’s this organization, probably the  TRW guys had made this mistake, nobody in the Agency had ever checked the  calculations or knew enough to check the calculations.Now, this in effect… not  real serious…  
- Q2: Does this relate to the SS-13, and that the -19 could only be so much bigger  than the -13 and there was an error on the size of the -13 or something like that?

[翻譯]
但再次強調，這僅僅是一個症狀，顯示出這個組織中，可能是TRW的人犯了這個錯誤，機構中沒有人曾檢查過這些計算或知道如何檢查這些計算。現在，這實際上不太嚴重...
- Q2：這是否與SS-13有關，-19只能比-13大這麼多，而對-13的尺寸有誤差之類的？

--- 段落 181 (484 字元) ---

[翻譯]

--- 段落 183 (443 字元) ---
And there was this error in calculations that I had known about, I mean I didn’t know about this thing, there was  this error in calculation, but I had thought it was based upon our estimated size of  the -13 so that therefore the projected growth meant the -19 could be so big, but  we were wrong about the size of the -13, which meant that the -19 was going to  break the limit.- Marshall: It could be.My memory is not that good.It could be.

--- 段落 185 (468 字元) ---
I guess one of the fun things about this period was the raising-of-the-Soviet submarine project.- Q4: Glomar Explorer.- Marshall: Yep.An interesting reflection: I talked with Schlesinger about it because  there was a set of issues about whether to go forward with it.57 And it goes back  to an idea, which we’ll maybe get into, of Schlesinger’s, and mine, too, this business of thinking about things you do in terms of their impact on other people,  on your opponents.

[翻譯]
我想這個時期有趣的事情之一是蘇聯潛艇項目的提升。- 問題4：格洛馬探險家。- 馬歇爾：是的。一個有趣的反思：我和施萊辛格交談過，因為是否繼續進行這個項目存在一系列問題。這又追溯到一個想法，也許我們可以深入探討，就是施萊辛格和我的，關於把你所做的事情想成對其他人、對你的對手有什麼影響的這種思維。

--- 段落 186 (485 字元) ---
His view was, yes, this is risky, but from time to time the U.S.should pull off some real exploit, just to shake up the other guy.- Q4: To keep them unbalanced.- Marshall: And this is sort of, therefore, the right kind of thing to do, not only for  its purported immediate payoffs that you get, but its perceptions, psychological  aspect of things.- Q4: Is this the period in which you were doing, they did the work on the anomalies,  the 56, the 58 anomalies, whatever we called them.

[翻譯]
他的觀點是，是的，這很冒險，但美國偶爾應該要進行一些真正的冒險行動，只為了讓對手感到震驚。- Q4：讓對手失去平衡。- 馬歇爾：因此，這是正確的做法，不僅是為了所謂的立即回報，還有心理層面的感知。- Q4：這是你們進行 anomalies、56年、58年的研究的時期嗎，無論我們稱它們為何。

--- 段落 187 (449 字元) ---
This is the things that the  Soviets are doing which we can’t find an adequate explanation for.- Marshall: Yes, I think that work was going on, and Herzfeld was much involved in  that kind of thing.Yeah, I think so.Anyway, the period, though, is kind of crazy, all this arms control nonsense going  on.When you see it up close and see how irrational it all is, and how subject it is  to these problems like this arithmetic about the size of the -19.

[翻譯]

--- 段落 197 (497 字元) ---
At any rate, the third thing was to undertake a development program of tools,  methods, databases, and so on.In addition to these formal things, Schlesinger used me a lot as an intermediary  with the intelligence community.Soon after he came here, he called Proctor down  and said, “I just find it hard to believe that the Soviet military effort consists of six  percent of their gross national product.Will you go take another look at that and  tell me why any reasonable man should believe that?

[翻譯]
不管怎樣，第三件事是進行一個工具、方法、數據庫等方面的開發計劃。除了這些正式的事情外，舒萊辛格經常讓我擔任與情報界之間的中介。他來這裡不久後，叫來普羅克特，說：“我真的很難相信蘇聯軍事努力佔他們國民生產總值的百分之六。你可以再去看看，告訴我為什麼任何理智的人應該相信這個事情嗎？”

--- 段落 198 (441 字元) ---
” When I came, he told me  about that and then we had some further meetings.Then they finally decided they  were going to write something and look at it, and they came back with a paper that  was totally unconvincing, that said the most it could be is, like, about one percent  off in either direction.Then in ‘76, of course, they… they’d known about it for  about a year, but in ‘76 they had to change it and move it up to 12 to 13 percent.

[翻譯]
當我到達時，他告訴我關於那件事然後我們進行了進一步的會議。然後他們最終決定要寫一些東西並查看它，他們回來的文件完全沒有說服力，只說可能差距在一個百分點以內。然後當然在'76，他們...他們已經知道這一點大約一年，但在'76年他們不得不將它的範圍修改為12至13個百分點。

And I have the paper, the memos that I wrote for Schlesinger back to them.59  
- Q2: What forced them to raise it?- Q4: Oh, it was the inflation rate.- Marshall: No, what forced them to raise it was an emigre who came out, who had  seen some books that were convincing to them.60 Plus, when they went and did  some work on the dollar-ruble exchange rates for some selected systems that  they had some evidence on, they decided that they had been way off for modern  systems.

There would have  to be an emigre who came and said, “I actually saw the books and it’s wrong,” or there was some very sensitive intelligence information in several cases that  would enable them to get a window of insight, which was not a random sample  window, but it was a window.And they have to go back and question themselves.But they couldn’t bring themselves to go about doing it on their own.- Marshall: Yeah.

[翻譯]
必須有一位移民來到這裡並說：“我實際看到那些書，結果是錯誤的”，或者在幾種情況下有一些非常敏感的情報信息可以讓他們獲得洞察的機會，這不是一個隨機樣本視窗，而是一個窗口。他們不得不回頭檢視自己。但他們無法獨自去做這件事。- 馬歇爾: 對。

--- 段落 203 (458 字元) ---
One of the first  things that we did when we got here was to take over responsibility for that and  having it finished.When the final report was being prepared, and we’d not had  much to do with it up to that time…  [gap for tape change]  …it called for a listing or discussion of the strengths and weaknesses on both  sides.When it came to the final thing, the intelligence people, the DIA guys,  simply would not put down any weaknesses on the Soviet side.

[翻譯]
我們剛到這裡時，首先做的事情之一就是承擔責任，確保事情完成。當最終報告正在準備時，而在那之前我們沒怎麼參與其中......在最後關頭，情報人員、國防情報局的人，簡直就是不肯在蘇聯一方列出任何弱點。

--- 段落 204 (398 字元) ---
At one point  they had made the preposterous explanation that, yes, they might have some  weaknesses, but even if they did exist, they would notice them and fix them, so  that it wasn’t worth talking about them or taking much notice of them.I remember saying to them, “Would that that were so about our weaknesses.” So it was  resolved, finally, by Lt.Gen.Danny Graham, who had just taken over DIA.

[翻譯]
有一段時間，他們曾經做出荒謬的解釋，認為他們可能有一些弱點，但即使存在，他們也會察覺並修正，因此不值得談論它們或太過關注它們。我記得對他們說過：“希望我們的弱點也能如此。”最終由剛接任DIA的Danny Graham中將解決這個問題。

--- 段落 205 (489 字元) ---
And  talking with him… Danny and I had gotten to know one another, I guess, while  I was still at the NSC.We had talked a lot about Soviet weaknesses, so he wasn’t  in any position to say that the Soviets didn’t have any weaknesses.So he got it  changed.But it’s just symptomatic of these people.The constant weakness of the  intelligence community, this unwillingness to really deal with, or to have an intelligent assessment of the opponent’s weaknesses.- Q4: Let me give you an example.

[翻譯]
與他交談時……丹尼和我彼此已經認識了，我想，在我仍在國家安全委員會的時候。我們討論過蘇聯的弱點很多次，所以他無法說蘇聯沒有弱點。所以他改變了看法。但這只是這些人的典型特徵。情報界持續的弱點，對真正處理對手的弱點或做出明智評估的不願意。－Q4：讓我給你一個例子。

--- 段落 206 (311 字元) ---
There were a whole set of four or five myths that  they had about the Soviet Army.One of which was that the Russians are stupid  because they design the T-62 tank and only somebody who was less than about  six foot, five foot-eleven, or something like that could fit into it.And they made  a big play out of it.

[翻譯]
有一整套四五個他們對蘇聯軍隊的神話。其中之一是俄羅斯人很笨，因為他們設計了T-62坦克，只有不到六英尺高、五英尺十一英寸高的人才能進入。他們對此大肆宣揚。

--- 段落 207 (489 字元) ---
And there was in a meeting with one of these intel guys and  a couple of people from the Army made this comment, and Pickett said, “Pardon  me, but do you have demographic data on the average height of the Soviet  male?” “Well, yes we do.” “What is it, what is the average height of the Soviet  male?” “Probably about 5-foot-6.” And Pickett said, “So are they designing the  tank…” Pickett said, “What is the height of a male who can climb in the Army M-  60?” And the answer was 6-foot-4.

[翻譯]
在一次與情報人員和幾名陸軍人員的會議中，皮科特說：“請原諒我，但你有關於蘇聯男性平均身高的人口統計數據嗎？” “是的，我們有。” “那麼，蘇聯男性的平均身高是多少？” “大概5英尺6英寸。” 皮科特說：“那麼他們是不是在設計坦克…” 皮科特問：“能夠爬進陸軍M-60坦克的男性身高是多少？” 答案是6英尺4英寸。

--- 段落 208 (428 字元) ---
And Pickett said, “Where is that on the height  distribution?” Guy on the Army staff said, “It’s on the 99th percentile.” Pickett said,  “Shall we go back and try this all over again about who is stupid?” And it was just  these… the guys who were doing [indistinct] analysis for the Defense Intelligence  Agency, had just a very narrow focus on that.It was just absolutely phenomenal.And there are other stories.- Marshall: Yes.

[翻譯]
皮克特說："這在高度分布中的位置在哪裡？"陸軍參謀的一名人士說："這是在第99個百分位數上。"皮克特說："我們要回去，再試一次看看誰愚蠢嗎？"當時這些在為國防情報局進行【不清楚】分析的人，對這個問題非常狹窄地聚焦在那一點。這實在令人驚訝。還有其他的故事吧。- 馬歇爾：是的。

--- 段落 209 (476 字元) ---
The other thing to say about this period is—I guess we talked about  it before, the last time—that one of the things that Schlesinger was very interested in, and, in fact, both of us were because we had talked a lot about it back  at RAND, was this whole aspect of the political-psychological impact or use of  military forces, their role beyond fighting, or getting your way without fighting by  looking impressive enough, and so on.I think we’d both been interested in that.

[翻譯]
這段時期要說的另一件事是，我想我們之前已經談過了，那就是施萊辛格非常感興趣的一個事情，事實上，我們兩個人都很感興趣，因為在蘭德公司時我們曾多次討論過這個話題，就是軍事力量的政治心理影響或使用，他們在戰鬥之外的作用，或者藉著看起來令人印象深刻來達到目的，等等。我想我們兩個都對此感興趣。

--- 段落 210 (323 字元) ---
I  had been interested in that going way back because of Goldhamer and Leites and  so on.Something that was very important for both Schlesinger and I, while we  were both at RAND, was reading Robert Ardrey’s The Territorial Imperative, which  immediately raises the issue of the nonrational aspects of man and his behavior.

[翻譯]
我很早就對這個感興趣，因為Goldhamer和Leites等等。當我們兩個都在蘭德公司時，對於舒萊辛格和我來說很重要的一件事是閱讀羅伯特·阿德里的《領土本能》，這立刻提出了人和他的行為的非理性方面的問題。

--- 段落 211 (383 字元) ---
63  Our interest was based partly on an obvious fact of history, that coercion and  display of forces and so on are used to gain your ends without fighting, and also  on the possibility that this is not just a matter of, you show up and the other guy  does a set of calculations and so on, but that there are other mechanisms at work  and that you ought to understand that and so on.

[翻譯]
我們的興趣部分基於歷史上的明顯事實，即使用脅迫、展示力量等手段來在不用交戰的情況下達到目的，同時也基於這種可能性：這不僅僅是你出現後對方進行一系列計算等等，還可能存在其他機制在發揮作用，因此你應該理解這一點。

--- 段落 212 (440 字元) ---
So one of the other things I did for Schlesinger, after sort of getting on board,  was to start this whole program of work on perceptions and so on.Now, actually,  when I was working for Henry, I had already started down this road by making a  request to the Agency—again, Henry was a naturally interested party in this kind  of thing—and so we… Remember this Bob Levine?- Q4: Um-hum.- Marshall: So we assigned this one guy to do this work.

[翻譯]
所以在加入後，我為舒萊辛格做的另一件事是開始整個關於知覺等工作的計劃。實際上，在為亨利工作時，我已經踏上了這條路，通過向機構提出了這個要求——亨利是這類事情的自然關注方——所以我們...還記得這個鮑勃·萊文嗎？- Q4：嗯嗯。- 馬歇爾：所以我們指派了這個人來做這項工作。

--- 段落 213 (453 字元) ---
The idea was to try to look  at everything we could find from the Soviets to find out: “What is it that they pay  attention to about us?What sorts of things seem to give us high scores in their  books?What things don’t matter or give us low scores?” In other words, how can  we then start to do those things or show those characteristics which impress  them and influence their assessments?When I got here, Schlesinger was very, very interested in this.

[翻譯]
這個想法是嘗試看一切我們可以從蘇聯找到的東西，以找出：「他們關注我們的哪些方面？什麼類型的事情似乎在他們的書籍中給我們高分？什麼事情並不重要或給我們低分？」換句話說，我們如何開始做那些事情或展現那些特點，以給他們留下深刻印象並影響他們的評估？當我到達這裡時，舒曼格對此非常感興趣。

--- 段落 214 (481 字元) ---
It was one of his  absolutely fundamental views about things.So I started this work.I got some  money from the Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency.Stephen Lukasik  was the head of DARPA then, and I think, probably, Schlesinger had called him.So I went over, and one of the first projects we started was the stuff that started  out at RAND with Herb Goldhamer in charge.There was a meeting at RAND.64  That’s when I first met Lionel Tiger, but I had read his book before that.

[翻譯]
這是他對事物的絕對基本觀點之一。所以我開始了這項工作。我從國防部高級研究計劃署得到了一些資金。當時Stephen Lukasik是DARPA的負責人，我想，可能是Schlesinger叫他來的。所以我前往，我們開始的第一個項目之一是在RAND由Herb Goldhamer負責的工作。那時在RAND舉行了一次會議。那是我第一次遇見Lionel Tiger，但在那之前我已讀過他的書。

--- 段落 215 (476 字元) ---
I had read  both Men in Groups and The Imperial Animal.Men in Groups probably came out in  around ‘70 or ‘69, or something like that [1969].65 The Imperial Animal came out  in ‘73 [1971].66 We invited him and a bunch of others and started off this whole  series of things.- Q2: Who was it— You said RAND was taking the lead on this?Marshall: Yeah.- Q2: Who was doing it there?- Marshall: Herb Goldhamer.And he continued on with a whole bunch of things up  to the time he died.

[翻譯]
我曾經讀過《Men in Groups》和《The Imperial Animal》。《Men in Groups》應該是在70或69年左右出版的，《The Imperial Animal》是在73年出版的。我們邀請了他和一群其他人，開始了這一系列的活動。問題2：是誰，你說蘭德公司在這方面領先？馬歇爾：對。問題2：在那裡是誰在做這件事？馬歇爾：赫伯·戈德哈默。他一直繼續做很多事情，直到他去世的時候。

--- 段落 216 (341 字元) ---
67 The other thing to say about this period is, again, this kind of contrast between  Schlesinger and Kissinger.Kissinger, I think, really had a very pessimistic view of  America’s future.He really did, and at that time, given what the hell was going on  in this country, one had some rights to be pessimistic.But Schlesinger wasn’t at  all.

[翻譯]
在這個時期另一個要提及的事情是，再次提及薛辛格和基辛格之間的對比。我認為，基辛格對美國的未來非常悲觀。在那個時候，鑑於這個國家正在發生的混亂局面，他擁有悲觀的理由。但薛辛格卻完全不同。

--- 段落 217 (486 字元) ---
[Indistinct] In fact, I think one of the most interesting things that Schlesinger  ever said—I think it was in some Time magazine [11 Feb ‘74] article—which I think  people never understood very well, was that he thought of himself as an “evangelist”  [in the article, Schlesinger says “revivalist”].68 A lot of the conflict between Kissinger and Schlesinger had to do with this very different view of what the long-term  strengths and weaknesses were between ourselves and the Soviets.

[翻譯]
事實上，我認為舒勒辛格曾經說過最有趣的一點是他自認為是一位「佈道者」（在某個《時代雜誌》[1974年2月11日]的文章中提到，舒勒辛格說是「復興運動者」）。基辛格和舒勒辛格之間的許多衝突都源於對我們和蘇聯之間長期實力和弱點的非常不同看法。

--- 段落 220 (448 字元) ---
70 One of the things he spent most of his time  on was this issue of “the least miserable option,” which was the way it was talked  about.You know, if you really face up to the thing of what are you actually going  to do after deterrence has failed, then this notion of simply unleashing the Single  Integrated Operational Plan is—

- Q2: —荒謬的。- 馬歇爾: 絕對，胡說八道。- Q2: Cotter在AE還是在哪裡？- 馬歇爾: 他在AE。

--- 段落 224 (403 字元) ---
Cotter and Pete Haas, Deputy Director for Science and Technology of  the Defense Nuclear Agency…  See, the problem was that they wanted to do a whole bunch of things and I was  in a very good bureaucratic position to help them, because, after all, Net Assessment can do anything, right?I mean look at almost any issue.So they wanted  to do a lot of work on the Soviet doctrine, and exercises, and so on.

[翻譯]
柯特和皮特·哈斯（Pete Haas），国防核能局科学技术副局长……看，问题是他们想做很多事情，而我正好处于一个非常好的官僚地位可以帮助他们，毕竟，综合评估可以处理任何事情，对吧？我的意思是看看几乎任何问题。所以他们想对苏联的学说、演习等进行大量研究工作。

--- 段落 225 (471 字元) ---
It all started  with a DNA-DARPA effort that began in probably ‘73, ‘72, and was called the New  Alternatives thing.It was an effort to look at technologies and what could they do  for you, and it was there that there was this first, not really first, but a major push  toward precision-guidance weapons.By the time I moved here in ‘73, Cotter had,  of course, come before me, and he and the DNA people very much wanted to  look at how you would attack the Soviet forces.

[翻譯]
一切始於一個DNA-DARPA的努力，大概是在'73年或'72年開始的，名為新替代方案。這是一個旨在研究技術及其對你有何影響的努力，正是在那裡第一次（雖然不完全是第一次）出現了對精密制導武器的重大推動。到我在'73年搬過來時，柯特當然已經先我一步了，他和DNA的人非常希望研究如何攻擊蘇聯軍隊。

--- 段落 226 (458 字元) ---
And there was this multiplicity of  interests.On the one hand, our position in tactical nuclears meant that they had  to remain dispersed until they tried to converge for attacks quickly, but then you  could try to attack them so that [indistinct] disorganized [indistinct], but in order  to do that you had to look a lot at how they would really come down, and find the  details of their operational arrangements.That’s some of the things they wanted to do.

[翻譯]
在這種情況下，存在著多種利益。一方面，我們在戰術核武器方面的地位意味著它們必須保持分散，直到它們試圖迅速匯合進行攻擊，但隨後你可以試圖攻擊它們，使得它們混亂無序，但為了做到這一點，你必須仔細研究它們到底會如何攻擊，找到它們的作戰安排的細節。這是他們想要做的一些事情。

--- 段落 227 (454 字元) ---
It all verged on being intelligence and  this and that, and they would be precluded from doing it.But if I tasked them to do  it, then they could do that, or they could then get the intelligence people to go along  with whatever.So they came seeking me.Also, Haas came offering lots of money,  not only for the things that they wanted to do, but things I wanted to do.Additionally, I had no budget, so I got money for studies out of DNA and out of DARPA.

[翻譯]
這一切都涉及情報和種種事情，他們會被禁止這樣做。但如果我讓他們這樣做，他們可以這樣做，或者他們可以讓情報人員配合。所以他們來找我。此外，哈斯提出了許多錢，不僅用於他們想做的事情，還包括我想做的事情。此外，我沒有預算，所以我從DNA和DARPA這里得到了進行研究的資金。

--- 段落 236 (472 字元) ---
Then  there was another one about, well, the crew compartment [Eds: in the T-62] is  much too tight, and the comment from the loader or the tank commander was,  “This is the only tank that I’ve ever been in where you can probably sleep while  you are driving, while it was being driven across… because you are wedged in  tight enough that you don’t bang your head against every piece of the…” I mean  it was just one thing after another one.- Marshall: Right, yeah, right.

[翻譯]
接著有另一個關於T-62的問題，那就是，車員艙太過狹窄，裝填手或坦克指揮官的評論是，“這是我所見過唯一可以在開車時躺下睡覺的坦克... 因為你坐得太緊了，不會撞到每一個部件... ”我是說，一個接著一個問題。- 馬歇爾：是的，沒錯。

--- 段落 237 (283 字元) ---
And Pickett went around and interviewed the people  who were putting these things back in working order and had driven them a lot  just to see… See, a lot of the claims were that these are so uncomfortable, so  bad, that people, once they’re in them for a while, just can’t function.

[翻譯]
皮克特四處走動，採訪那些負責修復這些設備並且長時間使用它們的人，只是為了看一看…因為很多人聲稱這些設備非常不舒適，太糟糕了，以至於人們一旦在其中待上一段時間，就無法正常運作。

--- 段落 249 (457 字元) ---
I’d like to be  able to say that that’s probably the first time that the Agency’s been put under  constant pressure, and begin to get away from old-timer’s analysis, but I find it  hard to believe that they could be that insulated, and could be that insulated  from pressures like that in the ‘50s and ‘60s.- Marshall: Well, I think in the ‘50s they were quite open.The reason I got to know  a lot of the Agency guys was because they would come out to RAND.

[翻譯]
我想說，這可能是機構第一次承受持續壓力，並且開始擺脫老一輩的分析，但我很難相信他們可能會那麼與外界隔離，可能在50年代和60年代不受類似壓力的影響。-馬歇爾：嗯，我認為50年代的時候他們相當開放。我認識許多機構人員的原因是因為他們會來到RAND。

--- 段落 250 (473 字元) ---
And they  were interested in how we got this, or what analysis we used?It’s true that once I  got into government, and had customers who were the people that I was serving  and I thought needed better analysis, then I was pressuring them and tasking  them in various ways to try to do these things.But to tell one last story: One of the things that I did for Schlesinger, that I think  I mentioned, was this business of being an intermediary to the intelligence  community.

[翻譯]
他們對我們是如何得到這些資料或使用了何種分析方法感興趣？事實上，一旦我進入政府，有了我所服務的客戶，我認為他們需要更好的分析，那麼我就會向他們施加壓力，以各種方式要求他們嘗試進行這些事情。但最後告訴一個故事：我為施萊辛格做的一件事，就是我提到過的，就是成為情報界的中間人。

--- 段落 251 (456 字元) ---
I mentioned my work with regard to the Soviet military burden and  the cost of their military programs, but another case was this thing that flared up  about Somalia.The Russians appeared to be taking over the use of this airfield  and they had some ships tied up in the nearby port.The airfield was very close  to the seashore, and they probably had missiles in there; they were constructing  some buildings that looked like they might house the missiles.

[翻譯]
我提到了蘇聯軍事負擔和軍事計劃成本的相關工作，但另一個案例是關於索馬里的事情。俄羅斯人似乎在接管這個機場的使用權，他們在附近的港口有一些船隻停泊。這個機場非常靠近海岸，他們可能在那裡擁有導彈；他們正在建造一些看起來可能用來存放導彈的建築物。

--- 段落 252 (377 字元) ---
72 So Schlesinger  wanted an analysis by the people at the Agency about, “What do we know about  the whole process by which the Russians go about acquiring access and the use  of facilities?Are there some general patterns?Where are they in this thing?” and  so on.So I went out there, and I think it may have even been Fritz Ermarth who  was in charge of the group I contacted.

[翻譯]
所以舒萊辛格想要機構的人對「俄羅斯人如何取得設施訪問和使用的整個過程我們知道什麼？是否有一些一般模式？他們在這件事中處於什麼位置？」進行分析。所以我出去了，我想我聯繫的組織可能甚至是弗里茨·厄瑪斯負責。

--- 段落 253 (442 字元) ---
They started asking what I thought were kind of dumb questions, like, “We could  do a better job if you could tell us what decision this is going to lead to,” and so  on.I said, “First, I’m here to tell you Schlesinger wants it.Why don’t you just do it.Secondly, listening to you I come to the conclusion that you don’t know anything about this government.There isn’t any decision that’s going to be made next Thursday or something like that.

[翻譯]
他們開始問我一些我認為有些愚蠢的問題，比如：“如果您告訴我們這個決定將會導致什麼，我們就可以做得更好”，等等。我說：“首先，我來告訴你們，舒勒辛格想要這樣做。你們為什麼不就這樣做呢？其次，聽了你們的話，我得出的結論是，你們對這個政府一無所知。沒有什麼決定會在下星期四之類的時間做出來。”

--- 段落 254 (455 字元) ---
There’s this controversy about what the  significance of this is.Don’t you know that on issues like this there’s some kind of  complex social-cultural-political process that takes place, and these assessments  are part of an input to that process, and hopefully they make people reach conclusions that are wiser than if they don’t have this input?In any case, Schlesinger  already knows what he believes; you’re not instructing him about what he believes.

[翻譯]
這裡存在著一個關於這件事情重要性的爭議。你難道不知道在這樣的問題上，存在一種複雜的社會文化政治過程，這些評估是該過程的一部分，並希望它們讓人們得出比沒有這些評估更明智的結論嗎？無論如何，施萊辛格已經知道自己的信仰；你不是在告訴他他所信仰的是什麼。

--- 段落 255 (491 字元) ---
He wants you to produce something that’s useful in this type of long-term  effort to persuade others that maybe this could be something serious that they  should pay attention to.”  
- Q2: This goes back to the cooking-the-books argument.I mean, it’s those people,  “Tell me why you want to use the thing, ostensibly so I can shape my analytic  effort, but really so that I can figure out what answer you are looking for so I can  cook the books and give you the answer.”  
- Marshall: Yeah.

[翻譯]
他希望你製作出一些對於這種長期說服他人的努力有用的東西，也許這可能是一些他們應該重視的嚴肅事情。
- Q2: 這又回到了刻意造假的爭議。我的意思是，那些人，“告訴我你為什麼想使用這個東西，表面上是為了讓我形塑我分析性的努力，但實際上是為了讓我找出你想要的答案，這樣我就能捏造數據並給你答案。”
- Marshall: 是的。

### Introduction  
1.Reviewed prior session  
    — Got to Rumsfeld  
    — Stories, some themes  
2.Purpose  
    — Emphasis on themes (intellectual)  
    — Rumsfeld, Brown  
    — People chip in—help me  
### Reflections  
1.‘70s period of big development for me (rich—Net Assessment created; needs  lots of work to do it justice)  
2.Value of responsibility  
    — Long-term competition/RAND responsibility for strategic programs  
    — Net Assessment  
    — Time to think at NSC/Gen.

[翻譯]
### 簡介
1. 回顧之前的會議
    -開始談蘭斯菲爾德
    -故事，一些主題
2. 目的
    -強調主題（智力層面）
    -蘭斯菲爾德，布朗
    -人們參與-幫助我

### 反思
1. '70年代對我來說是一個重要的發展時期（豐富-網絡評估的誕生；需要付出很大努力才能充分體現）
2. 責任的價值
    - 長期競爭/蘭德負責戰略計劃
    - 網絡評估
    - 在國家安全理事會/將軍身上思考的時間

### 1973–1976

[翻譯]
1973年至1976年

### In 1973, the Watergate scandal broke out, leading to President Nixon's resignation in 1974. The Vietnam War also ended in 1973 with the fall of Saigon. In 1975, the Khmer Rouge captured Phnom Penh, leading to the Cambodian genocide. And in 1976, the United States celebrated its Bicentennial.

--- 段落 265 (361 字元) ---
- Marshall: Let’s start now.What the intention is, is to finish off the ‘70s.I read the record of the last session.We bogged down as we were just approaching the tenure  of Secretary of Defense Donald Rumsfeld.But I also looked at it from the point of  view that there are a lot of stories that are not as well organized as one might like  about general themes.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我們現在就開始吧。我們的目的是要完成‘70年代的任務。我讀了上次會議的記錄。當我們接近國防部長唐納德·拉姆斯費爾德的任期時，我們陷入了困境。但我也從這樣的角度看待這個問題，有很多故事並沒有被組織得像我們想要的一樣，關於一些主題。

--- 段落 266 (363 字元) ---
So what I thought I’d do this time is say a little bit more  about the Secretary of Defense James Schlesinger period and also try to focus  some on some major themes, then deal with Rumsfeld and Secretary of Defense  Harold Brown.Let me start by talking a little bit about the period as a whole, the ‘70s.It seems to  me that a lot of things happened in the ‘70s.

[翻譯]
所以這一次我想多談一些國防部長詹姆斯·施萊辛格時期的事情，並嘗試聚焦一些主要主題，然後再談談拉姆斯菲爾德和國防部長哈羅德·布朗。讓我先談一下整個七十年代這段時期，似乎在七十年代發生了很多事情。

--- 段落 267 (471 字元) ---
I’m not talking about events in the  world, I’m talking about me and about the shape of this office which, in effect,  was just set during that time period.At least net assessment as it currently exists  was created intellectually in that period, to a large extent.So if you’re looking at  the book, the ‘70s really looks like a period that, when you get it all fleshed out,  might end up being a couple of chapters or something like that, or more than just  one chapter.

[翻譯]
我不是在談論世界上的事件，我在談論我自己，以及在那個時間段設立的這個辦公室的形狀。至少目前存在的綜合評估在那個時期在很大程度上在思想上創造出來。所以如果你看這本書，70年代看起來真的像是一個時期，當你把所有東西都完整呈現出來時，可能最終會變成一兩章，或者不只是一章。

--- 段落 268 (500 字元) ---
I think it’s hard to do it justice, and I haven’t done enough digging  back and so on to fully reconstruct the period.The other thing about the ‘70s, as I thought about that period, and also the period  really of ‘69, because I actually thought of this as starting in the summer or fall  of ‘69… In thinking about it, what struck me about myself and what happened  is how important assuming new responsibilities was in getting one to rethink  how you really ought to think about some particular area.

[翻譯]
我認為很難做到完全公正，而且我還沒有做足夠的研究來完全重建那個時期。談到70年代，當我想到那個時期，以及69年的時期，因為我實際上認為這是從69年的夏天或秋天開始... 在思考這件事時，我對自己和發生的事情的印象是，承擔新責任對於重新考慮應該如何真正思考某個特定領域是多麼重要。

--- 段落 269 (473 字元) ---
It certainly happened  at RAND when I took over from Schlesinger to run the strategic forces program,  because it made me focus on the question, “What in the hell should RAND really  be doing?What should the program really look like?How should we be thinking about strategic forces?” And that led to this whole thing on the long-term  competition and a kind of change in paradigm of, OK, the way you really want to  look at this thing is very differently than we have been.

[翻譯]
當我接替斯萊辛格來管理戰略力量計劃時，這確實發生在蘭德公司，因為這讓我專注於問題：“蘭德公司到底應該做些什麼？計劃應該是什麼樣子？我們應該如何思考戰略力量？”這讓我思考了整個長期競爭的問題，以及一種范式轉變，認為我們對這個問題的看法應該與以往不同。

--- 段落 270 (419 字元) ---
In part, it’s a recapturing  of some style of thinking that existed at RAND at the very beginning but that had  disappeared.And partly it reflected the influence of the business policy/strategy  framework that had come up in my look at organizations and so on.Just the fact  that I had this new responsibility required me to look at that.A similar thing, I think, really happened with the whole net assessment business.

[翻譯]
在某種程度上，這是對蘭德研究所最初存在但已經消失的某種思維風格的重新捕捉。部分原因也反映了商業政策/戰略框架對我的影響，這是我在研究組織等領域時提出的。僅僅是我有這個新責任就要求我去深入研究這個問題。我認為，整個網絡評估業務也類似地發生了類似的事情。

--- 段落 271 (525 字元) ---
In  some ways, it was fortunate that during the early ‘70s, when I first went to the  National Security Council staff, the main thing that—while nominally this was called  the Net Assessment Group, and we were to start that activity or recreate something  at the NSC level—the main tasks that we really spent most of our time on, particularly Chip Pickett and I, were on the implementation of the Nixon reorganization  of the intelligence community and all that, which, in retrospect, wasn’t intellectually  very interesting.

[翻譯]
在某些方面，我在70年代初第一次進入國家安全委員會工作時算是幸運的，雖然名義上這被稱為網絡評估組，我們要在NSC層次開展這項活動，但我們真正花費大部分時間的主要任務，特別是我和Chip Pickett，是在尼克松重新組織情報社區以及其他方面的實施上，回想起來，這並不是令人感到非常有趣的智力活動。

--- 段落 272 (476 字元) ---
I learned something about how stubborn, stupid, organizations  can be, the response of the Central Intelligence Agency to all this and their total  failure to really fix anything, do anything.But that’s an observation about the world  in a certain sense.It didn’t change the way I thought about things very much.But there was this opportunity to really think a little bit at the NSC about, “Alright,  we’re supposed to do these net assessments: How should you really do these?

[翻譯]
我學到一些東西，關於這些固執、愚蠢的組織，中央情報局對此的反應以及他們完全無法真正修復任何問題，採取任何行動。但這是從某種意義上對世界的觀察。這並沒有很大程度地改變我的思維方式。但在國家安全委員會，確實有機會深入思考一下，“好吧，我們應該進行這些網絡評估：你應該如何真正進行這些評估？”

--- 段落 273 (363 字元) ---
If  these things are to be serious and people are to base some decisions on them,  how do you really do the best possible job?” So I had time, then.I think that it  could have been that, given some responsibility and somebody say the first one  has to be produced in six months, you would pull out…systems analysis and …  these models and say “Let’s do something.

[翻譯]
如果這些事情是要嚴肅對待，人們會根據它們作出一些決策，那麼你要如何做到最好？我當時有時間。我覺得，如果給予一些責任，有人說第一個必須在六個月內完成，你可能會拿出系統分析和這些模型，然後說“讓我們做些什麼”。

--- 段落 274 (384 字元) ---
” And that’s kind of intellectually respectable or acceptable to people, but may be very far from, if you’re truly serious,  what the thing ought to be like.So I think it was actually very fortunate that we  didn’t have to jump into it right away, which, as I mentioned the last time, came  about because Secretary of Defense Melvin Laird threw up all kinds of bureaucratic obstacles.

[翻譯]
這在某種程度上是在智力上可以被人們接受或尊重的，但如果你真的很認真，這可能與事實應該如何相去甚遠。所以我認為我們沒有立刻投入其中其實是很幸運的，就像我上次提到的那樣，這是因為國防部長梅爾文·萊爾德對此架起了各種官僚障礙。

Army in Europe  and Commander of the NATO Central Army Group], and had initially asked his intelligence officers to tell him about what the other people really were like and got  absolutely nothing out of it, and so he chose what was a very effective strategy  for him {…}.He sat down with the junior analysts and they told him stories about  {…} and the screwups and so on.Out of that they got educated about the kind of  things he was really interested in to base judgments on: How ready?

But as far as the office was concerned, that was created after  we got here.- Q2: I mean how you went about doing the business of the office.One of the things  that always struck me about this office was there was never any suspense date for  any product.The office sort of worked the product until it was good.It wasn’t like  the office had to produce one by September or January.The office weren’t driven  by the other internals within the Department…  
- Marshall: Yeah, right.

[翻譯]
但就辦公室而言，這是在我們到達後才創建的。Q2: 我是指你如何著手處理辦公室的業務。這個辦公室的一件事讓我印象深刻的是，從來沒有產品的最後期限。辦公室會持續改進產品，直到達到標準。不像辦公室必須在九月或一月生產出產品。辦公室不會被部門內的其他因素所驅使…
- Marshall: 是的，對。

- Q2: …like, got to get an annual report out or things like that.When Jeff McKitrick  replaced Barry Watts, you said, “Take six months to read everything you can in the  office and then we’ll start talking about…” Assignments where they said take six  months and get smart as you can about these things were rare.Does that go back  to your RAND days, or your own personal thing, or do you think it was shaped in  some way by the NSC?- Marshall: No, mostly my own personal view of things.

[翻譯]
問題2：…比如，必須發布年度報告之類的事情。當傑夫·麥基特替換了巴里·瓦茨時，你說：“花六個月的時間閱讀辦公室裡的所有東西，然後我們再談論…” 他們告訴你花六個月時間，盡可能了解這些事情的任務很少。這是否源自你在RAND的經驗，還是源自你個人觀點，或者你認為它在某種程度上受到了NSC的影響？- 馬歇爾：不，這主要是我自己對事物的看法。

--- 段落 282 (450 字元) ---
Also, we’ve had the luxury  and been extraordinarily fortunate in just being allowed to do what I wanted  to do, in a sense.Of course, there were times when people asked for something  and then we did it more or less on a schedule.But my feeling was that, in the first  place, you didn’t have to update these balance assessments more than every  couple of years.Things didn’t happen, turn over, unless there was some major  new source of information.

[翻譯]
此外，我們非常幸運並且得以自由地做我想做的事情。當然，有時會有人要求做某些事情，我們會在許可的情況下按照一定的時間表進行。但我的感覺是，一般來說，你並不需要每隔幾年就更新這些平衡評估。除非有了一些重大的新資訊來源，否則事情通常不會發生變化。

--- 段落 283 (192 字元) ---
- Q2: Or the collapse of the Soviet Union or something like that.- Marshall: The other thing was that you really wanted to produce a high-quality  product, and so you took the time to do that.

[翻譯]
問2: 或者蘇聯解體或像那樣的事情。- 馬歇爾: 另一件事是你真的想要生產高質量的產品，所以你花時間來做到這一點。

--- 段落 284 (472 字元) ---
- Q3: Just following up on this business of how responsibility changes the way you  think: Was it because you were given responsibility for certain intellectual tasks  that you found yourself thinking about how to do that, or was it the fact that you  were given responsibility for managing the activities of subordinates so you had  to think about how you would break it up into tasks which people had to work  on, or both?- Marshall: No, I think it was mainly the first.

[翻譯]
問3：就負責任如何改變你的思考方式這個問題，我只是想追踪一下：是因為你負責某些智力任務，你開始思考如何做到這一點，還是因為你負責管理下屬的活動，所以你必須考慮如何將其分解成人們必須工作的任務，或兩者兼有？- 馬歇爾：不，我認為主要是第一種情況。

--- 段落 285 (449 字元) ---
- Q3: So somebody gives you a subject and said understand…  
- Marshall: Well, in the one case, the RAND thing, I was to take over this program and  looked at what people were doing.And I didn’t think that amounted to anything.Then the question was, "What should we be doing?" I wanted to determine what  a really adequate look at this would be.Then I came to this view that the way you  needed to look at it was in terms of a long-term competition.

[翻譯]
- Q3: 所以有人給了你一個主題，說明白…
- 馬歇爾：嗯，在這個情況下，RAND這個事情，我負責接手這個計劃，看了看人們正在做什麼。我覺得那沒有什麼成效。然後問題是，“我們應該做什麼？”我想確定一個真正充分的觀點，這個觀察應該是什麼。後來我得出這樣的觀點，你需要以長期競爭的角度來看待這個問題。

--- 段落 286 (449 字元) ---
Therefore, these  studies of individual choices of, you know, this new bomber, really needed to be  seen as moves in this competition, as part of the implementation of a strategy  for achieving some set of goals that you really had, and that it just shouldn’t be a  matter of a more modern and up to-date way of killing the same targets that you  had been “killing” for some while, or just a response to some change in the Soviet air defense system.

[翻譯]
因此，對於個人選擇這種新轟炸機的研究，確實需要將其視為競爭中的一步，作為實現一系列目標的策略的一部分，而不僅僅是一種更現代化和最新的殺傷相同目標的方式，或者僅僅是對蘇聯防空系統變化的回應。

--- 段落 287 (445 字元) ---
My view was that you really need to think of this thing in a  very different way, and therefore look at the decision about a bomber in terms of  the whole force and the whole strategy that you were pursuing.Of course, the fact was that, at a certain level, the U.S.never has strategies like  that.Organizations can—The Air Force, say, was committed to the bombers and  had some sense of the strategy, although it was never articulated very well.

[翻譯]
我認為您真的需要以非常不同的方式思考這件事情，因此要從整體力量和您正在追求的整體策略來看待對轟炸機的決定。當然，事實是，在某個層面上，美國從來沒有這樣的戰略。組織可以，比如說，空軍致力於轟炸機並對戰略有一定的認識，儘管這並沒有被表達得很好。

--- 段落 288 (361 字元) ---
But  my experience was that once you had articulated it that way, there were often  people—here in the Pentagon it was particularly the guys in the Office of the Director of Defense Research and Engineering who came from the business world—  who immediately grabbed onto that.Somebody like Dick DeLauer [Under Secretary of Defense for Research and Engineering].

[翻譯]
但我的經驗是，一旦你以這種方式表達了這個觀點，通常會有人（在五角大樓這裡特別是來自商界的國防研究與工程總監辦公室的人）會立刻抓住這一點。像迪克·迪劉爾（國防研究與工程副部長）這樣的人。

--- 段落 289 (440 字元) ---
You talked to him about how part  of the thing that we’re doing is driving up the cost of their staying in business, and  he quickly had some of his guys do a rough calculation of the cost of the Soviet  air defense system and what you might do, what’s the next set of costs you can  impose on them.In that sense, some of the civilians, particularly these guys from  the business world, had far more the right framework for looking at this.

[翻譯]
你和他談談我們所做的一部分是如何增加他們經營成本的事情，他很快讓他的人做了蘇聯防空系統的粗略計算，以及你可能會採取什麼行動，接下來可以對他們施加什麼樣的成本。從這方面來看，一些平民，尤其是來自商業界的人，對於看待這個問題有更正確的框架。

--- 段落 290 (459 字元) ---
I think it really happened in the ‘80s, but I’ll tell the story of General Lew Allen’s  [Air Force Chief of Staff, 1978–1982] reaction to the kind of competitive strategies  sorts of things.He wasn’t sure it was wise for two reasons.One was that we were  too erratic, and therefore we might start something, they would react, and then  we wouldn’t continue on to the next stage, and we’d be worse off than if we’d  not done anything, which is quite plausible.

[翻譯]
我想這件事確實發生在80年代，但我要講一下對於類似競爭性策略的事情，將軍Lew Allen（美國空軍參謀長，1978年至1982年任職）的反應。他認為有兩點原因不確定這樣做是否明智。一個原因是我們太不穩定，因此我們可能會開始某件事，他們會做出反應，然後我們就無法繼續進行下一階段，我們最後會比不做任何事情更糟，這是很有可能的。

--- 段落 291 (406 字元) ---
On the other hand, his view was that  the costs are meaningless to them.It’s as though they had infinite resources and  there was no sense that they…It was as though…  
- Q3: There weren’t opportunity costs.- Marshall: Yeah.His view suggested that in socialist countries there are no opportunity costs.They can always just go ahead and put more resources in, and there’s  no pain and nothing ever happened.

[翻譯]
另一方面，他認為成本對他們來說毫無意義。就像他們擁有無限的資源一樣，沒有任何感覺…好像…  
- Q3：沒有機會成本。- 馬歇爾：是的。他的觀點認為在社會主義國家中不存在機會成本。他們可以隨時投入更多資源，而且不會有痛苦和任何後果。

--- 段落 292 (473 字元) ---
Whereas other people have a sense of, “No,  they have limited resources, too, and there are consequences,” and so on.OK.So let me then talk about the ‘70s and what are some of the interesting  themes to me, from the intellectual side of things, apart from this whole invention  of net assessment.The thing that strikes me the most is the constant interest in, going back to this  business of perceptions, concern for the calculations and perspectives of the  other players.

[翻譯]
然而，其他人則會認為，“不，他們資源有限，也會有後果”等等。好的。那我接下來談談70年代對我來說一些有趣的主題，除了整個網絡評估的發明之外，從性質的角度。最讓我印象深刻的是對其他玩家觀點、計算和觀點的持續關注。

--- 段落 293 (443 字元) ---
As I mentioned last time, that came out of interest that Schlesinger  and I had at RAND, triggered by reading, at least initially, and I think for both of us,  Robert Ardrey’s The Territorial Imperative, and interest in, essentially, the peacetime aspects or uses of military power.75 One of the things that struck me and  struck him was that almost all the analysis about military forces goes into the war  and how the fighting might be done.

[翻譯]
正如我上次提到的，這源於我們在蘭德研究所對施萊辛格和我感興趣，最初是受到羅伯特·阿德里的《領土本能》啟發，我認為對我們兩人來說興趣在於軍事力量的和平時期方面或用途。其中一件讓我感到震撼的事情也讓他感到震撼的是，幾乎所有關於軍事力量的分析都是關於戰爭以及如何進行戰鬥。

--- 段落 294 (380 字元) ---
While people use words like “presence” and  have some general sense that, yes, it’s better to be strong than to be weak and  things like that, there’s very little analysis of this matter.In particular, Schlesinger  was very interested in the question of, “alright, these things are going on, How do  you do well at it?What actions, what ways of demonstration really are effective?

[翻譯]
雖然人們常使用「存在感」等詞語並大致感覺到，是的，強大比較弱小更好之類的事情，但對這個問題的分析非常少。特別是，施萊辛格對這個問題非常感興趣，“好吧，這些事情正在發生，你該如何做得好呢？哪些行動，哪些表現方式真正有效呢？

--- 段落 295 (489 字元) ---
” And then it spills over into the whole area of deception and many other things,  like Henry Kissinger’s and Richard Nixon’s views on crises as opportunities as well  as problems.Even before I got to the Pentagon, when I was working for Kissinger I tried to get  the intelligence people to do some analyses, as best they could, of the Russians  and what they pay attention to about us.What things get us good scores in their  books as against things that get us bad or indifferent scores?

[翻譯]
然後這就延伸到欺騙等許多其他事情的整個範疇，就像亨利·基辛格和理查德·尼克松對危機的看法，視之為機會和問題。即使在我進入五角大廈之前，當我還在為基辛格工作時，我試圖讓情報人員根據俄羅斯人對我們關注的內容進行一些分析，他們對我們哪些方面印象好，哪些方面印象不好或不在意？

--- 段落 296 (345 字元) ---
And you know, you  come up with some interesting things.Then later, there are still other developments, and you even get into issues of the prestige effects of reaching the moon  and all of that.76  But clearly this theme of perceptions and the peacetime uses of military power is  something that runs through a lot of what was done in the ‘70s.

[翻譯]
你知道，你提出了一些有趣的想法。後來，還有其他的發展，甚至涉及到太空競賽對聲望的影響等議題。但顯然，這種感知和和平時期利用軍事力量的主題貫穿了70年代的很多研究。

--- 段落 297 (390 字元) ---
The second thing is this long-term competition perspective, and in the beginning  and in the middle ‘70s, in particular, this writing of various things on actual strategy or strategic planning sorts of things for Rumsfeld and for Brown, which, again,  brought back in a lot of these economic dimensions of things, and led to the  creation of the Investment Balance and some of these things.

[翻譯]
第二個重點是這個長期競爭的觀點，在開始和70年代中期特別是，寫了一些關於拉姆斯菲爾德和布朗實際戰略或戰略規劃方面的東西，再次帶回了許多經濟方面的因素，並導致投資平衡和一些其他事項的產生。

--- 段落 298 (398 字元) ---
Those two things,  plus all the things that get into the development of net assessment, are the main  intellectual things, I think.Let me just talk briefly about the Schlesinger period, to pick up some things that  I think didn’t come through clear enough during the last talk.This was a period,  really, of the development of the state of the art of doing these things.We had the  time to do them.

[翻譯]
這兩件事情，再加上參與網絡評估發展的所有事情，是我認為最主要的智力活動。讓我簡要談談舒萊辛格時期，提到上次講話中我認為沒有講清楚的一些事情。這個時期真的是發展這些事情的藝術水準的時期。我們有時間做這些事情。

--- 段落 299 (474 字元) ---
Soon after I got here, Schlesinger and I talked, and there were  these three areas that I mentioned last time.He was interested in assessments on  the strategic balance, the NATO-Warsaw Pact balance, and the maritime balance.We started to work on that, and made, I think, the least progress on the strategic  balance.I also did a bunch of special things for Schlesinger.It also was after I got here that we changed the nature of the task, in some sense,  for net assessment.

[翻譯]
我抵達這裡不久後，與施萊辛格見面，我提到了上次提過的三個領域。他對戰略平衡、北約-華沙條約平衡和海上平衡的評估很感興趣。我們開始著手進行工作，在戰略平衡方面取得的進展應該是最少的。我還為施萊辛格做了一些特殊的事情。也就是在我到達這裡後，我們改變了對淨評估的任務性質。

--- 段落 300 (450 字元) ---
That is, up till that time we were tasking the people in the  Pentagon to do assessments from the NSC, because that’s the way it was thought  that it would be done.They were broad, general studies with many participants  and task forces, which ended up—I came here before the first one was finished—  with these brokered, bullshit analyses; you know, “the Soviets don’t have any  weaknesses” nonsense out of the Defense Intelligence Agency and so on.

[翻譯]
換句話說，直到那個時候，我們讓五角大樓的人從國家安全委員會做評估，因為大家都認為應該這樣做。這些評估是廣泛的、涉及眾多參與者和工作小組的研究，最後我在第一輪評估完成前就來到這裡了。這些評估結果是通過斡旋達成的、鬧劇一樣的分析；你知道的，“蘇聯沒有任何弱點”之類的廢話出自國防情報局等。

--- 段落 301 (314 字元) ---
After  we had finished off that first one, Schlesinger’s attitude was, to put it in his way  of speaking, “Enough of this shit.Let’s get on and do something serious.” So the  whole thing then became that these were private assessments sent to him, and  he read them, and he would then pass them on if he wanted to.

[翻譯]
完成了第一件事後，施萊辛格的態度是，用他的方式來說，“這種狗屁事夠了，我們該做些嚴肅的事情了。”所以整個事情就變成這些是私人評估發送給他的，他會閱讀它們，如果他想要，他會轉發它們。

--- 段落 302 (266 字元) ---
The fact was that  we were still learning how to do it, so we didn’t have a lot of really great things to  offer him, because of start-up times and the fact that once you started, you found  that none of the right data existed, and all that.So we weren’t so helpful.

[翻譯]
事實是我們仍在學習如何做這件事，所以我們並沒有太多真正出色的東西可以提供給他，因為起步時間較長，而且一旦開始了，你會發現並不存在正確的數據，所有這些。所以我們並沒有提供太多幫助。

--- 段落 303 (420 字元) ---
Another thing I spent a lot of time on was serving as an intermediary for him with  the intelligence community, trying to get special studies, special assessments  done, trying to get them to look again and see whether they wouldn’t find some different answers to things like the military burden of the Soviet Union and some  things of that sort.77  But basically, the whole way of doing things began to take shape then.

[翻譯]
另一件我花了很多時間做的事情是充當他與情報界之間的中介，試圖進行特別研究、特別評估，試圖讓他們重新檢視，看是否可以找到不同的答案，像是蘇聯的軍事負擔等等。但基本上，整個工作方式開始形成那時。

--- 段落 304 (450 字元) ---
Certainly the avoidance of models, the reliance on judgment, the importance of data  on long-term trends and asymmetries, the importance of really understanding  the other side’s doctrine and concepts, which would be a major aspect of the  asymmetries, were all part of the net assessment approach.As I mentioned, there  was a lot of attention to the psychological-political effects or uses of military  forces.And it wasn’t just the military forces.

[翻譯]
當然，避免依賴模型，依靠判斷，重視長期趨勢和不對稱數據，真正理解對方的學說和概念的重要性，將是不對稱因素的主要方面，都是網絡評估方法的一部分。正如我所提到的，對軍事力量的心理政治效應或使用受到了很大的關注。而且這不僅僅是對軍事力量。

--- 段落 305 (335 字元) ---
For example, when Schlesinger was  Secretary, it became the U.S.’s turn to host one of these big, formal NATO meetings [Nuclear Planning Group meeting, 17 Jun 1975].78 In discussion with him,  we decided that… Again, one of the things your forces do is not just impress the  enemy, but your allies.Well, it’s not even just your forces.

[翻譯]
例如，當舒萊辛格擔任國務卿時，輪到美國主辦這些重要的正式北約會議[核規劃小組會議，1975年6月17日]。在和他討論後，我們決定...再者，你的部隊所做的一件事情不僅僅是給敵人留下深刻印象，也包括你的盟友。嗯，甚至不僅僅是你的部隊。

--- 段落 306 (496 字元) ---
So we consciously chose  to hold the meeting in California, so that the defense ministers and other allied  officials could fly across the whole country, because most of these people never  get beyond Washington.And so it’s held at the Naval Postgraduate School, which  I knew had appropriate facilities.And then they were taken down one day to the  missile-launching sites and tours of the silos at Vandenberg Air Force Base and  things of that sort.All, in part, based on bucking up the allies.

[翻譯]
因此，我們有意選擇在加利福尼亞州舉行會議，這樣國防部長和其他盟國官員就可以穿越整個國家飛到那裡，因為這些人中的大多數從未離開華盛頓。所以會議在海軍研究生院舉行，我知道那裡有適當的設施。然後他們被安排一天參觀范登堡空軍基地的導彈發射基地和地下金庫等等。所有這些部分都是為了支持盟友。

--- 段落 307 (316 字元) ---
So Schlesinger was  very interested in all of these dimensions, as I was.- Q3: Did you get any feedback?- Marshall: No, it’s hard to know.I don’t know, it didn’t, I think…I even found a Robinson Jeffers poem for Schlesinger to use in his speech at this meeting.At any rate,  he was very, very interested in all that.

[翻譯]
因此，Schlesinger 對所有這些層面都非常感興趣，我也是。問題3：您有任何反饋嗎？馬歇爾：沒有，很難知道。我不知道，我想……我甚至為Schlesinger找到了一首羅賓遜·傑佛斯的詩，讓他在這次會議上使用。無論如何，他對這一切都非常非常感興趣。

--- 段落 308 (365 字元) ---
Another thing that we did along this line, I mean while we were thinking a lot  about the Soviets, how they score us, how they see us—again to follow up on  the business of the allies—I undertook, with Nathan Leites’s help, to try to find  out, If we’re going to try to impress the allies as well as the Russians, what do they  notice?What do they pay attention to?

[翻譯]
在這條路線上，我們另一個做的事情是，在我們密切關注蘇聯，考慮他們如何評價我們、如何看待我們的同時，我們又去深入探討盟友的問題。在內森·萊特斯（Nathan Leites）的幫助下，我著手試圖找出，如果我們要向盟友和俄羅斯人留下印象，他們會注意到什麼？他們關注什麼？

--- 段落 309 (407 字元) ---
I used my connections into the French to  talk with them and found some interesting things, which wasthat what appeared  to weigh very highly with them, because of the importance of their own nuclear submarines to them, was essentially antisubmarine warfare, in the sense of  who was ahead in that.That seemed to get very big weight.Nathan went off to  interview the British, and the Germans, in particular.

[翻譯]
我利用我與法國人的聯繫進行交談，發現一些有趣的事情。他們似乎十分重視的是他們自己的核潛艇的重要性，基本上是反潛戰，也就是在這方面誰領先。對他們來說這似乎非常重要。Nathan 前去掉訪英國人，尤其是德國人。

--- 段落 310 (438 字元) ---
79 Then subsequently, he  did another thing on Germany, which we had to circumscribe all publication of,  because, in essence, it said it is very doubtful that the Germans will actually fight.But Nathan had some very keen insights into the Germans.80  
- Q3: Is this the time when he came up with this image of “pygmies, midgets, and  giants?”  
- Marshall: No, that was just verbally.That antedates this, I think.It goes back to…  Right.

[翻譯]
79 然後隨後，他對德國做了另一件事，我們不得不限制所有發表，因為實質上它表示德國人實際上可能不會戰鬥。但是內森對德國人有一些非常敏銳的見解。  
- Q3: 這是他提出“矮人、侏儒和巨人”形象的時候嗎？  
- 馬歇爾： 不是，那只是口頭上講的。我想那是早於這個時間，它回溯到... 對，是的。

--- 段落 311 (488 字元) ---
The other thing that had a big impact as far as the office was concerned, I  think, was that we got a reasonable start on getting funding for studies through  the Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency and through the Defense Nuclear  Agency.Again, one of the things that happened during this time was that Don Cotter was here and wanted to do various kind of studies, and Pete Haas [Deputy  Director for Science and Technology] of DNA came around and asked what they  could do for me.

[翻譯]
就辦公室而言，另一件對我們產生重大影響的事情是，我們開始透過國防部高級研究計劃局和國防核能機構獲得研究資金方面取得了合理的進展。在這段時間內發生的另一件事是唐·科特（Don Cotter）在此，並希望進行各種研究，DNA的科技副總監皮特·哈斯（Pete Haas）也來找我詢問他們能為我做些什麼。

--- 段落 312 (288 字元) ---
That was, in part, what he would have done anyway, but it also,  I’m sure, was seen as something they could use to then get me to authorize or  request DNA to do things that it wanted to for Cotter, but that Cotter didn’t necessarily have the authority or the right portfolio to get into.

[翻譯]
這在某種程度上本來就是他會做的事情，但我相信，對他們來說也被視為可以讓他們讓我授權或要求DNA做他們想要為Cotter做的事情，但Cotter不一定有權力或權利組合進行。

--- 段落 313 (464 字元) ---
For example, Cotter was  very interested in this whole business of analyzing Soviet exercises in Europe, and  in the conventional aspects of that as well as the nuclear, but given his portfolio, it  was hard for him to get into that and hard for DNA to get into it.- Q2: Where was he?- Marshall: He was the Assistant to the Secretary of Defense for Atomic Energy.- Q2: AE?- Marshall: AE, yeah.But Net Assessment had the virtue that we could use them for  anything.

[翻譯]
例如，科特對分析蘇聯在歐洲進行的演習很感興趣，包括常規方面和核武方面，但鑑於他的職務範圍，很難讓他參與其中，也很難讓國家核安全局（DNA）參與其中。- Q2：他在哪裡？- 馬歇爾：他是國防部原子能助理。- Q2：原子能？- 馬歇爾：對，是原子能。但是綜合評估局有一個優勢，就是我們可以讓他們參與任何事情。

--- 段落 314 (434 字元) ---
We could say, “We want you to do those things.” So a lot of that was done.But pretty much from the beginning, we got a fair amount of money, and that got us  into this pattern of extensive contracting for outside work, which was very important,  particularly in some of these cases where you didn’t believe the CIA answers to a lot of  questions.You’d go get somebody intelligent to look at those questions.OK.Let’s go on to Rumsfeld.

[翻譯]
我們可以說，“我們希望你做這些事情。” 所以很多事情都做了。但從一開始，我們就得到了相當多的錢，這讓我們進入了大量外包工作的模式，這對於一些情況非常重要，特別是在你不相信CIA對很多問題的答案時。你會找一個聰明的人來看那些問題。好的，讓我們繼續談談拉姆斯菲爾德。

--- 段落 315 (476 字元) ---
Rumsfeld came in around late November or early December of ‘75 [20 Nov 1975].He was here during ‘76, so he was here just for essentially a  little over one year.I was very impressed with Rumsfeld.I think, in fact, in some ways,  of all the people I’ve worked for, that he was potentially the best Secretary of Defense.- Q2: That’s a lot of people.I mean, that’s pretty…  
- Marshall: I think that because of his political skills and ability and interest in using  good people.

[翻譯]
盧姆斯菲爾德大約在1975年11月底或12月初到任。他在1976年期間都在這裡，所以他只在這裡待了一年多一點。我對盧姆斯菲爾德印象非常深刻。我覺得，事實上，在我曾經服務過的所有領導人中，他有可能是最優秀的國防部長。- Q2：這樣的人數真的很多。我是說，這相當…- 馬歇爾：我認為是因為他的政治技巧、能力和對利用優秀人才的興趣。

--- 段落 316 (472 字元) ---
Schlesinger, of course, was a close friend of mine, but he scared too  many people.People were frightened of him.I told the story last time that when  he was the Director of Central Intelligence, a large part of the middle management hid from him out at CIA.He and I always got along terrifically, but lots of  people were just frightened of him.- Q3: He was on a visiting committee for a Harvard thing and he had the same effect  at Harvard.People were terrorized—“Oh no!

[翻譯]
謝西爾辛格當然是我一個親密的朋友，但他嚇壞了太多人。人們對他感到害怕。我上次講過一個故事，當他擔任中央情報局局長時，許多中層管理人員都躲避他。他和我總是相處得很好，但很多人只是害怕他。他曾經參加哈佛一個委員會，對哈佛也有同樣的影響。人們都感到恐懼 - 「哦，不要！」

--- 段落 317 (402 字元) ---
We’re going to have to give…  Schlesinger is going to be there and he is going say some goddam thing and  we’re not going to know what to say.”  
- Marshall: Yeah.- Q2: Of course that’s true.- Q3: Yes.I got along fine with him.- Marshall: He and I got to be very close at RAND.And there was a set of people that  he dealt with, Cotter and others.But kind of the ordinary bureaucrat was just  terrified.

[翻譯]
我們將不得不給予...施萊辛格（Schlesinger）會在那裡，他會說一些該死的話，而我們卻不知道該說什麼。- 馬歇爾（Marshall）：是的。- Q2：當然是真的。- Q3：是的。我和他相處得很好。- 馬歇爾：在蘭德（RAND）時，他和我關係非常密切。還有一群他交往的人，科特爾（Cotter）和其他人。但對一般的官僚來說，他們只是感到恐懼。

--- 段落 318 (445 字元) ---
- Q2: So you think that it was Rumsfeld’s bureaucratic and organizational, people  skills… 
- Marshall: Yeah, that’s right.He seemed also, as I say, to use people extraordinarily  well, all kinds of people.And then he also was politically astute, you know.But he  didn’t have a long stay.He largely left us alone, except that he would make requests, I mean when there  was some question or some issue that he was interested in or concerned with.

[翻譯]
Q2：所以你認為是拉姆斯菲爾德的官僚和組織能力，還有人際技巧...
Marshall：是的，沒錯。正如我所說，他似乎非常擅長運用各種人才。而且他也很有政治敏感度。但他並沒有長時間留下來。除非是在某個他感興趣或關心的問題或議題上，他通常會讓我們自己做，只是偶爾會提出要求。

--- 段落 319 (446 字元) ---
He had some questions, I remember, about the strategic balance and what did I  think, or the nature of deterrence, or something like that, and I would write him a  paper.We also created some short, four- or five-page assessments, kind of summary stuff.But basically we were left alone and we went ahead and did that.The other thing that impressed me about him was that he had this kind of strategic sense of, “Let’s think about where we’re going.

[翻譯]
我記得他有一些問題，關於戰略平衡或我認為的事情，或者是威慑的本質之類的，然後我會給他寫一篇論文。我們也製作了一些短小的、四至五頁的評估，類似總結的東西。但基本上我們是獨立操作，繼續向前做。另一件讓我印象深刻的事情是，他有這種戰略意識：“讓我們想一想我們要去的地方”。

--- 段落 320 (465 字元) ---
” And he tried to do something  for the Navy, on the naval programs.I remember he asked for a paper overnight.Jim Roche and I prepared something that he liked a lot.I can remember the  meeting that took place.It was on a Saturday morning.Rumsfeld had a bunch of  people in.And an Office of Program Analysis and Evaluation guy got up to talk  about things and was going on and obviously had no sense at all about what kind  of perspective Rumsfeld was interested in.

[翻譯]
他試圖為海軍做些事情，就海軍計劃而言。我記得他曾要求隔夜準備文件。吉姆·羅奇和我準備了一些他很喜歡的東西。我還記得那次會議。那是在一個星期六早上。朗斯菲爾德邀請了一群人。一位辦公室程序分析和評估的人起身發言，談論事情，但顯然完全不知道朗斯菲爾德感興趣的視角是什麼。

--- 段落 321 (459 字元) ---
So about half way through the thing, Rumsfeld says, “Why don’t we stop looking  at our shoelaces and raise our sights and see where we are going.”  
- Q3: This is an example of not scaring people…  
- Marshall: And it was because of that, that and our own interests, that Roche and  I wrote this July ‘76 thing, saying, “What would a strategy for defense really look  like?How would you organize it, using business analogies of, What ‘businesses’  are you in?

[翻譯]
所以大約在進行中途，倫斯菲爾德說，"我們為什麼不停止低頭看鞋帶，提高我們的視野，看清我們要去哪裡。"
- Q3：這是一個不嚇人的例子...
- 馬歇爾：正是因為這個原因，以及出於我們自身的利益，羅奇和我在1976年7月寫了這篇文章，說，“防禦的戰略真正應該是什麼樣子呢？你如何組織它，使用商業類比，你在做什麼‘生意’？”

--- 段落 322 (351 字元) ---
What are you trying to do in that ‘business?’ What are the major trends  and other things that you ought to take account of in thinking about that part of  the ‘business?’” That’s how we got into doing something beyond the more narrow  assessment.That carried over later, which we will get to, to Brown, who was also  interested in this kind of thing.

[翻譯]
你在那個「業務」中試圖做什麼？在考慮該部分「業務」時，應該考慮哪些主要趨勢和其他事情？這就是我們如何開始超出更狹窄的評估範圍。這種做法後來延續到布朗身上，他也對這種事情感興趣。

--- 段落 323 (351 字元) ---
In fact, while we wrote this thing for Rumsfeld,  that is the July ‘76 thing, and he looked at it and responded favorably, Jimmy  Carter came in as President and there wasn’t much time to do anything about it.Then we sent it to Harold Brown, and he liked it, and then we did some strategic  planning experiments for him.81 And we’ll get to that later.

[翻譯]
事實上，當我們為拉姆斯菲爾德寫這件事情時，也就是1976年7月的事情，他看了並作出了正面回應，但是卻換了吉米·卡特成了總統，我們沒有太多時間去做任何事情。然後我們把它送給了哈羅德·布朗，他喜歡這個想法，然後我們替他做了一些戰略規劃實驗，我們後面會再提到。

--- 段落 324 (337 字元) ---
The other interesting thing that happened during the Rumsfeld period was the  start of this strategic dialogue with the Israelis, which ran from April of ‘76 through  about 1980.82 The Israelis had approached Schlesinger twice.He may have been  approached through other things, but I knew of two approaches because they  came through me.

[翻譯]
在朗斯菲爾德時期發生的另一件有趣的事情是從1976年4月開始，持續到1980年左右的這場與以色列人的戰略對話。以色列人兩次接觸了施萊辛格。他可能是通過其他途徑接觸的，但我知道有兩次接觸是通過我這裡來的。

--- 段落 325 (455 字元) ---
Something else which is worth mentioning about the Schlesinger period was that  shortly after I got here—I came here right after the Israeli-Arab War, Yom Kippur  War—Schlesinger put me in charge of a quickie “lessons learned” effort.Each of  the Services was going to undertake a much longer term, thorough effort, and  the Joint Staff ran off and did something, but he wanted an effort to try to get  any lessons learned that could be useful in any way.

[翻譯]
值得一提的是，施萊辛格時期的另一個重要事情是，在我來這裡不久之後-我是在以色列阿拉伯戰爭、贖罪日戰爭之後來到這裡的-施萊辛格讓我負責一個快速的“經驗教訓”工作。每個軍種都將進行一項更長期、更徹底的工作，聯合參謀會做一些工作，但他希望通過一項努力，嘗試獲得任何可能有用的教訓。

--- 段落 326 (402 字元) ---
So we organized an effort,  and I borrowed Tony Cordesman from ARPA to go over there and gather materials and so on.And we had tried to send S.L.A.Marshall there.He made a quickie trip  and talked to the Israeli military that he knew best, came back, wrote something.Schlesinger liked him a lot and wanted to send him back in, but then the Israelis  wouldn’t let him back in the country.- Q2: Jeez.Why?

[翻譯]
所以我們組織了一個工作小組，並向阿帕爾借來東尼·科德斯曼，讓他去那裡收集材料等等。我們曾試圖派遣 S.L.A. 馬歇爾去那裡。他進行了一次快速的旅行，與他最熟悉的以色列軍方進行了交談，回來後撰寫了一些東西。施萊辛格很喜歡他，想再次派他去，但是以色列人不讓他再進入該國。- 問題2：天哪，為什麼？

--- 段落 327 (365 字元) ---
- Marshall: The basic reason was, I think, that… Look, from the Israeli point of view,  that war was very traumatic, because it showed up deficiencies in their planning,  in their thinking.So there was a big internal quarrel in Israel afterwards.There was  this big investigation.I forget the name of that commission that they set up.- Q3: Agranat?- Marshall: Yeah.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我認為，基本原因是...看，從以色列的角度來看，那場戰爭非常具有創傷性，因為它暴露了他們計劃和思維上的缺陷。所以後來在以色列內部引發了一場大爭議。他們進行了一場大調查。我忘記他們成立的那個委員會的名字了。- Q3: Agarnat？- 馬歇爾：是的。

--- 段落 328 (419 字元) ---
So it was very controversial, and Marshall probably was most associated with one of the factions, and so they didn’t want him back in the country.So we couldn’t get him to do it, so we organized this other effort and, as I say, put  Cordesman on it.When Cordesman came back, he relayed this request by the Israelis that they  wanted to set up a direct channel between the Ministry of Defense and the Defense Department.

[翻譯]
因此，這是非常具爭議性的，馬歇爾可能與其中一個派系最有關聯，因此他們不希望他回到該國。因此，我們無法讓他參與，所以我們組織了另一個行動，就像我說的，讓科德斯曼參與其中。當科德斯曼回來時，他傳達了以色列方面的請求，他們希望建立以色列國防部和美國國防部之間的直接聯繫渠道。

--- 段落 329 (492 字元) ---
We found out later, I think, that part of it was related to the fact  that they did not trust their ambassador here [Simcha Dinitz], who they felt was  interfering with the appropriate discussions between the two military establishments.Schlesinger checked with Kissinger, who was at State, and the thing was  kind of vetoed.I don’t think Schlesinger was strongly tempted anyway, and it was  a little unspecific as to what they wanted.There was a similar kind of request that  happened later.

[翻譯]
我們後來發現，我想，其中一部分與他們不信任他們在這裡的大使[辛卡·迪尼茨]有關，他們覺得他正在干預兩個軍事機構之間的適當討論。舒萊辛格向基辛格查證，基辛格當時在國務院，事情被否決了。我不認為舒萊辛格真心想這樣做，而且他們要求的內容有點不具體。之後又發生了類似的請求。

--- 段落 330 (194 字元) ---
But after Schlesinger had left and Rumsfeld was already on board, a man named  Saadia Amiel came to see me, and he saw other people, again requesting the  establishment of this kind of dialogue.

[翻譯]
但在舒萊辛格離開後，拉姆斯菲爾德已經上任後，一位名叫薩迪亞·阿米爾的人來找我，他見過其他人，再次要求建立這種對話。

--- 段落 331 (490 字元) ---
In the aftermath of the ‘73 war, the Israelis  were trying to create more of an Office of the Secretary of Defense-like structure  to both oversee the forces, but also they became aware—well, it goes back to the  ‘67 war, when the French had cut them off after having been their main supplier—that they were beginning to do more of their own weaponry, and, I guess,  after the ‘73 war, they decided they needed to do more thinking, planning in  order to decide what they ought to invest in.

[翻譯]
在‘73年戰爭結束後，以色列人試圖建立更像國防部長辦公室的結構，以監督軍隊，同時他們意識到—這可以追溯到‘67戰爭，當時法國切斷了他們作為主要供應商後，他們開始自行生產更多武器，我猜在‘73戰爭之後，他們決定需要更多思考和計劃，以決定他們應該投資在什麼方面。

--- 段落 332 (432 字元) ---
So Amiel came by, and again I kind of put him off, but he finally convinced Deputy  Secretary of Defense Robert Ellsworth that some such interchange should take  place.Rumsfeld agreed, and I was asked to be the point of contact for doing this.They wanted to keep these discussions out of any forum which the Israelis could  use to argue for, you know, “What about the $200 million we asked for?” “Where’s  the shipment of so and so?

[翻譯]
於是阿米爾來訪了，我再次有點推遲了，但最後他成功說服國防部副部長羅伯特·艾爾斯沃思，認為應該進行某種交流。羅姆斯菲爾德同意了，我被要求成為進行這項工作的聯絡人。他們希望將這些討論保持在以色列無法用來主張的任何論壇之外，你知道，“我們要求的兩億美元呢？” “那些東西的運送到哪裡了？”

--- 段落 333 (488 字元) ---
” So it was explicitly understood that this was not to  be a forum for any of that.It was to be a discussion with them, and also in some  ways a channel for advice to them, as to how they ought to think about their own  future, and do a better job of planning and so on.Also, the thing was to be kept  very quiet.And in fact, no one knew about this, which was a problem, because  the people who nominally do all the relations with the Israelis, got their nose got  out of joint and so on.

[翻譯]
因此，人們明確了解這不是一個討論這些事情的論壇。這是一個與他們討論的地方，同時也是向他們提供建議的渠道，告訴他們應該如何思考自己的未來，更好地規劃等等。另外，這件事情要保持極度的祕密。實際上，沒有人知道這件事，這是一個問題，因為名義上負責與以色列人打交道的人感到不滿。

--- 段落 334 (452 字元) ---
But initially, we had a kind of cover for doing it, which was, “We’re going there just to get information.”  
- Q2: So State Department did not approve that?- Marshall: I don’t know whether that was ever checked with State.I have no idea.But when Brown came in, he was told about this.The thing was done on a basis  of twice a year, and by that time, they came here in April of ‘76 and we went there  in September, October, something like that, of ‘76.

[翻譯]
但最初，我們有一種偽裝的藉口，即“我們只是去那裡獲取資訊。”
- Q2: 那國務院沒有批准這個嗎？- 馬歇爾：我不知道是否有向國務院查證過這件事。我毫不知情。但當布朗上任後，他被告知了這件事情。這件事是以每年兩次的頻率進行的，到了那個時候，他們在1976年4月來到這裡，我們在1976年9月或10月左右去了那裡。

--- 段落 335 (417 字元) ---
In the Carter Administration,  Brown then asked about it, and he, Secretary of State Cyrus Vance, and Assistant  to the President for National Security Affairs Zbigniew Brzezinski knew about it  and were the only… And we would send him reports of the discussions.And, I  don’t know, I presume he told them, at some breakfast meetings or something  like that, about things.- Q2: Who within the Defense Department knew?

[翻譯]
在卡特政府中，布朗隨後詢問了這件事，他、國務卿賽勒斯·范斯和國家安全事務助理日比斯基·布热津斯基知道這件事，並且是唯一知道的人...我們會向他發送討論報告。而且，我不知道，我推測他在一些早餐會議之類的場合告訴了他們一些事情。- Q2: 在國防部內部有哪些人知道？

--- 段落 336 (478 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, people then sort of knew it was happening, but they got none of  the reports.- Q2: They didn’t know what it was?- Marshall: They sort of knew what it was, but they didn’t… It ended in the last year  of the Carter Administration because Assistant Secretary of Defense for International Security Affairs David McGiffert and company couldn’t stand it any longer,  that is, to be excluded.- Q2: How’s the intelligence community play on that?- Marshall: Not at all.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：嗯，那時人們有點知道正在發生的事情，但他們沒有得到任何報告。- Q2：他們不知道那是什麼嗎？- 馬歇爾：他們有點知道那是什麼，但他們沒有...在卡特政府最後一年結束，因為國防部國際安全事務助理部長大衛·麥吉弗特（David McGiffert）和他的同事再也無法忍受被排除在外的情況。- Q2：情報界在這方面起什麼作用嗎？- 馬歇爾：完全沒有。

--- 段落 337 (394 字元) ---
- Q2: None of them involved, they got none of the reports, they never saw you over  there talking to the Israelis and wondered, “What the hell?”  
- Marshall: Well, the attachés knew we were over there, and they would hear something about it.What they reported, I don’t know.We didn’t pay much attention to  that.The ambassador there we would talk to; during part of the time it was Sam  Lewis.

[翻譯]
Q2：他們當中沒有人參與，他們沒有得到任何報告，也沒看到你在那裡跟以色列人交談，不禁疑惑：“到底發生了什麼？”
馬歇爾：欸，那些外交官知道我們在那邊，他們可能聽到了一些消息。至於他們報告了什麼，我不清楚。我們並沒有太在意這些。我們會和那裡的大使交談；在一段時間裡是山姆·路易斯。

--- 段落 338 (445 字元) ---
My counterpart, initially—I forget the man’s name, a guy who was a special  assistant to Shimon Peres, who was the defense minister when the thing started,  and had been the ambassador to France, and then later when the Likud came in,  was the Deputy Minister of Defense, and his name was Mordechai…Zippori.So at any rate, there isn’t too much to say, as I say, about the Rumsfeld period, I  think, as far as interests that continued to develop.

[翻譯]
我的對應人員，起初-我忘了那個男人的名字，他是西蒙·佩雷斯的特別助手，當事情開始時，他是國防部長，後來成為駐法國大使，後來利科德黨上臺後，他成為國防副部長，他的名字是莫德開...希波利。無論如何，關於拉姆斯菲爾德時期，我想說的並不多，就我所知，興趣並沒有持續發展。

--- 段落 339 (13 字元) ---
### 1969–1973

[翻譯]
1969年至1973年

感謝您使用翻譯服務！有任何問題歡迎再提出。

--- 段落 340 (424 字元) ---
- Q1: Did you begin working for Henry Kissinger because he and President Nixon  were dissatisfied with the National Intelligence Estimates they were receiving?- Marshall: [Name of person unclear] and Mitchell conveyed the same comments  about the NIEs.It happened before I got involved.What I was told by Kissinger  was that shortly after the Administration was in place, Nixon had read a few NIEs.He thought they were poor.

[翻譯]
問1：您是因為亨利·基辛格和尼克松總統對他們收到的國家情報估計感到不滿才開始為他工作的嗎？- 馬歇爾：[無法確定人名]和米切爾表達了相同的意見。這是在我參與之前的事情。基辛格告訴我的是，就在政府上任後不久，尼克松閱讀了一些國家情報估計。他認為它們很差。

--- 段落 341 (473 字元) ---
He thought they were much worse than the ones he  remembered from when he had been the vice president—I don’t know whether  that’s really true.At any rate, he was greatly dissatisfied.So, he got Mitchell and  Kissinger to kind of look at things.And I think the three of them had a meeting to  compare notes on, “OK, what’s wrong with these things.Why don’t we like them?”  And that was one of the outstanding complaints—this lack of the separation of  the fact and opinion.

[翻譯]
他覺得這些事情比他擔任副總統時記憶中的更糟糕 - 我不知道這是否真的屬實。無論如何，他感到非常不滿。因此，他讓米切爾和基辛格一起來看看這些事情。我認為他們三個人開了一次會議，比較了一下，「這些事情有什麼問題。為什麼我們不喜歡它們？」其中一個優先的投訴就是這種缺乏對事實和意見的區分。

--- 段落 342 (248 字元) ---
84 Not just that they don’t separate them, but the thing is  written in a way that you don’t know whether that’s a fact, or a judgment, and  that you needed clearly stated what things are facts, and what things are inferences, judgments, and so on.

[翻譯]
不僅是他們不將它們分開，而且這件事寫得讓人不知道那是事實還是判斷，而且您需要明確地陳述哪些事實，哪些是推論、判斷等。

--- 段落 343 (442 字元) ---
Now Kissinger, when he first talked to me, had other complaints, in the sense  that… He said to me, “Look, on the intelligence reports with respect to technology and so on, I’m not able to judge…but in the political stuff I feel I can judge and  they’re terrible.They’re not better than, and indeed they’re probably worse than  the kind of stuff you just read in the newspapers every day.They have no real  depth….There’s nothing behind them.

[翻譯]
現在 Kissinger，當他第一次與我交談時，有其他抱怨，意指...他對我說：“看，關於技術等方面的情報報告，我無法判斷...但在政治方面，我覺得我能夠判斷，它們糟透了。它們不比每天在報紙上讀到的那些消息好，實際上可能還更糟。它們毫無真正深度...背後毫無內涵。"

--- 段落 344 (288 字元) ---
The people writing them don’t seem to  have any real understanding of what’s going on.They report what’s going on but  then they go off and they have their speculations and so on and they’re just not  really worth anything.”  
- Q1: Was Kissinger really interested in intelligence reform?

[翻譯]
寫這些東西的人似乎並不真正了解正在發生的事情。他們報導了正在發生的事，但然後他們進行了推測等等，實際上並沒有什麼價值。
- 問題1：基辛格真的對情報改革感興趣嗎？

--- 段落 345 (461 字元) ---
- Marshall: Now, of course, part of the problem was Henry was… He would talk  with somebody like me or someone on the staff about how terrible, rotten it all  was, but then he would never really say that to the intelligence people.I think  it showed up in the whole way in which he conducted business while he was in  government, certainly in the State Department, where he gathered a set of people around him and then shut off the rest of the State Department.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：當然，亨利的問題之一是...他會和我或其他工作人員談論這一切有多麼糟糕，但他從來沒有真正對情報人員說過。我認為這在他在政府任職期間的整個業務運作中表現出來，特別是在國務院，他聚集了一群人周圍，然後把國務院其他部門的人擋在外面。

--- 段落 346 (457 字元) ---
I don’t know whether Nixon said he wanted someone to look into this, and that’s  why Henry called up and had me do these initial studies…  
- Q1: Did Fred Iklé recommended you to Kissinger for the work on intelligence?- Marshall: Well, I think so, I mean you might talk with Fred, I never really asked him.- Q1: When were you first asked to work for Kissinger?- Marshall: I must have got this call in September of ‘69 because I dropped by to see  Kissinger.

[翻譯]
我不知道尼克森是否說過他想要有人研究這個問題，這就是為什麼亨利打電話給我要我進行這些初步研究的原因...
- Q1：是弗雷德·伊克勒向您推薦了與基辛格合作對情報工作的嗎？- 馬歇爾：嗯，我想是的，您可以和弗雷德談談，我從來沒有真正問過他。
- Q1：您是何時被要求為基辛格工作的？- 馬歇爾：我一定是在1969年的9月接到這個電話，因為我當時去看了基辛格。

--- 段落 347 (448 字元) ---
