Actually, the call came from Al Haig, asking me whether I’d come by  and see Kissinger.I was on my way to Europe for a lengthy vacation, probably  around the middle or the third week in September.So I dropped by Washington on my way and had a meeting with Kissinger.And then, I think I was away about a  month, and came back.Then had to disengage myself from the stuff I was doing  at RAND.I ended up going there in the very early part of December.

[翻譯]
事實上，打來的電話是來自阿爾海格，問我是否可以過去見基辛格。當時我正在去歐洲度長假的途中，可能是在九月中旬或第三周左右。所以我路過華盛頓，在途中與基辛格見面。我大概離開一個月，然後回來。之後我必須從在蘭德所做的工作中脫身。最後我在十二月初去了那裡。

--- 段落 348 (421 字元) ---
- Q1: What can you say about your study of intelligence flow to the White House?- Marshall: The first thing that I did was this study tracing the whole flow of intelligence into the White House.How it happened, how decisions were made about  what to send.First I found out, “Where does this stuff actually come from?” Then  I interviewed people from each of these places to look into how it was they went  about deciding.

[翻譯]
Q1：請問您對情報流向白宮的研究有何看法？- 馬歇爾：我做的第一件事是進行這項研究，追踪所有情報流入白宮的過程。發生了什麼事，關於要發送什麼決定是如何做出的。首先我找出了，“這些情報究竟來自哪裡？”然後我訪問了來自每個地方的人，調查他們是如何做出決定的。

--- 段落 349 (432 字元) ---
NSA had a very organized kind of interface and they had some people who would  come down essentially once a month and sit down… Not just with the guy who  ran the Situation Room, who was in fact a guy from NSA, but to sit around with  some other people and try to say, “Well, OK, what are the things that are of most  interest…”  
- Q1: But the NSA representatives would meet with people from the NSC staff?Who  was talking to whom?

[翻譯]
NSA擁有一個非常有組織的界面，他們有一些人基本上每個月都會來參加，坐下來…不僅與負責情報室的那個人見面，實際上他是NSA的一個人，還與其他一些人圍坐在一起，試圖說：“好吧，哪些事情最有趣…”
- Q1: 但NSA代表會與NSC工作人員會面嗎？誰在和誰交談？

--- 段落 350 (358 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, it really was with the people in… My impression was they met with  the two people who ran the Situation Room and some of the other analysts who  were in the Situation Room.And it was probably through them that they understood what people on the staff wanted, were requesting, had an interest in, etc.,  etc.Whereas the CIA did none of that.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：嗯，實際上是與…我的印象是他們與掌控情報室的兩個人和其他一些分析師見面。可能是通過他們了解職員想要什麼、要求什麼、感興趣的事情等等。而中央情報局卻沒有這樣做。

--- 段落 351 (342 字元) ---
No, somebody told me that that the CIA took its cues from The New York Times  in deciding what intelligence to send to the White House; I don’t know whether  he was being dismissive.But their [Eds: the CIA’s] whole idea was that they know  what’s interesting and important, I mean you just have to read the newspapers or  something like that.

[翻譯]
不，有人告訴我說中央情報局從紐約時報那裡汲取靈感，決定要送哪些情報給白宮；我不知道他是否在表示輕蔑。但他們（指中央情報局）整個理念是他們知道什麼是有趣且重要的，我的意思是你只需要讀報紙之類的東西就可以了。

--- 段落 352 (491 字元) ---
It was, “We have this high-quality product…”  Now, a lot of that was particularly targeted on the issue of what went into the  daily President’s report, but just more generally, they just felt that through the  attendance of Helms and others at various meetings and other things that they  just didn’t need any special apparatus or to spend much real effort at finding out.They just didn’t spend much effort of any systematic sort.- Q1: It was a long-standing problem?- Marshall: I think so.

[翻譯]
這樣說，「我們擁有這個高質量的產品...」。如今，很多人特別關注每日總統報告中的問題，但更廣泛地看，他們覺得透過參加不同會議和其他活動，像是海姆斯等人，他們並不需要任何特別的設備或花很多真正的努力去找出答案。他們就是沒有花太多系統性的努力。- 問題1：這是個長期存在的問題嗎？- 馬歇爾：我想是的。

--- 段落 353 (306 字元) ---
I talked with members of the Kennedy/Johnson NSC staffs and  they had similar complaints about intelligence.But again, one of the things I said  is how little they seemed to care about the customers, even though they protest  that, “We’re here to serve,” particularly these top level people would say this.

[翻譯]
我與甘迺迪/約翰遜國家安全會議的成員交談，他們對情報機構也有類似的抱怨。但是，我提到的一點是，他們似乎對客戶非常不在乎，盡管他們抗議說：“我們在這裡為客戶服務”，特別是這些高級人士經常這樣說。

--- 段落 354 (480 字元) ---
One  of the first things I did when I went to work for Kissinger permanently was to go  through a number of books that Kissinger recently had written and extracted  from them sections that I thought provided the most insight into how he looked  at the world, what he thought, the kind of information that would be useful to  him, and sent that around to them.But that’s the kind of thing, in my view, if they  were serious about their offers of help, they would do for themselves.

[翻譯]
當我正式加入基辛格團隊工作時，我做的第一件事之一是閱讀基辛格最近寫的一些書籍，並從中提取我認為能最深入了解他如何看待世界、他的想法以及對他有用的資訊的部分，然後把這些內容發送給團隊。但我認為，如果他們真的認真提供協助的話，他們應該自己去做這樣的事情。

--- 段落 355 (375 字元) ---
But they  didn’t do any of that.Just really crazy.So, to a large extent they thought that they had their way of doing things and  it was the best way and they didn’t—despite their talk of wanting to help, they  were very unresponsive to what customers actually wanted, even somebody like  Kissinger.- Q1: Did the CIA interface with groups at Harvard, Stanford, and elsewhere?

[翻譯]
但他們沒有做任何事情。真的很瘋狂。因此，在很大程度上，他們認為他們有自己的做事方式，這是最好的方式，但是儘管他們說想要幫助，他們對顧客實際想要的東西非常不關心，甚至像基辛格這樣的人。-問題1：CIA是否與哈佛、斯坦福等地的團體接觸過？

--- 段落 356 (490 字元) ---
- Marshall: The thing that struck me at the time was how at that point the CIA had  kind of shut itself off from much connection with any other organizations doing  stuff that could potentially have been interesting to it.And they kind of seemed  to have, for the while, just adopted the notion of, “We’re the real experts, we don’t  need to talk to other people.” Which was very different than the situation in the  ‘50s.- Q1: How did the CIA of the ‘50s differ from that of the late ‘60s?

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：當時讓我印象深刻的是，當時CIA已經與其他可能對其有興趣的組織切斷了很大程度的聯繫。他們似乎在那段時間內只是採納了“我們是真正的專家，不需要與其他人交流”的觀點。這與50年代的情況非常不同。- Q1：50年代的CIA與60年代末期的CIA有何不同？

--- 段落 357 (471 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, I guess my own experience of it was really being at RAND… It may  have been particular to RAND, but not exclusively.Because they had this special  group up at MIT.I forget the guy’s name now who was up there… But they had a  number of connections out.Now, that was a kind of contracting arrangement to  get certain kinds of studies… But it was a way of having an interface with people  in academia, working in the economics and political science worlds.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：嗯，我想我的經驗主要是在蘭德研究所…這可能是特定於蘭德，但並非專屬。因為他們在麻省理工學院有這個特殊的團體。我現在忘記了那個在那裡的人的名字…但他們有一些與外界的聯繫。這是一種合約安排，用來進行特定類型的研究…但這是一種與學術界中從事經濟學和政治科學的人建立界面的方式。

--- 段落 358 (365 字元) ---
In the case  of RAND, people came out, particularly Frank Walters and Wally Seidel, who were  analysts working on the Soviet missile programs, aircraft programs.And in the  middle ‘50s, ‘56 or so, they started to come out to try to understand what RAND  was doing in the systems analysis-type of analysis techniques, how they might be  used in what they were doing.

[翻譯]
在RAND的案例中，特別是Frank Walters和Wally Seidel這兩位分析師，他們在蘇聯導彈計劃和飛機計劃上工作。 在50年代中期，大約1956年左右，他們開始出來試圖了解RAND正使用系統分析類型的分析技術，以及這些技術如何應用在他們正在進行的工作中。

--- 段落 359 (450 字元) ---
Also in a certain sense the beginnings of their effort to cost the Soviet programs, to do a comprehensive effort, that a guy named  Jerry Godaire, who was out at the Agency.85… some of the ideas came from  people like Loftus and me at RAND.That you needed to do something like that to  check on the overall resource demands implied by various kinds of programs that  the Soviets were undertaking.Anyway, there was quite active interchange with  them.

[翻譯]
在某種意義上，他們開始試圖評估蘇聯的計劃成本，做了一個全面的努力，這是由一個名叫傑瑞·戈代爾(Jerry Godaire)居於機構。一些想法來自像洛夫特斯和我在蘭德公司的人。你需要做一些類似的事情，來檢查蘇聯正在進行的各種計劃所暗示的整體資源需求。總之，我們與他們之間進行了非常活躍的交流。

--- 段落 360 (349 字元) ---
And then somehow, by the late ‘60s, it had pretty much dried up, I think.And I  think it came about, in part, because of, maybe this sense that, “We’re the real professionals and we don’t really need to keep up these connections.” Secondly, the  people in the ‘50s— The whole place was made up of people who were brought  in just a few years before.

[翻譯]
然後，不知怎的，到了60年代後期，我想這種情況幾乎已經消失了。我認為這可能是因為“我們是真正的專業人士，不需要保持這些聯繫”的感覺出現了一部分。其次，在50年代，那裡的人們-整個地方都是由幾年前才過來的人建立的。

--- 段落 361 (290 字元) ---
But by the late ‘60s, you were beginning to have people  rise fairly high in the bureaucracy who had come in and their whole careers had  been within the Agency.And I remember, in fact, in the ‘60s, when I was brought on… Well, I was an Agency consultant from about ‘56, I guess, something.

[翻譯]
但到了60年代晚期，開始有一些人在官僚體系中升得相當高，他們進入機構後整個職業生涯都在機構內度過。我記得，事實上，在60年代，當我被引進時…嗯，我應該是從大約56年開始成為機構顧問。

--- 段落 362 (429 字元) ---
Anyway…I suppose it would  have been the early ‘60s… Under McCone an organization was formed called National Intelligence Programs Evaluation (NIPE), headed by John Bross, and it was  to look at the broadest management issues of the community as a whole.Bross  for some reason knew something about me—I don’t know exactly how that had  come about—but he invited me to come in to see him, and then he made me a  consultant of his.

[翻譯]
無論如何...我想應該是在60年代初...在麥康的領導下，成立了一個名為國家情報計畫評估（NIPE）的組織，由約翰·布羅斯領導，主要是為了全體社群的廣泛管理議題。布羅斯出於某種原因知道一些關於我的事情-我不確定這是如何發生的-但他邀請我去見他，然後讓我成為他的顧問。

--- 段落 363 (405 字元) ---
In fact, that was one of the most active relationships [indistinct] in the ‘60s.And he said to me once that it really worried him that this combination  of their having moved out to McLean and the fact that people in the Agency had  spent their whole professional lives in the Agency and didn’t know anybody, let  alone in the rest of the city, but in, you know, New York or wherever, really worried  him.

[翻譯]
事實上，在六十年代，這是其中一段最活躍的關係。他曾經告訴我，他真的很擔心他們搬到麥克林和那些在機構工作一生卻不認識任何人的人，連在城市其他地方，例如紐約或其他地方，都不認識，這讓他非常擔心。

--- 段落 364 (447 字元) ---
He used to shake his head about what that was going to lead to, because of  his own experience and that it was very valuable to have contacts in other worlds,  whether it was on Wall Street or wherever it is that you can get information from.And these people going up with these new careers didn’t have any of that.- Q1: Did the situation improve?- Marshall: “Consumer research” by the intelligence community has gotten a little  better over time.

[翻譯]
他過去常為那將導致什麼而搖頭，因為根據他自己的經驗，在其他世界建立聯繫非常寶貴，無論是在華爾街還是其他地方，都可以從中獲取信息。這些人開始進行新的事業時並沒有任何這方面的經驗。問1：情況有改善嗎？- 馬歇爾：隨著時間的推移，情報界對“消費者研究”有了一些進步。

--- 段落 365 (355 字元) ---
They now do some surveys of users; I don’t know that it really  influences what they do.It was striking how little interface or real knowledge they  had of what consumers wanted.One of the things I did was to conduct a survey of people on the NSC staff about  what they wanted.Strengths, weaknesses, what things weren’t they getting that  they might want.

[翻譯]
他們現在對用戶進行一些調查；我不知道這是否真正影響他們的做法。令人驚訝的是，他們對消費者想要什麼幾乎沒有界面或真正的了解。我做的事情之一是對NSC工作人員進行調查，了解他們想要什麼。優勢，劣勢，他們沒有得到的東西是什麼，他們可能想要的。

--- 段落 366 (440 字元) ---
Found they wanted, if they could get it, some of the products to  be focused on longer term trends, basic things that were happening, not the dayto-day events, more speculative about the future, but really thoughtful.Producing such things runs up against the ethos of people in the intelligence  community, that they shouldn’t be speculating, that they should be getting hard  information and then at most interpreting that for the readers.

[翻譯]
他們發現，如果可能的話，他們希望有一些產品專注於長期趨勢，基本的事情正在發生，不是每天的事件，更多是對未來的推測，但真正富有思考性。製作這些東西如同與情報界的人倫理觀念相抵觸，他們認為不應該進行推測，而應該獲取硬性信息，然後對讀者進行最多的解釋。

--- 段落 367 (364 字元) ---
But the actual  consumers wanted something rather different, at least in part.But the consumers  also wanted to know where there were controversies and differences of opinion  within the intelligence community.But again, at that point, the community was devoted to the notion that they  should resolve their differences internally and kind of speak with one voice.

[翻譯]
但實際消費者想要的東西有些不同，至少在某種程度上。消費者也想知道情報界內部的爭議和意見分歧。但當時，情報界致力於解決內部分歧，並且統一發聲。

--- 段落 368 (387 字元) ---
But  also, I guess the thing that drove some of this stuff about these new institutions,  like the NSCIC [Eds: National Security Council Intelligence Committee], was this  dissatisfaction of Kissinger and Nixon with the products, that they just didn’t think  were very good and lacking real intellectual quality.- Q1: What was the background of your study of the quality of intelligence?

[翻譯]
但我猜想，驅使一些有關這些新機構，如國家安全委員會情報委員會，的事情的原因是，基辛格和尼克松對產品的不滿，他們認為這些產品質量不高，缺乏真正的知識品質。問題1：您對情報品質的研究背景是什麼？

--- 段落 369 (453 字元) ---
- Marshall: When I was about to start work, I had another meeting with Kissinger in  which we reviewed again what he wanted done.And after discussion, one of the  things that I was asked to do as a second study was to make a judgment after  really looking at the assessments, estimates of the missile programs, because that  was the big thing that was happening… It had been left slightly open what particular area to pick to do this quality assessment.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：當我即將開始工作時，我又和基辛格開了一次會，我們再次檢討他希望完成的任務。經過討論後，我被要求進行第二項研究，要在真正查看對飛彈計劃進行的評估和估計後做出判斷，因為這是發生的重要事情... 就這個質量評估要選擇做哪個特定領域有些模糊不清。

--- 段落 370 (458 字元) ---
And it was then that essentially  the Soviet strategic missiles programs were picked.SS-9 was one of the biggest  of the issues.Questions about how many there were, what the characteristics of  the new systems were.And it wasn’t only just the technical things, but there were  issues of whether they had reloads, what was the motivation for moving to the  new systems…  
- Q1: I was just interested in why Kissinger was interested in the missiles assessment.

[翻譯]
當時蘇聯戰略導彈計劃開始被重視。SS-9導彈是其中一個重要議題。人們紛紛問起有多少個導彈、新系統的特點是什麼等問題。不僅僅是技術問題，還有關於是否有替裝、轉向新系統的動機是什麼等議題…

- 問題1：我只是對基辛格為何對導彈評估感興趣感到好奇。

--- 段落 371 (396 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, I think I proposed it, because I knew that it was an area of interest to  him.- Q1: And you had a competence in the area.- Marshall: And he agreed with that.- Q1: What were your findings?- Marshall: I thought there were just a lot of limitations, I guess in the NIEs on Soviet  strategic forces.I’m a little vague at this point on my findings.It wasn’t a very  favorable report.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：嗯，我想我提出這個建議，因為我知道這是他感興趣的領域。- Q1：而且你在這個領域有能力。- 馬歇爾：他同意了這一點。- Q1：你的研究發現是什麼？- 馬歇爾：我覺得NIE對蘇聯戰略力量存在很多限制，這方面的研究結果並不太理想。我對自己的研究結果有點模糊。

--- 段落 372 (454 字元) ---
In the sense that… There were things that they did report on  that represented the very skillful effort that was being made through various collection devices to analyze the programs, I mean in the sense of, you know, a new  silo was going in here or there, or, you know, “We see this at the test facilities at  Tyuratam,” and so on.Or various other technical analyses about the performance  of these missiles.But beyond that, there just wasn’t anything.

[翻譯]
就在這方面...他們報導了一些代表著透過各種收集裝置進行分析所做出的非常精湛的努力，我的意思是，你知道，在這裡或那裡出現了新的主塔，或者說，“我們在圖拉塔姆測試設施看到了這一切”，等等。還有關於這些導彈性能的各種技術分析。但除此之外，就沒有其他東西了。

--- 段落 373 (296 字元) ---
And I remember later, when I was working for Kissinger, not when I was doing  this study, there was a book called The Soviet Space Bluff [The Russian Space Bluff],  written by a defector [Leonid Vladimirov], which was filled with fascinating stuff,  giving you the names of the various designers.

[翻譯]
我記得以後在為基辛格工作時，而不是在進行這項研究時，有一本書名為《蘇聯太空謊言》[俄羅斯太空謊言]，由一名叛逃者[李奧尼德·弗拉迪米羅夫]撰寫，充滿迷人的內容，提供各種設計師的名字。

--- 段落 374 (472 字元) ---
I mean the intelligence community was very late in providing any information about—I brought this book to the  attention of people in the Agency, but they never did anything about it, to go  interview this guy, or anything.I mean, he was living in England.So, any sense of the personnel rivalries, the process by which these things were  designed, or about the organizations and so on…they didn’t provide anything.Or they…We didn’t have any broad sweeping recommendations.

[翻譯]
我指的是情報機構非常晚才提供有關這本書的任何信息 - 我向機構的人提到這本書，但他們從未採取任何行動，去採訪這個人，或者其他任何事情。我是說，他當時住在英格蘭。所以，關於人員之間的競爭，這些事情的設計過程，或者有關機構等等的情況...他們沒有提供任何信息。或者說...我們沒有任何廣泛的建議。

--- 段落 375 (476 字元) ---
We had some  recommendations which came out of this look at missile things, which led to this  proposal to do this prototype SS-9 study as an exemplar of the kind of the level of  analysis you would like to see.- Q1: Did your findings have an impact?- Marshall: Mmmm, ah, maybe a slight bit of improvement in subsequent NIEs as a  result of this exercise.I don’t know.The real improvement came with Larry Gershwin going out there.I mean it took that to make a real difference.

[翻譯]
在這次對導彈事物的研究中，我們得出了一些建議，這促成了這個對SS-9原型的研究提案，作為您希望看到的分析水準的示範。 Q1：您的研究結果是否產生影響？- 馬歇爾：嗯，或許這次練習的結果在隨後的NIEs中稍微有所改善。我不知道。真正的改善是由拉里格什溫帶出去的。我意思是這才會有真正的不同。

--- 段落 376 (418 字元) ---
He didn’t go out  there until Harry Rowen went out there.So it was the very early ‘80s.- Q1: What other areas of intelligence analysis needed improvement, in your opinion?- Marshall: One of the things I tried to get them to look at, like when they did this  special SS-9 study, was…try to get at things like the manpower costs associated  with different systems—Was that a motive for switching to newer systems or not?

[翻譯]
直到哈里·羅文走出去才去那裡。所以那是在80年代初期。問題1：在您看來，情報分析的哪些其他領域需要改進？- 馬歇爾：我試圖讓他們看到的一個事情是，就像當他們進行這個特別的SS-9研究時，嘗試去了解與不同系統相關的人力成本 - 這是否是改換新系統的動機？

--- 段落 377 (496 字元) ---
They seemed to be content to just report, “Well, two more silos have started,” with  no interpretation of, “Why is that happening?What does that suggest?” Couldn’t  provide any insight about any of the internal processes that led to any of these  things.Because I had requested it, they at least made an attempt to answer some of  these other kinds of questions.But again, it seemed to me that it was very important to understand the economics of this, I mean, what did these things really  cost?

[翻譯]
他們似乎只滿足於報告說：“好吧，又有兩個糧倉開始運作了”，沒有對“為什麼會發生這種情況？這意味著什麼？”進行任何解釋。他們無法提供任何關於導致這些事情發生的任何內部過程的見解。因為我已經請求過，他們至少試圖回答一些其他類型的問題。但再一次，對我來說很重要的是要了解這個經濟學，我的意思是，這些事情到底成本是多少？

--- 段落 378 (407 字元) ---
So, anyway, they made a stab at these things.Also, more about the relation of the SS-9 to the SS-7 and things like that, so you get some sense of the evolution of their systems and so on.- Q1: How long did the SS-9 study take?- Marshall: It was more like a year study, from spring 1970 to fall 1971.- Q1: Among the other special products for Kissinger, the main thing was the analysis  of key personalities?

[翻譯]
所以，無論如何，他們試圖對這些事情有所了解。而且，關於SS-9與SS-7之間的關係等等，這樣你就能感受到他們系統的演進等等。- Q1：SS-9的研究花了多久時間？- 馬歇爾：這更像是一年的研究，從1970年春天到1971年秋天。- Q1：對於基辛格的其他特別產品，主要是分析關鍵人物嗎？

--- 段落 379 (377 字元) ---
- Marshall: Biographic intelligence guidelines, if I remember correctly, it was kind of  a two-page form to be filled in that had headings, specifying the kind of information we wanted about the person.But I don’t think it ever had any impact at all.In the first place, Henry had this great interest in these people that he might have  to deal with in one fashion or the other.

[翻譯]
Marshall：如果我沒記錯的話，生平情報指引是一種兩頁表格，需要填寫有關人物信息的項目。但我認為它根本沒有任何影響力。首先，亨利對這些人感興趣，他或許需要以某種方式與他們打交道。

--- 段落 380 (448 字元) ---
One of the first things that came up was  this interest that he had in these psychological profiles that had been prepared  by Jerry Post and other people out at the CIA, which he wanted more of.He even  had the idea of some psychiatrist up in the Boston area, that was connected with  a very famous…this was a professional psychiatric clinic for the treatment of mental  diseases…I know about it from the work that I’d done with Herbert Goldhamer.

[翻譯]
其中一件首先浮現的事情是他對那些由Jerry Post和其他CIA的人準備的心理學檔案的興趣，他希望有更多這樣的資料。他甚至想到波士頓地區的某位精神科醫師，這位醫師和一家非常有名的…這是一家專門治療精神疾病的專業精神科診所有關…我對此有所了解是因為我和Herbert Goldhamer合作的工作。

--- 段落 381 (324 字元) ---
It  existed way back in the 1830s, 1840s and it was a private place where people with  mental problems could go, as contrasted with the state system of asylums.86 Any -  way, so Kissinger even wanted to get more work and thought it would be interesting  for this guy to somehow get involved in this.So he wanted more effort.

[翻譯]
這個地方起源於1830年代和1840年代，是一個供患有精神問題的人前往的私人場所，與國家精神病院制度形成對比。無論如何，Kissinger甚至想要做更多工作，認為讓這個人某種方式參與其中會很有趣。因此，他想要更多努力。

--- 段落 382 (324 字元) ---
People in  the Agency were extremely reluctant, just didn’t consider it one of their top-ofthe-line products, a little disreputable…it’s speculative, it’s a little oddball, etc.The thing that was striking to me was, OK, here’s something that Henry liked,  thought was useful, wanted more of, but essentially couldn’t get it.

[翻譯]
機構內的人們非常不情願，他們並不認為這是他們頂尖產品之一，有點名聲不佳...這是一個投機性的東西，有點古怪，等等。對我來說，令人驚訝的是，這是亨利喜歡的事物，認為很有用，想要更多，但基本上無法得到。

--- 段落 383 (274 字元) ---
And then when this coup took place, he was again… “Well, who are these  people…” And you have the background in the files, which is about, as I put it in  a kind of cynical way, sarcastic way… I mean it’s fine if you’re going to entertain  them, they like scotch or bourbon.

[翻譯]
當這次政變發生時，他再次...「那這些人是誰...」並且你在檔案中擁有背景，就像我用一種玩世不恭、諷刺的方式表達的那樣... 我的意思是，如果你要款待他們，他們喜歡威士忌或波本酒。

--- 段落 384 (442 字元) ---
It’s stuff that’s presumably acquired or written  down based on social contacts with these people, some sense of them, whether  they’re womanizers or not, but there’s nothing about what are they really like psychologically, as personalities, except sort of crude descriptors, you know, “A strong  person.” Nothing about ideological beliefs.So it’s very limited, it doesn’t show  any insight into the person at all.Just puts him in a category.

[翻譯]
這些資料可能是根據與這些人的社交聯繫所獲得或撰寫下來的，對他們有一定的了解，無論他們是否風流成性，但並沒有深入探討他們在心理上真正是什麼樣的人，作為個性，除了一些粗糙的描述，你知道，“一個堅強的人”。沒有提及意識形態信仰。因此這非常有限，完全沒有展示對這個人的洞察力，只是把他歸類於某個範疇。

--- 段落 385 (488 字元) ---
You know, “Catholic,” “military officer,” “likes bourbon” or “likes rock-and-roll music.” No information  about his thinking, or how he might behave in certain circumstances.- Q1: The coup was in Panama?- Marshall: Maybe a “coup” is too dramatic a word.Takeover of the government by a  military officer, I think.So Kissinger gets this stuff and they barely know much about these people.Maybe only for one or two of them there’s even any data at all and what it is this  piffling material.

[翻譯]
你知道，“天主教徒”，“軍官”，“喜歡波本威士忌”或“喜歡搖滾音樂”。沒有關於他的思想或在某些情況下可能如何行為的信息。- Q1：這次政變發生在巴拿馬嗎？- 馬歇爾：也許“政變”這個詞太戲劇化了。我想是由軍官接管政府。所以基辛格得到這些東西，他們對這些人幾乎一無所知。也許只有一兩個人有任何數據，而這些數據幾乎微不足道。

--- 段落 386 (443 字元) ---
So I get asked, “What could be done about this?” So I looked into  this, tried to understand a little more about how the thing worked, but only for a  few days.Then said, “Well, one thing you could do at least is write down what it is you want about these people, what would be useful to you.” And we did that and  sent it over.- Q1: Would greater use of the Bayesian method for analysis and communication  have improved intelligence analysis?

[翻譯]
所以有人問我，“這件事可以怎麼辦？”所以我調查了一下，試著更了解這件事是如何運作的，但只有幾天。然後我說，“好吧，至少你可以做的一件事是寫下你對這些人的需求，對你有用的是什麼。”我們做到了，然後把它送了過去。- Q1: 如果更廣泛地使用Bayesian方法進行分析和溝通，是否會提高智慧分析能力？

--- 段落 387 (395 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well again, that came up right at the beginning, because one of the  things that also came out of this early technique [?] was the way that uncertainties were handled in this kind of backhanded way of, in paragraph 28 they say  one thing and then they halfway take it back in paragraph 57.Uncertainty should  be more squarely faced, they should look for ways of presenting the thing.

[翻譯]
Marshall: 嗯，這又一次是在一開始就出現的，因為早期技術中發現的其中一個問題是，不確定性是如何以一種迂迴的方式處理的，就像第28段提到了一件事情，然後在第57段卻又半途而廢。應該更直接面對不確定性，他們應該尋找展示事物的方法。

--- 段落 388 (481 字元) ---
And  Kissinger was in favor of this even in saying, “Well, there are six alternatives and  here are our best guesses about the probabilities of those.” Well, they didn’t like  that at all.- Q1: Did they make some effort?- Marshall: Well, there were a couple of experiments to do that.But I think they were  kind of halfhearted.They were being forced to do something they didn’t like.At  the level of the Board of National Estimates, it was just seen as too crude and not  literary.

[翻譯]
基辛格甚至認同這一點，說：“嗯，有六種選擇，這是我們對這些可能性的最佳猜測。”嗯，他們一點也不喜歡這樣的做法。- 問：他們有做出努力嗎？- 馬歇爾：嗯，有一些實驗試圖這樣做。但我認為他們不太積極。他們被迫做他們不喜歡的事情。在國家評估委員會層面上，這被認為太過粗糙而且不夠文學化。

--- 段落 389 (462 字元) ---
That’s not the way you would try to convey any of these things.The Bayesian method is partly how you do analysis and partly how do you present the stuff.- Q1: Was the use of Bayesian methods driven by the studies by Kelly and Peterson?- Marshall: So those guys were…I guess Kelly, when I first met him, was at DARPA,  then he went off into this— There were a couple of small firms that were pushing  this sort of analysis and how you would do that kind of thing.

[翻譯]
這不是你想要傳達這些事情的方式。贝叶斯方法在分析時部分應用，部分呈現資訊。問題1：凱利和彼得森的研究促使使用贝叶斯方法嗎？- 馬歇爾：那些人......我想，凱利，當我第一次遇見他時，他正在DARPA工作，然後他轉而專注於這個......有幾家小公司正在推這種分析方法和實踐的方式。

--- 段落 390 (102 字元) ---
There was another  guy that I knew from RAND that was at Michigan…Ward Edwards…a set of these  people.

[翻譯]
我認識一位在密歇根大學的蘭德研究所的另一位人，名叫沃德·愛德華茲...這些人中的一員。

--- 段落 391 (438 字元) ---
There was both the presentational kind of thing…the Bayesian kind of  thing… But then there was also a set of people out there that were working on  situations where you get information over time…and supposing you have a  set of estimates, the likelihood of various alternatives, and you get a new piece  of information, how do you modify each of these… In fact one thing I did was  I sponsored a conference out in Coronado in California.

[翻譯]
有兩種方式呈現…貝葉斯方式…但也有一群人在研究隨著時間推移而獲得資訊的情況…假設你有一組估計值、各種不同的可能性，當你得到新的資訊時，該如何修改這些…事實上，我曾贊助在加利福尼亞州科羅納多舉行的一場會議。

--- 段落 392 (455 字元) ---
There people who had  been working in this field were all brought together…  
- Q1: Now, was this while you were at the NSC or afterward?- Marshall: Probably was after, because I think I got DARPA to put up the money,  yeah, probably soon after I got to the Pentagon.But Pat Crecine I remember was  there, this guy from Michigan.- Q1: Now what did Kissinger think of some of these experiments or the results of  these experiments?- Marshall: I forget now.

[翻譯]
那些在這個領域工作過的人都聚在一起了...
- Q1：這是在你在NSC期間還是之後嗎？- 馬歇爾：可能是之後，因為我想我讓DARPA出錢了，是的，可能是我到五角大樓後不久吧。但我記得帕特·克雷辛在那裡，這個來自密歇根的家伙。- Q1：孟席格是如何看待這些實驗或者實驗結果的？- 馬歇爾：我現在忘記了。

--- 段落 393 (489 字元) ---
I know that we got some and shipped them into him.But I  don’t think we got much of a reaction.I think we tried it out on some of the other  people and they sort of liked it, but it wasn’t as though they were entranced by it.- Q1: Were there other ways in which you tried to improve intelligence analysis?- Marshall: I made this big effort on organizational behavior, but I described some of  that in the earlier interview or session.- Q1: While you were at the NSC?- Marshall: Yes, right.

[翻譯]
我知道我們有一些，然後把它們運送給他。但我覺得他的反應不是很強烈。我們也嘗試在其他一些人身上試驗，他們似乎有點喜歡，但並非對此著迷。- Q1: 您是否有其他方式試圖改善情報分析？- 馬歇爾：我在組織行為方面做出了很大的努力，但我在之前的訪談或會議中已經描述過一些了。- Q1: 在您在NSC時嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的，就是那個時候。

--- 段落 394 (435 字元) ---
- Q1: Covering which topic?- Marshall: Well, the thing took two forms.One, there were a few people at the Agency  who were quite interested in it, particularly some of the people over in the clandestine services side, that I had gotten to know while I was at RAND, because they  had come to me to try to get some information about a country that I had a lot  of contact with, and so I had talked to them somewhat in the course of that.

[翻譯]
問題1：涉及哪個主題？- 馬歇爾：嗯，這件事有兩個方面。首先，機構內有一些人對這個很感興趣，尤其是在秘密服務方面的一些人，我在蘭德研究所時與他們熟悉起來，因為他們找我取得一個我與一個國家有很多接觸的信息，所以在這過程中我有些對話。

--- 段落 395 (483 字元) ---
So,  after I was at the NSC, I said, “OK, look, here’s a way of doing analysis that might  be useful.I will try to tutor, in a way, although I don’t know what the right word  for it would be, some set of analysts, or some people, to try to make sure they  understand what it is they ought to try look at when they look at these organizations.What information do you really want to have?” And so on.So, three or four  of them came down several times and spent time talking about this.

[翻譯]
所以，在我去了NSC之後，我說：“好吧，這裡有一個可能會有用的分析方法。我會試著指導一些分析師，或者一些人，讓他們明白應該在查看這些組織時要看什麼。他們真正想要哪些信息？等等。所以，其中三到四位人幾次下來，花時間討論這個。

--- 段落 396 (332 字元) ---
And then…  That was one thing.There were these people who were very interested in it, who  kind of picked it up, did whatever they did with it, I don’t know, they kind of disappeared back into the clandestine services.Never had much effect on the people  in the Directorate of Intelligence.There may be some papers around from that.

[翻譯]
然後... 這是一件事。有一些人對這個非常感興趣，他們將它拿走，做了他們該做的事情，我不知道，他們隨後消失在秘密服務中。這並沒對情報局的人造成太大影響。也許這段時間會有一些文件。

--- 段落 397 (453 字元) ---
- Q1: There was an informal group of CIA producers you convened in late 1972 to  determine data needed to support intelligence analyses based on theories of organizational and human behavior.One member of the group looked at a case of  using those methodologies to understand the French position in GATT [General  Agreement on Tariffs and Trade] discussions in late 1973.Was that the same group?- Marshall: Well, it was kind of the second phase of that.

[翻譯]
問1：1972年底，您召集了一個非正式的CIA製作人小組，決定支持基於組織和人類行為理論的情報分析所需的數據。該小組的一名成員研究了一個案例，使用這些方法來了解1973年底關於GATT（關稅和貿易一般協定）談判的法國立場。這是同一個小組嗎？- 馬歇爾：嗯，這算是那個工作的第二階段。

--- 段落 398 (421 字元) ---
Because after we’d done  this other thing, just talking… What would you really want to know?I decided it  would be good to have a case that would be done, where they could show what  it was they could do.And it would be a kind of test of could they carry out something like this.Mainly the earlier discussions have been about, “Well, what do you  want to know?What are the kind of things you want to find out?” And so on.

[翻譯]
因為在我們做完這件事之後，只是在聊天...你真正想知道的是什麼？我決定好好安排一個案例，讓他們展示他們能做到的事情。這將是一種考驗，看看他們是否能完成這樣的事情。主要的早期討論都是關於，“嗯，你想知道什麼？你想找出什麼樣的事情？”等等。

--- 段落 399 (459 字元) ---
You’d  want to find out about the processes, who’s involved, things about the internal  procedures.But then it came to a point where we thought about, “Well, let’s do a  kind of test about what they can do.”  And the idea was—Or my idea was, “Well, look, a country I know about is France,  so let’s pick France.” It’s also, in principle, a country that we should be able to find  out a lot about.It’s not like Russia or China… So I went to see Ken [Kenneth W.

[翻譯]
你會想要了解這些過程，誰參與其中，內部程序的事情。但後來我們想到了一個問題，「好吧，讓我們來做一個測試看看他們能做什麼。」我的想法是 - 「好吧，我知道的國家是法國，所以就選擇法國吧。」原則上，這也是我們應該能夠找到很多信息的國家。這不像是俄羅斯或中國... 所以我去找了肯（肯尼斯·W.）。

--- 段落 400 (425 字元) ---
]  Dam to discuss with him… He was a kind of special assistant to George Shultz,  who was then the Secretary of the Treasury, I think.But Dam had an office in the  White House…I don’t remember whether Shultz did.…I knew Dam quite well, so  I went to him and said, “What is a topic?What is something we could get them to  focus on?” And he said, “Well, look, something that would be interesting is French  agricultural policy.

[翻譯]
與他討論……他在喬治·舒爾茲（George Shultz）當時是財政部長的一種特別助手，我想。但是達姆（Dam）在白宮有一個辦公室……我不記得舒爾茲是否有。我很熟悉達姆，所以我去找他，問他：“有什麼話題？有什麼事情可以讓他們集中注意力？”他說：“嗯，看，一個有趣的話題是法國農業政策。”

--- 段落 401 (335 字元) ---
” And I know a lot about that… Because the idea was to pick  something that we [?] could judge how good this thing was.So we picked that.I then proposed that—and I forget who it was that exactly I proposed it to—It  might have been Ed Proctor, who was still the head of the intelligence directorate.And he picked a guy who was retired.

[翻譯]
我對這方面很了解...因為想法是要挑選一些我們可以評判這個事物有多好的東西。所以我們挑選了那個。然後我提議，我忘記確切是向誰提議了，可能是還在情報司令部任職的艾德·普羅克特。他挑選了一個已經退休的人。

--- 段落 402 (414 字元) ---
…I can’t remember the guy’s name now, but  he’s somebody who I’d known for a long time, who had an economics background  and had been in the Agency from way back in the ‘50s, had recently retired at this  point.Who had been a close friend to Joe Loftus.So had been up to RAND several  times.So I really knew him pretty well.So Proctor proposed that they get this guy  back out of retirement, and give him this job.

[翻譯]
…我現在記不得那個人的名字，但他是我認識很久的一個人，具有經濟學背景，從上世紀50年代就在機構工作，最近才退休。他曾是喬·洛夫塔斯的密友，所以曾多次到過蘭德公司。所以我真的很熟悉他。普羅克特建議重新請這個退休的人出來，給他這份工作。

--- 段落 403 (392 字元) ---
And the idea was for the person to  draw on—not to have to do collection so much—what already was in the Agency.What did they really know?Pull together everything they knew that would fit this  particular topic of their agricultural policy and their negotiations stances.And he  did this paper, which I thought was not really very good, and neither did Ken Dam,  because we both looked at it.

[翻譯]
這個想法是讓這個人去利用機構內已經存在的資料，而不是繼續進行大量的資料收集。他們究竟知道什麼？將所有他們知道與農業政策和談判立場相關的內容整合在一起。他完成了這份報告，我覺得這份報告不是很好，肯．達姆也是這麼認為，因為我們兩個都看過它。

--- 段落 404 (462 字元) ---
Because it really didn’t take over this organizational  behavior thing, didn’t get down to the level that you need.But, anyway, it wasn’t  pursued anymore.I took it to be, “Look, these guys may not be up to doing this.”  
- Q1: How were intelligence products delivered to users?- Marshall: At the time, there was almost an exclusive reliance on the publications.I  think there always was a certain trickle of people who came down and met faceto-face with people.

[翻譯]
因為它真的沒有完全掌握這個組織行為的事情，沒有達到你需要的水平。但無論如何，它不再被追求。我認為這是說：“看來這些人可能無法做到這一點。”
- Q1：情報產品是如何交付給使用者的？- 馬歇爾：當時，幾乎完全依靠出版物。我認為總是有一些人下來與人面對面會面。

--- 段落 405 (427 字元) ---
I don’t mean briefings, but coming to the office, talking with  them and so on.I think Frank Walters at the time felt there was too little of this,  and it’s not just that the intelligence person making some sort of presentation can  communicate more about what’s behind the thing, or can answer questions, but  also can come away with a better sense of what the people he’s talking to really  are interested in and care about.

[翻譯]
我不是指簡報，而是指走到辦公室，和他們交談等等。我認為當時的弗蘭克·沃爾特斯覺得這方面太少了，這不僅是情報人員進行某種形式的演示，可以更多地溝通的觀點，或者回答問題，而且還能更好地了解他正在交談的人們真正感興趣和關心的事情。

--- 段落 406 (348 字元) ---
Another thing I tried to have done—it kind of didn’t get anywhere—I thought  that there were some kind of topics that actually short videos would be better.For example, instead of trying to describe, through writing or even verbally,  how a multiple-warhead system worked, that a short video that showed how it  worked would communicate a lot more.

[翻譯]
我嘗試做的另一件事情──在某種程度上沒有進展──我覺得某些主題實際上更適合使用短片。例如，不是透過文字描述或甚至口頭解釋多頭彈道系統運作的方式，而是透過展示它是如何運作的短片，能傳達更多信息。

--- 段落 407 (291 字元) ---
Or, I felt—and again, neither of these  things was done very well—thought that… Well, one of the things that seemed  to be happening at the time was that… Because of the split with the Russians, the  Chinese were moving their forces, and repositioning them more to the north and  so on, etc.

[翻譯]
或者，我覺得 - 而且，這兩件事都沒有做得很好 - 認為... 嗯，當時似乎正在發生的一件事是...由於與俄羅斯的分裂，中國人正在調動他們的軍隊並將它們重新定位到更北部等地方。

--- 段落 408 (484 字元) ---
And that, for example, if one, again, had a kind of even like a cartoon  version…or a map, and time-phasing showing, OK, here’s where all of these  forces were in the early ‘50s, here is… These units have moved from here, they’re  now over here… Or people have been taken from here and moved to there…  Fortification programs begun and various other things.That you would be able  to see if that kind of thing was just… The time-sequencing—You would see the  adjustment of the forces.

[翻譯]
例如，如果再次有一種像卡通版或地圖的版本，並且時間軸顯示，你可以看到在五十年代初這些部隊的位置，這些單位已經從這裡移動到這裡... 或者人們從這裡轉移到那裡... 設防計劃開始以及其他各種事情。你將能夠看到如果那種事情只是... 時間排序 - 你將看到部隊的調整。

--- 段落 409 (440 字元) ---
You would see also the big expansion of the Russian  forces along the—That would tell you more… First, the analyst would probably  see things he might not otherwise see.But they would be a wonderful way of  presenting things to people at the top level.I did have a primitive version of the MIRV thing done, that was never quite good  enough to show Henry, and the other one I kept asking people to do and never  succeeded in having it done.

[翻譯]
你也會看到俄羅斯軍隊的大規模擴張-這可以告訴你更多...首先，分析師可能會看到他可能否則看不到的東西。但這將是向高層人士呈現事物的一個很棒的方式。我曾經做過一個原始版本的MIRV計畫，但從來沒有好到足以展示給亨利看，我也一直讓人們做另一個版本，但從來沒有成功。

--- 段落 410 (255 字元) ---
But I think there are just terrific possibilities in the  presentation of stuff other than having people just read these things or look at  static maps and so on.Everything we know about man’s evolutionary history is just tremendously focused on the eyes.

[翻譯]
不過我認為在呈現東西方面，除了讓人們閱讀這些資料或觀看靜態地圖之外，還有很棒的可能性。我們對於人類進化歷史的了解都非常專注在眼睛上。

--- 段落 411 (463 字元) ---
Lionel Tiger says one of the reasons television is so compelling to people, as against reading, and is in some sense ruining  American education, as it is everyplace else, I guess, by competing for time with  people, is because people so prefer to get information… And the problem on  television is the information they get is so both inadequate and misguided that…  
- Q1: Any other presentation techniques?- Marshall: No, those were the main ones I think about.

[翻譯]
萊昂納爾·泰格認為，電視之所以對人們如此吸引，與閱讀相比，並且在某種程度上正在破壞美國的教育，也許在其他地方也是如此，是因為人們更喜歡獲取信息...電視上的問題是人們獲得的信息既不足夠也是偏誤的...

- Q1: 還有其他的呈現技巧嗎？- 馬歇爾：沒有了，這些是我所想到的主要的。

--- 段落 412 (455 字元) ---
Frank Walters was a CIA analyst, one of the good guys from the ‘50s that I knew  very well.I can’t remember exactly what his ideas were, but they’re probably like  this {…} briefings, face-to- face contact.- Q1: Could you describe the impact of the Schlesinger report on reform of the intelligence community and the role you played?- Marshall: I think it was in December of ‘70 that Nixon kind of instructed Shultz and  Kissinger to undertake this review.

[翻譯]
Frank Walters是一名中情局分析師，是我從50年代就非常熟悉的好人之一。我記不清楚他的想法是什麼了，但可能是像這樣{...}簡報，面對面的接觸。- 問題1：您能描述施萊辛格報告對情報界改革的影響以及您所扮演的角色嗎？- 馬歇爾：我認為是在70年12月，尼克松讓舒爾茨和基辛格進行這個審查。

--- 段落 413 (378 字元) ---
And then I think initially there was a March  reporting date, and then some decisions were supposed to be made in April-May  or something.Then it got postponed till later.And so you had the March 1971  Schlesinger report, which was kind of an interim report.Then there was further  work and a final report which made…87 And as I look at this thing it looks kind of  descriptive.

[翻譯]
然後我想最初是在3月有一個報告的日期，然後一些決定應該在4月或5月做出。然後它被延期到以後。所以你有了1971年3月的舒勒辛格報告，這在某種程度上是一個臨時報告。然後有進一步的工作和最終報告...87而當我看著這件事時，它看起來有點描述性。

--- 段落 414 (454 字元) ---
And the thing that happened between this and the reports that came  out later… The later ones are focused more on recommendations about what to  do and kind of the rationale for the changes and so on.And while I was the NSC  representative on the thing in an actual way, I guess nominally Wayne Smith was,  but then he asked me to do it because I’d done these earlier intelligence studies  for Henry.And the bulk of the effort was done by the OMB people.

[翻譯]
在這之間發生的事情和後來出現的報告之間... 後來的報告更專注於建議應該怎麼做，以及改變的理據等等。雖然我在這件事上實際上是國家安全委員會的代表，我想名義上是韋恩·史密斯，但後來他要求我來做，因為我曾為亨利做過這些早期情報研究。而這項工作的大部分工作是由管理與預算辦公室的人完成的。

--- 段落 415 (403 字元) ---
What happened  at the end was, however, that Schlesinger had gone over to the AEC [Atomic  Energy Commission]—I forget the dates of that—I guess probably in September,  I wrote the final kind of summary that went up to Nixon.You know, Here’s what  is recommended, and also attached were the things he would sign, like a general  memo… A memo to Helms as to his new duties and what he was directed to do.

[翻譯]
然而，最後發生的是，施萊辛格已轉投至原子能委員會（AEC）——我忘記了那段的日期——我猜可能是在九月，我寫了最終的摘要，提交尼克松。你知道的，這裡建議了什麼，還附有他會簽署的事項，如一份一般的備忘錄... 一份給 Helms 的備忘錄，解釋他的新職責和被指示要做的事情。

--- 段落 416 (392 字元) ---
And I drafted all of that, because there wasn’t a comparable person over at OMB  because Schlesinger had left.…And there may have been the start of some kind  of a draft…I think there was a partial thing that…May well have been that Bill  Kaufmann had—Because he was acting as a consultant to Schlesinger at the time.But all of that stopped when Schlesinger left and I took over to finish it.

[翻譯]
我起草了所有的內容，因為OMB那邊沒有一個可以媲美的人，因為施萊辛格離開了……也許開始有一些草稿的痕跡……我想那時可能有一部分……也許是比爾·考夫曼有參與，因為他當時是施萊辛格的顧問。但當施萊辛格離職，我接手完成它時，所有這些都停止了。

--- 段落 417 (385 字元) ---
Then Haig  and Smith undertook to send it around to the OMB people, to whoever else they  thought they needed to go to…Bronson Tweedy…I’m not sure all the people.And then a few changes and it was finalized… In fact, I prepared the final versions  and it was sent up through Smith and Kissinger, Haig, to Nixon to sign off on.- Q1: What happened after the recommendations went to Nixon?

[翻譯]
然後海格和史密斯承諾將其發送給OMB的相關人員，以及其他任何他們認為需要的人…布朗森·特溫迪…我不確定還有哪些人。然後進行了一些更改，最終定稿…實際上，我準備了最終版本，然後通過史密斯和基辛格、海格，交由尼克松簽署。- Q1：建議提交給尼克松後會發生什麼？

--- 段落 418 (469 字元) ---
- Marshall: After the reorganization was put in place, improving community management, we were involved in monitoring the implementation of the reorganization,  and secondly, reviewing in selected areas the quality of the products.I spent a lot of time talking with people up near Helms, who were involved in  making the changes, particularly a man named Bronson Tweedy and just following what they did.They had to set up this new IC staff, there were personnel issues.

[翻譯]
Marshall: 在重新組織完成後，我們著手改善社區管理，參與監督重新組織的實施，並在特定領域審查產品的質量。我花了很多時間與負責進行改變的Helms附近的人交談，尤其是一個名叫Bronson Tweedy的人，並跟著他們的做法。他們必須建立這個新的IC團隊，涉及人事問題。

--- 段落 419 (474 字元) ---
We’d monitor that and periodically make reports to Kissinger about it.We were  often consulted by those people.That was the main thing.We tried to do some things in the area of the training and management of analysis.One of the things we found was there was really no investment in the training  of analysts, or what there was was not very good.On the management side, we looked at the issue of career lines.And only in  a few areas did people stay in their particular area.

[翻譯]
我們會監控這個情況，並定期向基辛格報告。這些人常常會諮詢我們。這是主要的事情。我們試著在培訓和分析管理領域做些工作。我們發現一個問題是實際上並沒有對分析師的培訓進行投資，或者投資的效果並不明顯。在管理方面，我們關注職業生涯發展問題。只有少數幾個領域的人員會一直留在自己的專業領域裡。

--- 段落 420 (457 字元) ---
That happened in things  connected with the Soviet Union, but in other regional offices, people had very  little background.But again, even in the Soviet Union they had a group of people  dealing with the Soviet navy, but they turned over so rapidly that nobody there  ever got to have real expertise in the Soviet navy.So there’s this kind of incompatibility of the personnel system with getting really skilled people, knowledgeable  people doing analysis.

[翻譯]
這種情況在與蘇聯有關的事務中發生，但在其他地區辦事處裡，人們的背景非常有限。即使在蘇聯，他們也有一群負責處理蘇聯海軍事務的人，但因為人員流動過快，沒有人有機會真正掌握對蘇聯海軍的專業知識。因此，人員制度和培養真正有技術、有知識的分析人員之間存在著某種不相容性。

--- 段落 421 (343 字元) ---
We recommended that they look at that and see what they  wanted to do about that.We didn’t have any particular recommendations, we just  pointed out that there were really problems in terms of getting people to have  the intellectual capital to do a good job.I mean, what it comes back to in my mind— It shows also the virtue of lateral entry.

[翻譯]
我們建議他們看看這個問題，並想想他們想采取什麼行動。我們沒有特別的建議，只是指出在讓人們具有足夠的智力資本來做好工作方面確實存在問題。我是說，對我來說，最終歸結為橫向入職的優勢。

--- 段落 422 (488 字元) ---
I mean, again, one of the big problems with the career system out there is it’s  kind of based on the idea of getting younger guys—of course, it wasn’t formed  that way as an agency—and that’s one of the reasons the Agency was a lot better  in the ‘50s than I think it was later.They saddled themselves for security reasons, I  guess, among other things, with a career system in which people were supposed to  come in from universities.And a number of them just had undergraduate degrees.

[翻譯]
我的意思是，再說一次，存在的職業體制中其中一個主要問題是基於吸引年輕人的想法 - 當然，它成立時不是作為一個機構 - 這也是我認為60年代的機構比之後更好的原因之一。他們為了安全原因（我想，還有其他原因），困於一個人們應該從大學中進入的職業體制中。其中一些人只有學士學位。

--- 段落 423 (497 字元) ---
And kind of progress up and kind of learn on the job, and so on.Well, you’re not  necessarily going to get great analysts out of them.- Q1: Particularly if you’re not paying attention to training.- Marshall: That’s right.So the big thing about Larry Gershwin was, first, he was technically better trained than most of the people they’d had looking at the missile  programs, or the strategic forces programs and he’d shown real analytic ability,  and was brought in by Harry Rowen at my suggestion.

[翻譯]
然後逐漸進步，然後在工作中學習，依此類推。嗯，你不一定會從他們身上得到優秀的分析師。-問題1：特別是如果你沒有關注培訓的話。- 馬歇爾：沒錯。所以拉里·格什溫最重要的一點是，首先，他在技術方面接受的培訓比他們許多負責研究飛彈計畫或戰略力量計畫的人更好，並且他展現出真正的分析能力，並且是在我建議下由哈利·魯文引進的。

--- 段落 424 (434 字元) ---
They have a fundamental  problem of just the intellectual capacity and analytic capabilities of the people  they have.That means you can organize, you can invest, you can do certain kinds  of things well with a career system of that sort, but there are other things you  can’t do very well.So you can run collection systems and so forth…American  intelligence is relatively strong on collection and weak on analysis.- Q1: To this day?

[翻譯]
他們所面臨的一個基本問題是其人員的智力能力和分析能力。這意味著你可以組織，可以投資，可以在某些方面做得很好，但有些事情你做不太好。所以你可以運作收集系統等等...美國情報在收集方面相對強大，但在分析方面較弱。-問題1：直到現在為止？

--- 段落 425 (479 字元) ---
- Marshall: I think so, but I don’t pay very much attention to it anymore.But I look at  it and it doesn’t seem any better, but I don’t pay that much attention.And then the other thing we called their attention to was some possibilities of  new training type techniques, this method developed at RAND, reproducing  scoring systems, to judge how much people really knew about areas, how good  they were at reporting, how certain or uncertain they were about the answers they gave.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我想是的，但我不再非常注意這個了。我看一下，感覺好像沒有改善，但我沒有那麼在意。然後我們還指出了一些新的訓練技術可能性，這種方法是在蘭德發展的，可以再現評分系統，來判斷人們對某些領域的了解程度，他們在報告時有多出色，對自己給出的答案有多確定或不確定。

--- 段落 426 (465 字元) ---
But all that just frightened them, they didn’t want anything to do with  anything.This was people down in the organization, not Tweedy.Later when I was working for Henry, and Chip Pickett and I—in fact you might  talk to Chip about it—we had all of these misgivings about the personnel system,  about training, and we tried to communicate some of those in a variety of ways  to the people out there.But, you know, they were not really that inclined to do  anything.

[翻譯]
但所有這些只是讓他們感到害怕，他們不想再有什麼關係。這些是組織中的人，而不是 Tweedy。後來當我在為亨利工作時，和 Chip Pickett 一起時，事實上你可能要和 Chip 談談這件事，我們對人事系統、培訓等方面都有很多顧慮，試圖以各種方式將這些溝通給外界的人們。但他們並不怎麼願意採取行動。

--- 段落 427 (372 字元) ---
I mean, that meant changing something that was very basic in the organization and it would take a lot of effort, it would be a really big change.When we did encourage some of this lateral entry—I encouraged Schlesinger in  that direction and he did a little bit of it… And then later, particularly under Casey,  still more of it was done.I don’t know what’s happening now.

[翻譯]
我是說，這意味著改變組織中非常基本的事情，這將需要大量的努力，這將是一個非常大的變革。當我們鼓勵某些橫向入口時 - 我鼓勵Schlesinger朝著這個方向前進，他也做了一點... 然後稍後，尤其是在Casey的領導下，做了更多的這方面的工作。我不知道現在發生了什麼事。

--- 段落 428 (483 字元) ---
- Q1: Did you have any role in preparing the new National Security Intelligence Directives (NSCIDs) that followed the Schlesinger report?- Marshall: Not that I remember, I don’t think so.It might well have been the special  group over in OMB, but I’m not actually sure who did the drafting.- Q1: The NSCIC just met once or twice?- Marshall: Yeah, probably.It may have met some after Kissinger and I left.But that’s  right, I can only remember one meeting, actually, when I was there.

[翻譯]
問1：您是否參與了準備隨著施萊辛格報告而來的新國家安全情報指令（NSCIDs）的任何角色？- 馬歇爾：就我記得來說，我不認為有。很可能是OMB裡的特別小組製定的，但我並不確定是誰實際起草的。- 問1：NSCIC只開過一兩次會議吧？- 馬歇爾：是的，可能是這樣。也許在基辛格和我離開後有開過一些。但沒錯，我只記得在我在那裡的時候開過一次會議。

--- 段落 429 (439 字元) ---
- Q1: Did the infrequent meetings of the NSCIC result in a lack of direction given to  the intelligence community by decisionmakers?- Marshall: When I tried to get from Kissinger, “Well, what do you really want” and so  on, we didn’t get very much.I mean we’d get these kind of gripes about how bad  the stuff is and so on, but you couldn’t get them to sit down and put together…  You might talk with Chip Pickett about that.He was around.

[翻譯]
Q1：NSCIC稀少的會議是否導致決策者未能給情報界明確方向？- 馬歇爾：當我試圖向基辛格問出，“你真正想要什麼”之類的問題時，我們得到的不太多。我意思是，我們會聽到一些關於情況多糟糕之類的抱怨，但你無法讓他們坐下來共同努力...你可以跟奇普·皮克特討論這件事。他就在附近。

--- 段落 430 (408 字元) ---
I can’t remember whether we tried to send out some kind of  request for a statement of what they most wanted.The only thing that, as I say,  worked was this survey I did of the NSC staff, and through them you get what  they would have liked and what they thought Kissinger would find useful.I sent  the results out to the people at CIA.- Q1: What did they do with it?- Marshall: At the moment, not very much.

[翻譯]
我記不得我們是否曾試圖發出某種要求，要求他們最想要的是什麼。正如我所說的，唯一有效的是我對國家安全委員會(NSC)工作人員所做的這項調查，通過他們，你可以知道他們想要什麼，以及他們認為基辛格會覺得有用的。我把調查結果發給中央情報局的人們。- Q1：他們拿來做了什麼？- 馬歇爾：目前，沒有太多作用。

--- 段落 431 (440 字元) ---
There was one thing that was requested  by the people who followed the Soviet Union, which we put a special effort on.That was to create a new product, which was called something like “The Forum” or  something like that.Which was to come out maybe once a month and contain an  expression of views of people on some major controversy that existed.And they  hated it, and they continued it for a while and dropped it at the first opportunity.

[翻譯]
有一件事是蘇聯支持者提出的要求，我們非常努力去實現。那就是創造一個新產品，類似於“論壇”之類的東西。這個產品可能每個月出一次，包含人們對一些重大爭議的觀點。他們討厭這個產品，繼續了一段時間後，在第一個機會就放棄了它。

--- 段落 432 (469 字元) ---
But we did get to do it for about four, five, six months, something like that.- Q1: So there was just massive resistance across the board, or inertia?- Marshall: Right.Well, over time I think they’ve improved.They do some of their  own surveys now.I don’t think they’re as—And they have sent people around  to talk with people.And so they’ve picked up on some of it.I don’t know that it  really affects what they end up doing, that is the kind of products they produce.

[翻譯]
但我們確實做了大約四、五、六個月，類似這樣的事情。- 問題1：所以整個部門都存在巨大的阻力，或者是慣性嗎？- 馬歇爾：對的。嗯，隨著時間的推移，我認為他們已經有所改善。他們現在自己進行一些調查。我認為他們並不像...他們已經派人到處與人交談。因此他們有些收穫。我不知道這是否真的影響了他們最終所做的事情，也就是他們生產的產品。

--- 段落 433 (387 字元) ---
But they go through the process anyway.They didn’t do anything.They didn’t do  anything before.- Q1: You mentioned earlier that the Net Assessment Group was included in the intelligence reorganization document when it was brokered around by Smith and Haig.- Marshall: But it was not in my draft.- Q1: The March 1971 version of the Schlesinger report calls for a net assessment  function.

[翻譯]
但他們還是繼續進行流程。他們沒有做任何事情。他們以前什麼都沒做。- Q1：您之前提到網絡評估組（Net Assessment Group）被包含在情報重組文件中，當時由史密斯和海格簽署。- 馬歇爾：但這不在我的草稿中。- Q1：1971年3月版本的施萊辛格報告要求進行網絡評估功能。

--- 段落 434 (425 字元) ---
- Marshall: I had forgotten about that, but it wasn’t, I know, in the other version that I  drafted that included recommendations.- Q1: Lionel Olmer gave a talk at Harvard in 1980 in which he claimed that the  President’s Foreign Intelligence Advisory Board (PFIAB) wanted net assessment  performed by the NSC, but that Kissinger was resistant.- Marshall: Well, as I told you, there were several sources of a push to do that.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我已經忘記了這件事，但在我起草包含建議的另一個版本中，我知道這樣做並不是。- Q1：Lionel Olmer在1980年在哈佛大學發表演講，他聲稱總統外國情報諮詢委員會(PFIAB)希望由NSC執行網絡評估，但基辛格卻持反對態度。- 馬歇爾：嗯，正如我告訴過你的，有幾個來源都在推動這樣做。

--- 段落 435 (472 字元) ---
I think  I told you of these people who were involved in the Blue Ribbon Panel… The  three people that visited me from the Blue Ribbon Panel were on the staff.After  the fact, I talked with Ruben Mettler because I had been told that for the Blue  Ribbon Panel report that he had been the one that had pushed for this thing [net  assessment] within the DoD structure.But these people came over…and it was  before I finished.So it was early ‘70, probably March, maybe April.

[翻譯]
我想我曾告訴過你這些參與藍絲帶小組的人...從藍絲帶小組來拜訪我的三個人是工作人員。事實上，我和魯本·梅特勒交談過，因為我曾聽說他在藍絲帶小組報告中一直在推動國防部組織中的這件事情[淨評估]。但這些人過來了...而且那時我還沒結束。所以大概是70年代初，可能是三月或四月。

--- 段落 436 (419 字元) ---
They had somehow heard the fact that Henry had me doing this, came over, and lobbied for me  to put in my recommendations to him this reestablishment of a net assessment  group at the NSC.But I didn’t have any strong sense of— I didn’t personally feel  that that was the big thing.Maybe it would be good, maybe not, I don’t know.But  it didn’t fit with the things I was actually coming to, issues I was then addressing.

[翻譯]
他們不知何故聽說了亨利要我這樣做的事情，過來遊說我向他提出重建一個在國家安全委員會的淨評估小組的建議。但我並沒有明確感覺-我本人覺得這不是大事。也許這樣做會不錯，也許不會，我不知道。但這與我當時正在處理的議題沒有太大關聯。

--- 段落 437 (488 字元) ---
- Q1: Was the 6 December 1971 directive from Secretary of Defense Melvin Laird  what you were referring to when you said that Laird issued a directive creating  a Director of Net Assessment at the Pentagon the day after Nixon’s intelligence  memo came out?- Marshall: Maybe we didn’t see this and maybe it took this time… But we knew right  away that he had decided to do this.…I forget how we knew.- Q1: Before that he hadn’t acted at all on the recommendations of the Blue Ribbon Panel?

[翻譯]
問1：你所指的是1971年12月6日國防部長梅爾文·萊爾德發出的指令，當時你說萊爾德在尼克松發出情報備忘錄後的第二天在五角大樓設立了一個網路評估主任嗎？- 馬歇爾：也許我們當時沒看到這個，也許花了這段時間... 但我們立即知道他已決定這樣做... 我忘了我們是怎麼知道的。-問1：在那之前，他對藍帶小組的建議完全沒有採取任何行動嗎？

--- 段落 438 (458 字元) ---
- Marshall: No, he had not.- Q1: Why do you think he was so opposed to setting up a net assessment function?- Marshall: I don’t know that he was strongly opposed.But he probably wasn’t  strongly for it.I don’t know.Actually, the most interesting guy to talk to about it is  dead—Fred Buzhardt.When I was over at the NSC trying to get the net assessment process started, he was one of the really helpful people at the Pentagon and  he was very close to Laird.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：不，他並沒有。
- Q1：你認為他為什麼如此反對建立一個網絡評估功能？
- 馬歇爾：我不知道他是否強烈反對。但他可能並不強烈支持。我不知道。事實上，最有趣的談論對象已經去世了—弗雷德·布茲哈特。當我在國家安全委員會試圖啟動網絡評估流程時，他是五角大樓中一位非常幫助的人，並且和萊爾德關係非常密切。

--- 段落 439 (286 字元) ---
…But I don’t know who you could talk to about that.- Q1: What’s your general assessment of the result of the 1971 reorganization?- Marshall: Well, it’s so long ago, and so many other things have intervened.I don’t  know.It’s hard to—Certainly it changed eventually, but only eventually.

[翻譯]
...但我不知道你該和誰談論這件事。問題1：您對1971年重組的結果有什麼整體評價？- 馬歇爾：嗯，那是很久以前的事了，而且發生了很多其他事情。我不知道。很難說...當然最終是有變化的，但只是最終。

--- 段落 440 (216 字元) ---
I think the top-level management of the community—It’s hard to say that it’s—on issues  that matter, or the thing I have the best sense about, the quality of analysis—It’s  hard to say that it’s had that much effect.

[翻譯]
我認為社區的高層管理──很難說這是──對重要問題或我最了解的事情，分析品質──很難說它產生了很大影響。

--- 段落 441 (475 字元) ---
I mean in some areas—But it’s more this  matter of personnel, various people, like Gershwin, or some of the NIOs [National  Intelligence Officers] they’ve had in the general-purpose forces, I mean, Gorman was there for a while—sensible thing—the current guy— But I’m not close  enough to that set of organizations anymore to judge.But it certainly happened  very slowly.- Q1: But I mean from your perch at the NSC, when you were responsible for monitoring what was happening?

[翻譯]
在某些領域，更多的是人事問題，像是格什溫，或是一些在總合部隊擔任國家情報官的人，我是說，戈爾曼曾經在那裡待了一段時間，這是明智的做法，目前的那個人，但我已經不再緊密地與這些組織接觸了，無法評判。但這肯定是緩慢地發生的。問題1：但是從你在國家安全委員會的立場來看，你負責監測正在發生的事情，是這樣嗎？

--- 段落 442 (449 字元) ---
- Marshall: Oh, well, then, not very much happened at all.I mean it went very, very  slowly.I mean because Helms was being asked to take on responsibilities that he  didn’t really want.Set up new organizations like the IC staff.But it all went very  slowly, very slowly.And, as I say, two years later, which was essentially when I left,  not a lot had happened, I would say.- Q1: This was very helpful.- Marshall: Well, we can have further sessions.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：哦，那麼，其實沒有發生太多事情。我的意思是進展非常緩慢。因為海姆斯被要求承擔他其實不想要的職責。建立新組織，比如情報社員組。但一切進展得非常緩慢，非常緩慢。正如我所說的，兩年後，也就是我離開的時候，我想說並沒有太多事情發生。
- Q1：這很有幫助。
- 馬歇爾：好的，我們可以進一步討論。

--- 段落 443 (13 字元) ---
### 1969–1973

[翻譯]
1969年至1973年

### The Apollo Program was a series of manned missions to the moon conducted by the United States from 1969 to 1972. The program culminated in the successful landing of Apollo 11 on the moon on July 20, 1969. This was followed by several more missions, with Apollo 17 being the final mission to the moon in December 1972. Overall, the Apollo Program involved a total of 17 missions, with 12 astronauts setting foot on the moon.

阿波羅計劃是美國於1969年至1972年進行的一系列有人登月任務。該計劃在1969年7月20日取得成功，成功地將阿波羅11號著陸在月球上。此後還有幾次更多的任務，其中阿波羅17號是在1972年12月進行的最後一次登月任務。總體而言，阿波羅計劃共涉及17次任務，有12名宇航員登陸月球。

--- 段落 444 (425 字元) ---
- Q1: So you joined the NSC full time in 1972 as head of the Net Assessment Group?- Marshall: ‘Course, I mean, initially it was just me.And then Carol Doheny.And then  I recruited Chip Pickett, who must have come in the summer [July ‘72], and then a  few months later, Robin Pirie.And then we had this other–Then Carol had gotten  Jo Hunerwadel assigned.But she was someone who came on as one of the  regular NSC secretaries.

[翻譯]
問1：您在1972年全職加入NSC，擔任網絡評估小組主任嗎？- 馬歇爾：當然，最初只有我。然後是卡羅爾·多尼。然後我招募了奇普·皮克特，他應該在夏季[1972年7月]進來，然後幾個月後，羅賓·皮里。然後我們有另外一個...之後卡羅爾讓喬·胡納韋德被分配過來。但她是作為一位常規NSC秘書加入的。

--- 段落 445 (339 字元) ---
Then when Carol left, then she moved up to be the senior  secretary and we got this other secretary, Lexi Crow.And the five of us moved  over here.Let me say that one of the things that happened was that when I got the position  as head of the NSC Net Assessment Group, a number of people came around to  talk to me.Kind of give me advice.

[翻譯]
然後當卡羅離開後，她升任資深秘書，我們得到了另一位秘書，莉克西·克羅。我們五個人搬到這裡來。讓我說一件事情，當我擔任NSC網路評估組的負責人時，有許多人來找我談話，給我建議。

--- 段落 446 (367 字元) ---
One of the most interesting was General Polk,  and I mentioned some other things about his insight from his own time as the  commander of the ground forces in Europe.His approach was driven by the fact  that he thought it was very important to know how effective these other forces  really were, something about their typical mistakes or failings, and so on, and etc.

[翻譯]
其中最有趣的是波爾克將軍，我提到了他自己擔任歐洲地面部隊指揮官時的一些見解。他的方法是基於他認為了解這些其他部隊的實際效力非常重要，一些有關他們典型的錯誤或失敗的事情等等。

--- 段落 447 (455 字元) ---
And I guess the things I remember the most him talking about were these stories  that he got, and were indicative of the difficulties they had in movement—When  a unit was going to move from one place to the other, they would send out ahead  of them people that were almost the equivalent of traffic directors to make sure  they make the right turn at that crossroad, this crossroad.And then episodes of  them still getting lost, or making the wrong turn.

[翻譯]
我記得他談論最多的事情，是那些描述他們在移動中遇到困難的故事。當一個部隊要從一個地方移動到另一個地方時，他們會派出提前人員，他們幾乎相當於交通指揮員，以確保他們在十字路口和這個十字路口轉彎時走對路。然後離群索居或轉錯路的情況。

--- 段落 448 (458 字元) ---
These were all kind of indicators  to him of particular failings, problems that they were having.His point was that,  here he was, he was the commander of the American ground forces, and when  he asked his—down through his intelligence organizations, to tell him about  how good the opposing forces were, I mean qualitatively and so on, he was very  dissatisfied with what he got back.And that’s why he undertook this personal effort to find out for himself.

[翻譯]
這些都是對他某些失敗、問題的指示。他的觀點是，當他是美國陸地部隊的指揮官時，當他向情報組織詢問對手部隊的實力和質量時，他並不滿意所得到的回答。這就是為什麼他自己親自努力去尋找答案的原因。

--- 段落 449 (471 字元) ---
And I forget whether it was he or George Blanchard [a  subsequent commander of the American ground forces] telling me later of things  they thought about, planned to impress the Russian commander.Efforts were  made to invite the counterpart commander to come over and then to either in a  seemingly casual way or in a kind of staged way to kind of do things that would  impress him, like the speed at which certain kinds of actions could be taken and  executed and so on.

[翻譯]
我忘記是他還是喬治·布蘭查德（後來的美國地面部隊指揮官）告訴我後來他們考慮過的事情，計劃要給俄羅斯指揮官留下深刻印象。他們努力邀請對應的指揮官過來，然後以看似隨意的方式或某種安排好的方式做一些會令他印象深刻的事情，比如特定行動的速度和執行等等。

--- 段落 450 (285 字元) ---
I don’t remember specifically who [other than General] Polk came by to see me].But I was struck by the fact that all of a sudden there were a bunch of people  coming by to see me.- Q1: Could you talk about the review of combat models you did as part of the net  assessment work at NSC?

[翻譯]
我不記得具體是誰（除了波爾克將軍）來找我。但一件事讓我印象深刻，就是突然間有一大群人來找我。問題1：您能談談您在國安委員會做綜合評估工作時進行的戰鬥模型審查嗎？

--- 段落 451 (382 字元) ---
- Marshall: What I looked at was—To look at combat models—Well, I thought that  given what the fundamental task was, I wanted to see whether the models of  combat, and you know, at the, I suppose, division and above level, not very micro  combat, what the state of affairs was.Were they adequate?Would they reflect all of the factors that really ought to go into such an assessment?

[翻譯]
Marshall: 我所看的是 - 為了觀察戰鬥模型 - 嗯，我認為考慮到基本任務是什麼，我想要看看戰鬥模型是否足夠，你知道，大概在師級以上，不是非常微觀的戰鬥，局勢如何？它們是否足夠？是否反映了應該納入評估的所有因素？

--- 段落 452 (493 字元) ---
And so, I guess I  got briefed on the state of modeling and the existing models and fairly—First, I  more or less decided on my own, but I consulted with a number of people as to  their appraisal, and would the things really deal with the full range of factors that  ought to be taken into account, and decided that they weren’t going to be able  to.That, in particular, they didn’t take into account these kinds of levels of training,  morale, leadership, any of the more qualitative factors.

[翻譯]
因此，我猜我對建模的狀況和現有的模型有了初步了解。首先，我基本上是自己做出了決定，但我也諮詢了一些人對他們的評估，這些事情是否真的考慮了應該考慮的全部因素，最終我決定這些模型無法應對。特別是，它們沒有考慮到這些培訓水平、士氣、領導力等更具質量的因素。

--- 段落 453 (366 字元) ---
I remember talking with  General Polk about the state of the models.- Q1: You also conducted several intelligence case studies?- Marshall: The idea was—You know, it was one of the general tasks of this new NSC  Intelligence Committee to do these appraisals of the performance of the intelligence community.And we had started out with the performance in these crises.

[翻譯]
我記得和波克將軍談論模型的狀況。問題1：您也進行了幾個情報案例研究嗎？- 馬歇爾：這個想法是——您知道，這個新國家安全委員會情報委員會的一項主要任務是對情報界的表現進行評估。我們從這些危機中的表現開始著手。

--- 段落 454 (380 字元) ---
The studies of crises would have been done from…Beginning spring or summer  of ‘72 and done into the early part of ‘73—I mean the ones we had planned.The attempted overthrow of King Hussein and outside intervention in that crisis  was one of the case studies.The 1971 Indo-Pak war was another one.The other  case that I remember that we looked at was this…I forget the name of it.

[翻譯]
危機研究將會從...從1972年春季或夏季開始，一直進行到1973年初 - 我的意思是我們計劃好的那些。企圖推翻侯賽因國王和外部干預這場危機是其中一個案例。1971年印巴戰爭是另一個案例。我記得我們看過的另一個案例是......我忘記它的名字了。

--- 段落 455 (498 字元) ---
But  there was this period when there was this canal zone area in which the Egyptians  were supposedly not to—That the demilitarized strip, I guess, on the other side of  the canal—And they were not supposed to move into this area.But they began  surreptitiously to do so.And the issue was how well American intelligence was  able to monitor that—as I remember that.You ought to talk with Chip about  that, but I think…But I don’t remember NSSM 69 as being something that we  were that involved in.

[翻譯]
但是有一段時間，埃及有一個運河區域，據說埃及人不應該進入-我想是運河另一邊的非軍事化區域-他們不應該進入這個區域。但他們卻偷偷地這麼做了。問題是美國情報部門能否監控得宜-就我所記得的。你應該和Chip談談這個問題，但我記不得NSSM 69是我們參與的事情。

--- 段落 456 (456 字元) ---
But there was a phrase for this encroachment back into this  demilitarized zone.I don’t remember the specific insights from the case studies.But the things led  to a certain number of proposals of things that ought to be done in order to  do better in the future and so on.But as to the major insights, I guess that I felt  that what came out of it was this thing you mentioned [that the analysts did not  have the same perspective as Nixon and Kissinger].

[翻譯]
但對於重新侵犯這個非軍事區域的行為，有一個詞語。我不記得案例研究中的具體見解。但這些事情導致了一些提議，應該做一些事情以便在未來做得更好等等。但就主要看法來說，我想我覺得從中得出的是你提到的這件事情【分析師與尼克森和基辛格沒有相同的觀點】。

--- 段落 457 (362 字元) ---
But also how difficult it was  to get the intelligence community people to really do objective assessments of  their own performance.The first draft almost uniformly came back, Given all the  circumstances, we did well, even if it was manifest that they hadn’t done very well.They always had some out; you know, the circumstances prevented them from  doing well.

[翻譯]
但同時，讓情報界人員真正客觀評估自己的表現有多困難。第一份草稿幾乎普遍回來說，考慮到所有情況，我們表現不錯，即使顯然他們的表現並不是很好。他們總是有著藉口；你知道，情況使他們無法表現得好。

--- 段落 458 (485 字元) ---
So we usually had to go through two or three drafts before you could  finally get them to be a bit more objective and really do an appraisal from which  there would be some admission that this or that didn’t go so well and maybe  something that could be done about it.- Q1: You commented in the past that the post-mortems found a lack of objectivity  by the staff drawn from operating organizations; perishable data; lack of access to  top officials; sensitivity of certain activities.

[翻譯]
因此，通常我們必須經過兩三次草稿才能最終讓他們更客觀，並真正做出一個評估，從中會有一些承認這一點或那一點沒有做得那麼好，也許有些事情可以做出改進。Q1：您過去曾評論過，事後檢討發現運營組織的工作人員缺乏客觀性；易腐敗數據；無法接觸高級官員；某些活動的敏感性。

--- 段落 459 (366 字元) ---
- Marshall: Yeah, I think there was a memo around here, there was probably something written toward the very end of—You know, what did we learn from this  whole thing and so on.- Q1: And the case studies were followed by the study of intelligence in the 1973  Arab-Israeli War?- Marshall: And then along came this other event in ‘73, that we then took advantage  of.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：對，我想這裡應該有一份備忘錄，可能是在整個事情結束時留下的一些文字—你知道，我們從這個整個事件中學到了什麼之類的。 
- Q1：這些案例研究後，接著是對1973年阿拉伯以色列戰爭情報的研究嗎？ 
- 馬歇爾：然後在1973年出現了另一個事件，我們更進一步利用了這個機會。

--- 段落 460 (399 字元) ---
And we did the Arab-Israeli War study because one of the difficulties that we’d  found in doing the earlier assessments was that you often couldn’t really find out  which intelligence document or bits of things had actually reached particular  people, whether they had read them or not, and so on.So this was an attempt to  have a better feel for what materials actually reached the relevant people.

[翻譯]
我們進行阿拉伯以色列戰爭的研究，是因為我們發現在做早期評估時所遇到的一個困難是，往往無法確切得知哪些情報文件或訊息碎片實際上達到了特定的人，他們是否閱讀了這些資料等等。因此，這是為了更好地了解哪些資料實際上達到了相關的人的一個嘗試。

--- 段落 461 (448 字元) ---
And  then also to interview them while the thing’s going on as to how useful and so on  the stuff was.The study was done almost in real time.Talk more with Chip Pickett.And actually, you see, Chip stayed on after the rest of the group came over here,  because our movement over here was not too much afterwards.And he stayed  on to finish the report and then came over.So he was a lot more involved.He’d be  the better person to talk to about that.

[翻譯]
然後也要在做這件事情的同時訪問他們，了解這些東西有多有用等等。這項研究幾乎是實時進行的。與Chip Pickett深入交談。事實上，你看，Chip在其他團員過來這裡後留了下來，因為我們過來這裡的運動之後不久。他留下來完成報告然後過來。所以他參與得更深。他是更合適的人選來談論這個。

--- 段落 462 (390 字元) ---
But at any rate, so we’d been looking at one aspect of the performance of the  community, and I think at some meeting of the second level of this thing, the  working group [of the NSCIC], discussed, Well, what other areas could we look at.And one area was the quality of political and economic intelligence.And then the  question was, OK, we need to pick a country or some place to look at.

[翻譯]
但無論如何，我們一直在研究社區的表現方面，我想在這個事情的第二層次會議上，NSCIC的工作小組討論了，好吧，我們可以再研究哪些領域。其中一個領域是政治和經濟情報的質量。然後問題出來了，好的，我們需要選擇一個國家或某個地方進行研究。

--- 段落 463 (465 字元) ---
And then  several proposals were made and Yugoslavia was picked, because at the time,  even though it didn’t happen until much later, again there was some speculation  that Tito—I forget whether it was his health or what it was—but he might leave  soon.And so, it was a kind of case of, or a situation in which you would like to  have good information about these things.So, we then undertook this effort and, I guess as I remember it, we collected all this  stuff.

[翻譯]
然後提出了幾個提案，最終選擇了南斯拉夫，因為當時，儘管直到後來才發生，人們又有一些猜測認為，可能是提特（Tito）的健康狀況或其他原因，但他可能會很快離開。因此，這是一種情況，或者說是一種情況，您希望對這些事情有良好的信息。因此，我們開始了這一努力，我想我記得，我們收集了所有這些資料。

--- 段落 464 (437 字元) ---
You know, recent intelligence or probably from the prior couple of years or  so.And the materials, both various studies, or major papers, as well as current intelligence…We went and tried to understand, “Who were the people who prepared  this?” particularly at CIA, and some of their characteristics, I mean, did they really  know anything about Yugoslavia.I mean, what was the basis of their knowledge.- Q1: What yardsticks did you use?

[翻譯]
你知道的，最近的情報可能來自前幾年。還有相關研究、重要文件和最新的情報...我們試著理解“是誰準備了這些資料？”，特別是在中央情報局，以及一些他們的特點，我是說，他們真的了解南斯拉夫嗎？他們的知識基礎是什麼？- 問題1：你們使用了哪些標準？

--- 段落 465 (157 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, whether they had previous experience, had ever lived in the country,  knew any of the languages, you know.But we had this body of material.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：那麼，無論他們是否有先前的經驗，是否曾在該國生活過，是否懂得任何語言，你知道。但我們擁有這些資料。

--- 段落 466 (465 字元) ---
And then  we had some people from the outside—and I forget who they all were, except for  a couple of them that I—although they weren’t the only ones—For the economics stuff, the one person I remember involving was Joe Kirchheimer, who was a  friend of mine and secondly, a partner in Burnham & Company on Wall Street, had  been in the CIA in the ‘50s, had been in military intelligence in the war.- Q1: In other words, he was very qualified.- Marshall: Yes, right.

[翻譯]
然後我們有一些外部人士，我忘記他們都是誰，除了我記得其中幾個，雖然他們不是唯一的幾個。在經濟方面，我記得參與的一個人是我的朋友約瑟·基爾希默，他是華爾街Burnham＆Company的合夥人，在50年代曾在中央情報局工作，也曾在戰爭中擔任軍事情報工作。換句話說，他非常有資格。-問題1: 是的，對。

--- 段落 467 (454 字元) ---
He was one of the people we had look at the—But he wasn’t  the only one.There were two or three other people.We had a little panel of two  or three people for each, separately, for the economics and the political.And on  the political side, I remember that one of the people was Nathan Leites.But I can’t  quite remember who the other people were.And, in essence, we got pretty negative reviews from the panel after reading all  this stuff.In both cases.

[翻譯]
他是我們找來的人之一，但他並不是唯一的一個。還有兩三個其他人。對於經濟和政治，我們每個方面都有一個由兩至三人組成的小組。在政治方面，我記得其中一個人是Nathan Leites。但我不太記得其他人是誰。總的來說，在閱讀了所有這些東西後，我們從小組那裡得到了相當負面的評論。在兩個案例中都是這樣。

--- 段落 468 (473 字元) ---
In the case of the economic material…just thought that  there was better material that could be available to people in the government  from the banks on Wall Street, is the most particular thing I meant, but there were  undoubtedly other sources.And then for the political analysis, it was just felt that  there was very good reporting in Swiss and German newspapers, and just translating the articles from the better newspapers would be a lot better than the stuff  there.

[翻譯]
在經濟材料的情況下...只是覺得政府官員可以從華爾街的銀行獲得更好的材料，這就是我所意指的最具體的事情，但無疑還有其他來源。然後對於政治分析，只是感覺瑞士和德國報紙有很好的報導，只需翻譯來自更好報紙的文章會比那些材料好得多。

--- 段落 469 (415 字元) ---
Now, of course, there would be a tiny bit of material based on some special  intelligence, say, that the newspapers wouldn’t necessarily have.But it would  be—The bulk of what these people tried to write about was done far better by  people out in the real world.- Q1: And these outside sources had been ignored, neglected by the intelligence  community?- Marshall: Well, probably.Yeah, I doubt that they read them.

[翻譯]
現在，當然，會有一點點基於某些特殊情報的材料，比如報紙可能沒有的。但主要的部分是這些人試圖寫的，實際上在現實世界裡由其他人做得更好。- Q1：這些外部來源被情報部門忽略，忽視了嗎？- 馬歇爾：很可能。是的，我懷疑他們沒有讀這些。

--- 段落 470 (321 字元) ---
Well, in the first place, again, Yugoslavia—Well, it turned out that the people who  did this were part of the current intelligence people at CIA.Again, I think the  reporting from the clandestine service people at the embassy and so on would  have not had some of these difficulties.But these panels didn’t look at that.

[翻譯]
首先，關於南斯拉夫，結果證明進行這項活動的人員是中央情報局當前的情報人員。我認為，來自大使館的秘密服務人員的報告可能不會遇到這些困難。但是這些委員會並未考慮這一點。

--- 段落 471 (446 字元) ---
They  looked at the part that came out of the so-called intelligence analysis…But that  was done by people in the current intelligence part of CIA, and there, particularly  for countries like Yugoslavia, it was treated like almost a newspaper.There was the  Yugoslavian desk, and there would be two or three people on it.But they moved  from that to other jobs, or from other jobs to that.But they had no prior experience dealing with Yugoslavia.

[翻譯]
他們看了所謂的情報分析中出現的部分...但那是由CIA當前情報部門的人員完成的，尤其是對於像南斯拉夫這樣的國家，這些分析幾乎就像是報紙一樣。有南斯拉夫辦公桌，辦公桌上可能有兩三個人。但他們從那轉移到其他工作，或從其他工作轉移到那裡。但他們沒有任何處理南斯拉夫問題的先驗經驗。

--- 段落 472 (396 字元) ---
They only tended to—At the moment we wrote the  report, the years of even being on that desk, the average for the three people was  a year and a half.So they weren’t there long enough to get great know-how.They  probably didn’t read German.So sending them to German and Swiss newspapers  was not going to help unless there were some readily available translations.They  didn’t know the languages.

[翻譯]
他們只是傾向於-在我們撰寫報告的當下，三個人在那個崗位上的平均是一年半，所以他們還沒有足夠的時間去累積豐富的專業知識。他們可能不懂德語。因此，將他們派到德國和瑞士的報紙也無濟於事，除非有現成的翻譯版本。他們不懂這些語言。

--- 段落 473 (488 字元) ---
And it was again an insight to me that—And we talked to one of the people on  the NSC, who actually was the recipient of this stuff, the intelligence stuff, who  had twice served in Yugoslavia, in the embassy, and so he had about nine years  or so of on-the-spot experience in Yugoslavia.So it was an example to me of how  wrong—There was this book called Organizational Intelligence or something, I  forget the name of the author now.- Q1: Wilensky?- Marshall: Yeah, some name like that.

[翻譯]
這對我來說又是一個領悟——我們和國家安全委員會的一名成員交談過，實際上他是這些情報資料的接收者，曾在領館兩次在南斯拉夫服役，所以他在南斯拉夫有大約九年的實地經驗。這對我來說是一個例子，說明了我們多麼錯誤——有一本書叫做《組織情報》之類的，作者的名字我現在忘了。- Q1: 威倫斯基嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的，類似那樣的名字。

--- 段落 474 (460 字元) ---
But the point is—Walinsky or Wilensky—89 See  the people…The kind of academic theorists sort of treat the world as being that  there are these people, the real experts, and things are filtered up to other people  who are not really in touch with the real world and also don’t know very much  about it.And that the problem in organizations is that the people who really know  certain kinds of things, some part of it gets filtered out as it moves up to the top.

[翻譯]
但重點是 - Walinsky或Wilensky - 看到人們...這種學術理論家將世界看作是這樣的，那些真正的專家，事情被過濾給其他人，這些人與真實世界不太接觸，也對它沒有太多了解。組織中的問題是，真正了解某些事物的人，部分內容在傳遞到最高層時會被過濾掉。

--- 段落 475 (349 字元) ---
Here you had this case of the people down below just don’t know very much,  don’t have much interpretive skill, sending stuff up to, in this case, someone who actually had a good deal of experience and knew more about the country than  they did.And it’s the product of the personnel systems in the intelligence community for these smaller countries.

[翻譯]
這裡有一個案例，下面的人們並不了解很多，也沒有很強的解釋能力，他們將情報發送給一個實際上有相當經驗且比他們更了解該國的人。這是情報圈子中較小國家的人員系統的產物。

--- 段落 476 (476 字元) ---
I mean in the case of—If you have other kinds  of situations, where people can specialize for a long time, as in the case of Russia  and so on, it’s not as big a contrast.- Q1: Back on the Yugoslavia review.When was that done roughly?- Marshall: I think that was probably done in the spring of ‘73, would be my guess.- Q1: What impact do you think these different studies had or how were they used?- Marshall: Well, you know, again, they were sent out from this NSC committee.

[翻譯]
我的意思是，在某些情況下─如果存在其他類型的情況，人們可以長時間專門從事，就像俄羅斯等國家一樣，這並沒有那麼大的對比。─問題1：回顧南斯拉夫時，大致是什麼時候進行的？─馬歇爾：我想那個大概是在1973年春天進行的。這只是我的猜測。─問題1：您認為這些不同的研究有什麼影響或者它們如何使用？─馬歇爾：嗯，你知道，再說一次，這些都是由這個國家安全委員會委託發出的。

--- 段落 477 (465 字元) ---
First,  to the members on the committee itself, because they were done by the working  group.So all the major organizations were represented there…Well, I guess not  all, because I guess NSA wasn’t on it or so on.But then it went out.But you know,  again, it’s just another report and I don’t think very much happened as a result of  that.But Chip would be good on this, I mean he was the main collaborator…  
- Q1: On all of these studies, rather than Robin Pirie?

[翻譯]
首先，對於委員會內部的成員來說，因為是由工作組完成的。因此，所有主要組織都在其中代表……嗯，我猜不是所有組織，因為我猜 NSA 不在其中，或者其他組織也不在。但後來它被公布出來了。但是你知道，再說一次，這只是另一份報告，我認為並沒有太多事情發生作為結果。但是 Chip 在這方面很擅長，我的意思是他是主要的合作者…
- Q1：在所有這些研究中，而不是 Robin Pirie？

--- 段落 478 (353 字元) ---
- Marshall: Oh yeah, Robin was off…We were trying to get the net assessment part  of it going.- Q1: In your notes, you wrote: “History: — HAK • GPF [general-purpose forces] backup plan, leads to CIA work.”  
- Marshall: Well, I would guess—There had been this work that was done for Kissinger  in the summer of ‘70, you know, the initial net assessment.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：噢是的，羅賓離開了…我們試圖讓評估網絡的部分進行。
- Q1：在你的筆記中，你寫道：“歷史：- HAK • GPF [一般用途部隊]應急計劃，導致中央情報局的工作。”
- 馬歇爾：我想…基辛格在1970年夏天曾為此進行過工作，你知道，最初的網絡評估。

--- 段落 479 (496 字元) ---
And the whole motive  that he had was that he wanted this study done in order to have some things in  his hip pocket, so to speak, of programs that could be either augmented or so on,  etc., that would be worthwhile, if things did not go well with the Soviets and new  monies were available and…  So part of the background was that, OK, if you’re going to have these—This idea  that if things go badly you’re going to start some new things, they might as well  be things that would be impressive.

[翻譯]
他的整個動機是希望這項研究能夠有所準備，以便在蘇聯方面出現不利情況並有新的資金可用時，能夠進行一些相應的計劃。因此，背景的一部分是，如果情況惡化，將開展一些新的事物，最好是一些具有印象力的事物。

--- 段落 480 (384 字元) ---
- Q1: Now is this if things went badly in SALT or just a general deterioration in our  relations with…?- Marshall: I forget now what was worrying Kissinger.I suppose it was SALT or just  general behavior that kind of things…  
- Q1: There was a stalemate in the SALT talks around the time you started work on the  net assessment study and also there were the crises discussed earlier.

[翻譯]
問題1：這是因為SALT出了問題還是我們與某些關係普遍惡化了...？- 馬歇爾：我忘了基辛格當時擔心的是什麼。我想可能是SALT或者一般的行為那種事情...
問題1：在你開始進行網絡評估研究時，SALT談判陷入僵局，同時前面討論過的危機也在發生。

--- 段落 481 (454 字元) ---
- Marshall: But in any case, I had had this—From the beginning on this idea of the  net assessments—That is, that clearly one of the ways…One of our goals was  deterring the Soviets from various kinds of actions, encroachments, and so on.And that it would be important to understand, what did they pay attention to,  where did they give us good marks, where did they not give us good marks.And  so, once I had joined Kissinger, I thought more about that.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：但無論如何，從一開始我就有這個想法，即網絡評估——顯然，其中一種方式…我們的目標之一是遏止蘇聯進行各種行動、侵犯等等。了解他們關注的事項、給我們哪些好評、哪些不給好評是非常重要的。所以，一旦我加入基辛格，我就更多地思考這個問題。

--- 段落 482 (455 字元) ---
And then asked that  this study be done to make an attempt to answer those kinds of questions.- Q1: And what were the findings?I know it [the study] was completed after you  moved to the Pentagon.- Marshall: Well, as I remember it, I think there were a couple of reports that came  out…Again, I remember that there were some things that came out…There  certainly was some insights as to what it was they seemed particularly to pay  attention to and so on.

[翻譯]
然後要求進行這研究，試圖回答這些問題。問題1：結果是什麼？我知道這個研究是在你搬到五角大廈後完成的。馬歇爾：我記得，我想當時有幾份報告出來了...我記得當時有一些東西出來...他們似乎特別關注的事情也有一些啟示。

--- 段落 483 (492 字元) ---
But I don’t remember the details of the thing.But as I  remember, I thought the things were OK, and yet they were seen as difficult to  do, and the guy who did them I think moved on to something else, and they were  never kind of continued.- Q1: But there was just one person working on them?- Marshall: Yeah, right.90  
- Q1: Do you remember why Kissinger wanted the study of the Chinese ballistic  missile program done?- Marshall: No.In fact, it had been ordered before I had come on board.

[翻譯]
但是我不記得這件事的細節。但據我記得，我認為這些事情是可以搞定的，但被視為難以做到，而做這些事情的那個人我想轉而從事其他事情了，所以這些事情也沒有持續下去。- Q1：但是只有一個人在做這些事情嗎？- 馬歇爾：對。- Q1：你記得為什麼基辛格希望進行中國彈道導彈計劃的研究嗎？- 馬歇爾：不記得。實際上，這個命令在我上任之前就已經下達了。

--- 段落 484 (330 字元) ---
But it was one  of the first things that came in, when I came on board in early January of ‘72.And it  was one of the things that I was asked to evaluate.Well, also it was a special study  that had been asked for by him.And I don’t remember what triggered it.I remember reviewing it and sending up an appraisal of it to Kissinger.

[翻譯]
當我在1972年初加入時，這是其中一件最早出現的事情之一。這也是我被要求評估的事情之一。同時，這也是他要求進行的特別研究之一。我不記得是什麼觸發了這個研究。我記得審查了它並向基辛格提交了一份評估。

--- 段落 485 (489 字元) ---
And then…The thing  that was so ironic about it was that, here in this study they, in effect, say that they  haven’t deployed the missiles yet…At that time they believed that the Chinese  hadn’t deployed any missiles [MRBMs, IRBMs or ICBMs].That they hadn’t been  deployed, and went into a long story about why they were so sure in saying, we  would have seen this, we would have seen that.And all based on the assumption  that they would proceed very much the way we and the Russians had.

[翻譯]
然後...最具諷刺意味的是，在這個研究中，他們實際上表示他們還沒有部署導彈...當時他們相信中國尚未部署任何導彈[中程彈道飛彈、中程射程彈道飛彈或洲際彈道飛彈]。他們還講述了一個關於為什麼如此確定他們尚未被部署的長篇故事，並且認為我們會看到這個，我們會看到那個。所有這些都是建立在他們會以我們和俄羅斯人相同的方式進行的假設上。

--- 段落 486 (422 字元) ---
And then a  relatively few months—within six months, I think—they had to come in and say,  “Whoops, we now know they’ve been deployed more than that.They have been  deployed since about 1965.Now that we see what they’re doing” and so on, etc.- Q1: This is because they’re road-mobile missiles and they’re dispersed?- Marshall: Well, they’re different in their—Right—and they’re hidden in a variety  of ways and so on, etc.

[翻譯]
