然後在相對較短的幾個月之內，我認為在六個月內，他們不得不進來說：“哎呀，我們現在知道它們已經部署了更長時間。它們自1965年左右就開始投入使用。現在我們看到它們做了什麼”等等。問題1：這是因為它們是路移式導彈，且被分散部署嗎？- 馬歇爾：嗯，它們在不同方面是不同的-對，它們是以各種方式隱藏的等等。

--- 段落 487 (473 字元) ---
And obviously the Chinese had taken great care to be far  more deceptive about the whole business than either we or the Russians actually  had been.And, very likely, in my judgment, because they were actually apprehensive about the Russian reaction had it been detected.- Q1: Possible attack.- Marshall: Yeah.- Q1: But the problem, was it that the CIA was saying, “Well, here’s the setup of the  missile at the test site, and that we don’t see that duplicated in the field.

[翻譯]
顯然，中國人對整個情況比我們或俄羅斯人更加謹慎保密。在我看來，很可能是因為他們實際上對俄羅斯的反應感到擔憂，如果發現了這一行為。- Q1：可能的攻擊。- 馬歇爾：是的。- Q1：但問題是，是中央情報局在說：「在試驗場的飛彈設置方式，我們在現場看不到它的複製。

--- 段落 488 (423 字元) ---
And so,  therefore, it hasn’t been deployed?”  
- Marshall: Well, or that they’ve had certain kinds of tests, but, you know, that they  probably would deploy—We would see at the test site the kind of silos, the kind  of things that they would eventually deploy.And we don’t see that.We don’t see  any deployed systems that match anything.We don’t see anything that looks like  what we see at the test sites, and so on, etc.

[翻譯]
因此，它還沒有被部署嗎？
- 馬歇爾：嗯，或者他們進行過某些測試，但你知道，他們可能會部署一些——我們會在測試場地看到那種發射井、那種最終會被部署的東西。但我們沒有看到。我們沒有看到任何與之相符的部署系統。我們沒有看到任何看起來像我們在測試場地看到的東西，依此類推。

--- 段落 489 (166 字元) ---
- Q1: Do you remember if the misestimate of the size of the SS-19 ICBM occurred  during the May ‘72 Moscow summit?- Marshall: No, I don’t think it occurred during it.

[翻譯]
Q1：您是否記得SS-19洲際彈道飛彈尺寸的錯估發生在1972年5月的莫斯科峰會期間嗎？- 馬歇爾：不，我不認為它是在那時發生的。

--- 段落 490 (642 字元) ---
But it—The reason I remember it  was there was a strong reaction on Haig’s part, I think, because we were making,  in the negotiations, a big point of some particular measure of size, and if what this  new revelation meant, and everything, that this had been set—the size thing—  had been set based on our notions of the earlier estimate of the size, which was  smaller…And so, in effect, we either said, we were kind of complicating the negotiation by trying to force on them a size category which meant that the –19 would  be, in fact, a big missile, or you’re forcing them to lie and to… At any rate…  
- Q1: And Haig was upset about this?

[翻譯]
但我記得的原因是海格對此有強烈的反應，因為在談判中，我們對某個特定尺寸的重要性進行了強調，而這個新的揭示意味著，這件事情是基於我們對之前尺寸估計的概念來設立的，而該估計是較小的... 因此，事實上，我們要麼說，我們試圖在談判中強行將一個尺寸類別強加給他們，這意味著19號將事實上是一枚大導彈，要麼你們要逼他們說謊和... 無論如何... -問題1：海格為此感到不滿？

--- 段落 491 (307 字元) ---
- Marshall: Yes, right.- Q1: But the main point was that these were just examples of where the intelligence  community got things wrong?- Marshall: Yeah, right.- Q1: What were the general contents of the five-page handwritten letter you wrote  to Schlesinger when he became Director of Central Intelligence?

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾: 是的，沒錯。- Q1: 但主要問題在於，這些只是情報界失誤的案例嗎？- 馬歇爾: 是的，沒錯。- Q1: 當你寫了一封五頁手寫信給謝辛格成為中央情報局局長時，信的內容是什麼？

--- 段落 492 (461 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, the main thing I guess I recall about it was kind of saying to him—  ‘Course Schlesinger already, because of his previous position at OMB, where he’d  overseen a lot of—I mean the people who monitored intelligence were under  him and so on.And I, of course, had talked with him from time to time anyway  about it.But I guess the main thrust of the letter was to say to him, “Look, this is an  organization which isn’t as good as it used to be.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：嗯，我想我記得的主要事情是向他說的。當然，由於謝辛格先前在OMB的職位，他監督了許多情報監察人員等。我當然也時不時地和他談過這個問題。但我想信的主要目的是告訴他：“看，這個組織已經不像以前那樣好了。

--- 段落 493 (428 字元) ---
It has a lot of problems,” and try  to outline a number of problems based on the experience that I had had of the  inadequacies in the analysis area, its tendency to isolate itself from the outside  world in terms of very little lateral entry, all of that.I just kind of laid all that out for  him, as to the kind of place he was taking over and what seemed to be the kind of  major problems, the obstacles to change, and so on.

[翻譯]
它有很多問題，而根據我在分析領域中遇到的不足之處和其在與外界隔絕方面的傾向（即缺乏橫向進入），我試著概述一系列問題。我就把這些都向他說明了，關於他即將接手的地方的性質，以及似乎存在的主要問題、改變的障礙等等。

--- 段落 494 (434 字元) ---
- Q1: Even at the NSC, you were criticizing the intelligence community for its estimates of the Soviet defense burden.- Marshall: Yes.- Q1: And what do you remember about your work on that subject while you were at  the NSC?- Marshall: Well, it was…I mean I didn’t do very much about it there, as compared  with later, when I came here.But I had had doubts about it back at RAND.In fact,  Schlesinger and I had talked some about that.

[翻譯]
Q1：即使在國家安全委員會，你也批評情報界對蘇聯國防負擔的估計。- 馬歇爾：是的。- Q1：在你在國家安全委員會期間對這個主題的工作，你還記得些什麼？- 馬歇爾：嗯，那個…我在那裡沒有做太多，與後來我來這裡時相比，但我在RAND時就對此懷疑過。事實上，施萊辛格和我曾經談論過這個問題。

--- 段落 495 (315 字元) ---
And we also talked about it when  we did that net assessment for Kissinger in the summer of ‘70, or probably early  fall.And it just was unbelievable that they could produce the size of military  effort, be modernizing at the kind of pace they seemed to be, all on six percent  of a GNP which was smaller than ours.

[翻譯]
當我們在1970年夏季，或者可能是初秋為基辛格做網絡評估時，我們也談到了這個問題。他們憑著不到我們國家總生產的6%的GNP，就能夠產生如此規模的軍事努力，並且以他們看似的速度進行現代化，這簡直是不可思議的。

--- 段落 496 (464 字元) ---
Again, it was based on the notion that it  was about half ours, for the moment, accepting that the GNP was about the size  that the CIA said it was, which would make it about half of the U.S.GNP.With only  six percent of that being allocated, which would be roughly the equivalent of three percent of our GNP, that they could produce this very large set of military  programs.So Schlesinger and I felt that there was something doubtful about that,  going way back.

[翻譯]
再次強調，這是基於一個觀念，即目前大約一半的 GNP 屬於我們，暫時接受 CIA 所說的 GNP 大小，這將使其大約是美國 GNP 的一半。只有其中的百分之六被分配出去，這大約相當於我們 GNP 的百分之三，他們可以推出這麼龐大的一系列軍事項目。所以 Schlesinger 和我認為這件事有些疑問，這已經追溯很久了。

--- 段落 497 (347 字元) ---
And nothing I learned made me feel any better about it.- Q1: But this wasn’t something that you studied, I mean a formal study or asking the  intelligence community to relook, look at it again at that time.- Marshall: No.That was done largely here, initially when Schlesinger came here and  we started pressing this as one of the issues with them.

[翻譯]
但我所學到的任何事情都沒有讓我對此感到更好。問題1：但這不是你所研究的事情，我的意思是一項正式的研究或要求情報界重新審視它，當時並不是這樣的。 - 馬歇爾：不是，當施萊辛格到達這裡，我們與他們一起一開始壓迫這個作為其中之一的問題。

--- 段落 498 (476 字元) ---
Which led to their relook  at it, and coming back to us in, I suppose, ‘74, with this special memorandum, it  wasn’t a regular report, it came back initially as just a memorandum to Schlesinger, that we’ve looked at it, and we think the errors, we still believe the number and  the errors would be very small on either side of it.Q1: You had thought that the 1966 paper on Problems of Estimating Military Power  might have been related to work for Fred Wikner.- Marshall: Yes.

[翻譯]
這導致他們重新審視此事，並在我們應該是在74年提出了這份特別的備忘錄，這不是一份常規報告，它最初只是一份提交給施萊辛格的備忘錄，其中提到我們已經檢查過，我們認為錯誤數量及錯誤在此之外可能都很小。Q1：您曾認為1966年關於估算軍事力量問題的文件可能與弗雷德·維克納的工作有關。- 馬歇爾：是的。

--- 段落 499 (483 字元) ---
- Q1: But really the other work that you did—and I’ll talk with him—  
- Marshall: Is later.- Q1: Much, much later.- Marshall: Well, so probably wasn’t, yeah.So, I suppose it must have just come out  of the, at one level, the work that I had been doing for a long time with Loftus,  although that had pretty much stopped at that point.Loftus and I put out some  final reports I think that we did together in ‘63.Then I went off to France.Didn’t return until February or March of ‘65.

[翻譯]
- Q1：但實際上，你做的另一項工作——我會跟他談談——  
- 馬歇爾：是稍後。- Q1：要過很長時間。- 馬歇爾：那麼，可能不是，對吧。所以，我想這可能是源於我與羅夫特長期合作的工作，盡管當時這項工作基本上已經停止了。我們在'63年一起完成了一些最終報告。然後我去了法國。直到1965年的二月或三月才回來。

--- 段落 500 (479 字元) ---
And one of the main things that I  wanted to pick up at that point was trying to apply whatever was known about  organizations, organizational behavior.Which interest, in a way, had started in  the work with Loftus, had started back in the late ‘50s.And we did spend a lot of  time, or I spent a lot of time, thinking about how to understand the Soviets from  that perspective.But exactly why that thing [Problems of Estimating Military Power]  looks the way it is, I don’t know.

[翻譯]
在那個時候，我想要學習的主要事情之一是試圖應用已知的組織和組織行為的知識。這種興趣在與洛夫特斯的合作中已經開始，而這是在50年代末開始的。我們花了很多時間，或者我個人花了很多時間，思考如何從這個角度了解蘇聯。但關於為什麼《評估軍事力量的問題》看起來是這個樣子，我並不清楚。

--- 段落 501 (466 字元) ---
Or why the topic is exactly what it is.- Q1: As Director of Strategic Studies at RAND, you were responsible for sort of  integrating the efforts related to strategic forces that were done in the different  departments at RAND?- Marshall: Yes.- Q1: So this was a new layer of management?- Marshall: Yes, it was a new thing that had come out of discussions that Schlesinger  and I had had with Rowen, which led to Rowen initially asking Schlesinger to  undertake this.

[翻譯]
為什麼這個主題正是它存在的原因。- Q1：作為蘭德公司戰略研究主任，您負責整合在蘭德公司不同部門進行的有關戰略力量的工作嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的。- Q1：這樣一來，這是一個新的管理層嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的，這是由施萊辛格和我與羅文討論後產生的新事物，這促使羅文最初要求施萊辛格進行這項工作。

--- 段落 502 (492 字元) ---
And he did that for, maybe realistically, for six months.He hadn’t  gotten very far along in it when the 1968 election came along, and then he came  back on some of the transition team things and then ended up going into the  government here.So Rowen asked me to take it on.That was in early ‘69, I think,  because initially, when Schlesinger came back here during the transition period,  it wasn’t known whether he’d come back.The expectation initially was that he  would probably come back.

[翻譯]
他實際上可能做了大約六個月。當1968年的選舉來臨時，他還沒有走得太遠，然後他參與了一些過渡階段的工作，最終進入了政府。所以羅文要我接手這份工作。我想那應該是在1969年初，因為起初，當施萊辛格在過渡期間回到這裡時，還不知道他是否會回來。最初的預期是他可能會回來。

--- 段落 503 (334 字元) ---
So he [Schlesinger] probably knew about the offer to be assistant director in the Bureau of the Budget and accepted it in, I don’t know,  middle of January, late January, and shortly afterwards Rowen asked me to take  on the thing.And so I looked at—I’m not sure exactly all of what Schlesinger had done, or I  don’t remember exactly.

[翻譯]
因此，他[施萊辛格]很可能知道被提名為預算局助理主任的邀請，並在一月中旬或晚些時候接受了該邀請。不久之後，羅文請我接手這件事。所以我看了一下 - 我不確定施萊辛格具體做了什麼，或者我記不清楚。

--- 段落 504 (461 字元) ---
But anyway, one of the things I did was to get a kind  of a readout of, Well, who is doing work at RAND, and charging it off against, or  claiming that he’s working on strategic nuclear forces?And it was a very motley  assortment, because there had been no overall real direction.And Schlesinger, I think, hadn’t gotten far enough along to really take hold of  this.And so I then started to think about, Well, what should a program in this area  really look at?

[翻譯]
然而，其中一件事是我瞭解到，有人在蘭德公司進行工作，並將其歸因於或聲稱他正從事戰略核力量的工作？這一切都變得雜亂無章，因為沒有整體真正的方向。施萊辛格（Schlesinger）我認為還沒有足夠的進展來真正掌控這個問題。因此，我開始思考，在這個領域，一個真正的計劃應該看起來如何？

--- 段落 505 (366 字元) ---
What are the issues that you would want to have work being done  on?And so on, etc.And then it all kind of came out kind of naturally.And then I  had formed a small kind of discussion and planning group of not everyone who  claimed he was working in this area, but—and I even forget exactly who was on  it, but it was a small group of three or four people, probably.

[翻譯]
你希望進行哪些工作？等等。然後這一切都自然而然地發生了。後來，我組建了一個小型的討論和計劃小組，並非所有聲稱自己在這個領域工作的人都參與其中，但我甚至忘記了確切是誰參加了這個小組，可能是三到四個人。

--- 段落 506 (399 字元) ---
I had these ideas and  tried them out there, and then said, more or less said, Well, here’s the way I think  you really ought to look at this thing.Here’s a—In some sense we’ve been in this  kind of competition in this area for twenty years or more already and it’s going to  go on for a long time and we maybe need to look at it a different way and so on.And so it kind of led to that set of ideas.

[翻譯]
我有這些想法，試著在那裡實踐，然後說，或多或少地說，嗯，這裡是我認為你真的應該看待這件事的方式。在某種程度上，我們在這個領域已經進行了二十年或更長時間的競爭，這種競爭將持續很長時間，也許我們需要以不同的方式來看待它等等，所以它引出了這一套想法。

--- 段落 507 (445 字元) ---
And internally…I don’t know what the records show…My memory is that it…The  whole thing, at least in an early form, was written down by the end of the summer  of ‘69.And then I had this call from Kissinger’s office asking me to stop by, and I  was on my way to a vacation in France.And I stopped by in probably about the  third week of September and had a session with Kissinger and then went on my  way and was gone about a month and came back.

[翻譯]
在內部...我不知道記錄顯示的是什麼...依據我的記憶...整個事情，至少在早期形式下，是在1969年夏天結束時寫下的。然後我接到了基辛格辦公室的電話，要求我順道一下，我當時正在前往法國度假的途中。我在大約九月第三周順道拜訪了基辛格，然後繼續我的旅行，大約一個月後回來。

--- 段落 508 (475 字元) ---
And then when I came back I  continued to try to sort out things on this program, but I was also being badgered  by Kissinger to come back and get on with this study and so on, which I did in the  early part of December of ‘69.- Q1: Do you remember what kind of reaction you got from the Air Force, or from the  small group at RAND that you were meeting with?- Marshall: Well, they…I don’t know…The group at RAND, I mean the people I talked  to, thought that was interesting.

[翻譯]
後來我回來後，繼續嘗試解決這個計畫上的事情，但基辛格也一直在煩我回來繼續進行這項研究等等，這是在1969年12月初時進行的。Q1：您記得空軍或與您會面的蘭德小組對您有何反應嗎？- 馬歇爾：嗯，他們...我不知道...在蘭德的那群人，我指的是我談話的人，覺得這很有趣。

--- 段落 509 (477 字元) ---
But I think it was never particularly picked up or  taken anywhere at RAND.I got several letters and notes from people in the Air  Force who liked it, thought it was interesting.But that’s about it, as I remember.But, as I say, my memory is—  I don’t know whether anything shows up in that summer of ‘69.But essentially  it seems in my own mind a lot of it was done then, or the essence of it had been  worked out.91 But then I went away.Did some more probably when I got back.

[翻譯]
但我認為在蘭德公司這份文件從未特別引起注意或被帶出過。我收到了幾封來自空軍的人的信件和註解，他們喜歡它，認為它很有趣。但就我記得來說，就是這些了。但是，就像我說的，我的記憶或許有些模糊，我不知道69年夏天是否有出現什麼記錄。但基本上，在我自己心中，很多工作當時已經完成，或者至少已經找到了解決方法。但後來我離開了。回來後可能又做了一些工作。

--- 段落 510 (460 字元) ---
And there was also a lot of practical stuff of trying to get the monies allocated,  because I, in principle, now controlled the budget.“In principle,” I say, because  there was not a very effective apparatus for doing that.And then I went away.And then over ‘70, I mean I did the thing for Henry, the two reports, the last report  was finished very early in May.It was essentially the same time as the Cambodian enterprise was started.I then came back to RAND.

[翻譯]
而且還有很多實際的事情需要處理，因為從原則上來說，我現在控制預算。我說“從原則上來說”，因為實際上沒有一個很有效的機構來做這件事。然後我就離開了。之後在70年代，我做了亨利的事情，完成了兩份報告，最後一份報告在五月初完成。基本上是在柬埔寨活動開始的同一時間。然後我回到了 RAND。

--- 段落 511 (468 字元) ---
But then quite soon there was  this…Two things: one, there was the SS-9 study that he accepted, and I ran that,  coming back from time to time and doing it, and then this effort that started in  the summer of ‘70 on these standby programs and the net assessment.And then in December came this direction from Nixon to Henry and Shultz about  the reform of the intelligence community.And that started another cycle of my  commuting back and spending a lot of time there.

[翻譯]
但很快便出現了這樣的情況...有兩件事：一是他接受了SS-9研究，我負責管理這項工作，不時返回並進行，然後在1970年夏天開始的這個待命計劃和網絡評估。然後在十二月，尼克松向亨利和舒爾茨下達了關於情報社區改革的指示。這開始了我另一輪的通勤和花費大量時間在那裡。

--- 段落 512 (303 字元) ---
- Q1: So how much time did you really have to devote to shaping the interdepartmental research program on strategic studies?- Marshall: Well, I mean it was hard, given all of these other things, and probably, you  know—  
- Q1: How did you decide on the topic for the NSSM 186, the first net assessment?

[翻譯]
- Q1：你實際上為塑造跨部門戰略研究計劃花了多少時間？- Marshall：嗯，我是說這很困難，考慮到所有其他事情，也許你知道的——
- Q1：你是如何決定NSSM 186的主題，進行第一次淨評估的？

--- 段落 513 (475 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, we had had a long struggle to get the whole thing going, because  Laird kind of dragged his feet on it, I talked a lot to Buzhardt, and also Laird had as  a special assistant this guy who…I forget his name…Baroody…But I dealt mainly  with Buzhardt, but I had some meetings with Baroody.And both of them, I think, wanted to move ahead or be reasonable, but they—I  never really talked to Laird about it, but I mean he clearly resisted the idea of the  thing.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：嗯，我們為了讓整個事情進展艱難地奮鬥了很久，因為萊爾德在這件事上有些拖拖拉拉。我跟布茲哈特多說了一些話，而且萊爾德身邊有一個特別助手，那個人…我忘記他的名字了…巴魯迪…但我主要是與布茲哈特打交道，不過也有一些和巴魯迪見面的機會。我認為他們兩個都希望前進或者變得較為理性，不過他們…我從來沒有真正跟萊爾德討論過這個問題，但我知道他明顯地抗拒這個想法。

--- 段落 514 (407 字元) ---
So in the end, the way the things were going to be done was, while they  would be run from the NSC, the actual work would be farmed out to the most  relevant and interested party.We had a little working group…A guy named Al  Hall, who was here in the Pentagon…  
- Q1: He was like the Assistant Secretary for Intelligence.- Marshall: Yeah.And he also had been involved in this working group, for this NSCIC.

[翻譯]
所以最後，這些事情將要被執行的方式是，雖然它們將由國家安全委員會主導，實際的工作將被分派給最相關且感興趣的一方。我們有一個小工作小組...一個名叫艾爾·霍爾（Al Hall）的男士在五角大廈這裡... 
- Q1: 他就像情報部助理部長一樣。- 馬歇爾：是的。他也參與了這個國家安全委員會情報委員會的工作小組。

--- 段落 515 (496 字元) ---
So when we finally worked out a process that Defense would buy, then came the  question of picking a topic.And I’m not sure exactly why we picked the ground  forces.It may have been, Well, this is an area, let’s just start with it, and some  things probably favored it and so on.More work had been done looking at—not  real net assessments—but looking at the nuclear forces… So, anyway, that ended  up being picked as a reasonable one to start with, and see how this whole thing  was going to go.

[翻譯]
所以當我們終於找到國防部願意採購的流程時，接下來就是挑選一個主題的問題。我不確定我們為什麼挑選地面部隊。可能是因為這是一個領域，讓我們就從這裡開始吧，而且某些因素可能有利於它等等。之前也有更多人在研究 — 並不是真正的淨評估 — 但是會考慮核力量...總之，這最終被選定為一個合理的起點，看看整個事情會如何進行。

--- 段落 516 (396 字元) ---
But it was started very late.It was started probably just…at most six months  before I moved over here.- Q1: In fact, this NSSM 186 is dated 1 September 1973.- Marshall: Hmmm, yeah, right.So anyway, just a few months, right.But probably—It  had been so slow to have the whole thing come together that the people were  more or less in place, and a contract was put out to BDM to do a lot of stuff.

[翻譯]
但是這個計劃開始得很晚。大概就在我搬到這裡前，最多只有六個月時間。- Q1: 實際上，這個NSSM 186 的日期是1973年9月1日。- 馬歇爾：嗯，對。所以，大概就是幾個月的時間。但可能...整個計劃推進得很緩慢，人們或多或少已經到位，一份合同交給BDM公司進行許多工作。

--- 段落 517 (470 字元) ---
That’s  how Phil Karber and all these guys… They had an office down in the basement  someplace here and they got going.- Q1: Now did they do most of the work for the initial ground force net assessment?- Marshall: Well, a lot of it, yeah, right.- Q1: And then they continued after that?- Marshall: Yeah, right.That’s right, that contract.And I took that over and it became  a long-standing contract.- Q1: Do you know when you first started thinking about net assessment?

[翻譯]
這就是Phil Karber和這些人如何... 他們在地下室裡有一個辦公室，然後就開始了。- 問題1：那麼，他們是否為初期地面部隊網絡評估做了大部分工作？- 馬歇爾：嗯，很多，是的，是的。- 問題1：然後之後他們繼續做嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的，沒錯。是的，那份合同。我接手了，然後它變成了一個長期的合同。- 問題1：您知道您第一次開始考慮網絡評估是什麼時候嗎？

--- 段落 518 (463 字元) ---
- Marshall: I mainly wrote the 1970 net assessment, although Schlesinger spent a  little time on it.And there were people around—I mean, again, Charlie Herzfeld  was around, always pushing the idea of doing it.So I was thinking about it, and I’d  done that earlier paper on measuring military power, and so on.In a more systematic way, it would be for Wikner back in… [when Marshall wrote  his report on comparisons and R&D strategy, part of a larger RAND effort.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我主要撰寫了1970年的網路評估，雖然謝辛格也花了一點時間在這上面。周圍也有人——我的意思是，查理赫茲菲爾德總是在推動這個想法。所以我一直在考慮這個問題，我之前已經寫過有關衡量軍事力量的論文等等。更有系統性地，這是給Wikner回饋的…（當馬歇爾寫他有關比較和研發戰略的報告時，這是RAND的一部分努力中的一部分）。

--- 段落 519 (257 字元) ---
] And at  the time I did not particularly aspire to do that and so on.I thought it was interesting,  important, to try to have some way of measuring the comparative capabilities, and I  clearly didn’t think most of these simplified approaches did very much.

[翻譯]
在那個時候，我並沒有特別渴望這樣做等等。我認為嘗試找到某種方式來衡量相對能力是有趣且重要的，我明顯地認為大多數簡化的方法並不能做出多少貢獻。

--- 段落 520 (376 字元) ---
And I guess  I had—A lot of my interest in it grew out of this interest in the Soviet Union, but  in this organizational assessment, I mean of how much of both what people did,  how effective they were, depended on these organizational matters.But I hadn’t  any, did not envisage, or I wasn’t particularly pushing the idea of setting up an office to do these things and so on.

[翻譯]
我想我對這個的興趣主要源自對蘇聯的興趣，但在這種組織評估中，我意味著人們所做的事情，以及他們的效率有多少取決於這些組織問題。但我並不打算、也沒有預見，或者並沒有特別提出建立一個辦公室來進行這些事情等等。

--- 段落 521 (429 字元) ---
[indistinct] a good idea that somebody ought to  do, but I didn’t—At the time I was far more interested in the intelligence problems  and in this…different ways of looking at these issues of “doing well,” like the longterm competition set of ideas and in this application of these ideas coming out of  an organizational, almost social-cultural kind of perspective on these issues.- Q1: Did you also write a study of possible U.S.

[翻譯]
有個人應該去做的好主意，但我並沒有——當時我對情報問題更感興趣，以及不同角度看待這些"做得好"的議題，例如長期競爭理念集合以及這些理念應用在組織上，幾乎是從社會文化角度來看待這些問題。問題1：您是否也寫了一份可能的美國研究？

--- 段落 522 (324 字元) ---
responses to Soviet threats against  China with Richard Kennedy while working for Kissinger?- Marshall: It was almost a drafting of a little paper on the thing, appraisal for—Well,  and a recommendation about what we should do, I guess, which I didn’t think I  had any special competence in, but got dragged into by Kennedy.

[翻譯]
與理查德·肯尼迪一起為基辛格工作時，對蘇聯對中國的威脅做出反應-馬歇爾：這幾乎是對這件事情進行一點點草拟，對——評估以及我們應該做些什麼的建議，我想我並沒有特別的專業知識，但被肯尼迪拉進去了。

--- 段落 523 (463 字元) ---
- Q1: In Kissinger’s memoirs, and other sources, he mentions that at this time, early  1970, the NSC was doing a study of contingency planning for what the United  States should do if there were a war between the Soviet Union and China.- Marshall: Yes.- Q1: Now was this small effort that you and Kennedy worked on related to that?- Marshall: Well, I presume it was right at the beginning, because what he and I did, as  I remember, took place in December of ‘69.

[翻譯]
問1：在基辛格的回憶錄和其他資料中提到，當時在1970年初，NSC正在進行一項研究，探討如果蘇聯和中國發生戰爭，美國應該採取什麼樣的應變計劃。- 馬歇爾：是的。- 問1：那麼你和肯尼迪一起努力的這個小計劃是否與此有關？- 馬歇爾：我想應該是在開始階段，因為據我記得，他和我所做的是在1969年12月進行的。

--- 段落 524 (469 字元) ---
I came to kind of start this other stuff,  and was just kind of getting organized to do all of these studies and so on, etc.And this issue came up of the Russian—I don’t know, I forget—approaches to us,  but anyway, threats against the Chinese.- Q1: That was really in the late summer and fall of ‘69.- Marshall: That’s right.But somehow or another it had become an issue just at that  moment.And so, Kennedy indicated to me that Kissinger would like me to participate.

[翻譯]
我開始了這件事情的另一個部分，正在籌備進行所有這些研究等等。然後出現了俄羅斯對我們的威脅的問題，我不記得了，反正就是針對中國的威脅。這大概是在1969年秋天末期。肯尼迪告訴我，基辛格希望我參與其中。

--- 段落 525 (436 字元) ---
So it was kind of like being dragged off to the side, from the main thing I  was there to do, to just think through with him, you know, how should we react, what might we do and so on, and a little paper was prepared, which I participated  in the drafting of.And it was sent into Kissinger, and after that I never knew what  happened.- Q1: But what did you recommend in this short paper?- Marshall: I’m a little vague on that, you know.

[翻譯]
所以有點像是被拖到一邊，離開我本來要做的主要事情，只是和他一起思考，你知道，我們應該如何反應，可以做些什麼等等，並準備了一份小論文，我也參與了起草。然後這份文件被送到基辛格那裡，之後我就不知道發生了什麼事了。 - 問1：但在這份簡短的文件中，您推薦了什麼？- 馬歇爾：對此我有點模糊。

--- 段落 526 (423 字元) ---
But my guess is that one of the things  was, Well, you really ought to start some planning, some thinking what do you  really do if…I think it was kind of to discourage the Russians, but also think about  what you can do.But I don’t have any clear memory of that.- Q1: This is just for completeness.Make sure that what you want to say is in the book.- Marshall: Yes, right.- Q1: Could you talk about your work on deception?

[翻譯]
但我猜想其中一件事情是，嗯，你真的應該開始做一些規劃，一些考慮如果…我想這可能是為了嚇阻俄羅斯人，但也要考慮你可以做些什麼。但我對此並沒有清晰的記憶。- 問題1：這只是為了完整性。確保你想說的在書中有提到。- 馬歇爾：是的，沒錯。- 問題1：你能談談你對欺騙的研究嗎？

--- 段落 527 (360 字元) ---
- Marshall: I’d had this long-term interest in deception as a very important thing.And  probably when I was at the NSC, I forget whether I had any money to do it, but I  encouraged the people out at the Naval Postgraduate School, there were several  people out there who were interested in it, ended up with a—you know there’s a  volume on deception and so on.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：我對欺騙有這個長期的興趣，認為它是一件非常重要的事情。可能在我在NSC時，我不記得是否有資金去做這個事情，但我鼓勵了在海軍研究生院的人們，那裡有幾個人對這個感興趣，最終出現了一本有關欺騙等主題的著作。

--- 段落 528 (358 字元) ---
- Q1: So that grew out of your support for—  
- Marshall: Well encouragement, and then later I think I gave them money, I forget—  Right, yeah.- Q1: Anything else you want to say on that?- Marshall: No.- Q1: Alright.- Marshall: Except that it’s a big, important topic in which the intelligence community has been very slow and resistant to really looking at.

[翻譯]
問1：這是因為您對...的支持而產生的嗎？　　
Marshall：嗯，鼓勵，然後後來我想我給了他們錢，我忘記了，對，對。
問1：您對此還有其他想說的嗎？
Marshall：沒有。
問1：好的。
Marshall：除了這是一個重要的大題目，情報界一直很慢，很抗拒真正去研究這個問題。

--- 段落 529 (363 字元) ---
Not stuff that we would  do, but the fact that other people may do it, and one of the problems in the intelligence world is how to deal with that.It was one of the good things about Casey,  he understood what the real world was like.- Q1: Could you explain the line “Kissinger contrast of Chinese and Soviets” from the  notes for one of your talks on this period?

[翻譯]
並非我們會做的事情，而是其他人可能會做的事情，情報界面臨的問題之一就是如何應對這個問題。這也是凱西懂得實際世界情況的一個好處。Q1：您能解釋一下關於「學者對中國人和蘇聯人的對比」這句話在您談論這一時期的註解中的意思嗎？

--- 段落 530 (325 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, I remember when Kissinger came back from the ‘72—I mean the first  big official one that he went with Nixon… He had a meeting at which he briefed  a number of the people on the NSC.Maybe it was only those who had somehow  been involved in assisting the preparations.And I remember I did a few small  things.

[翻譯]
Marshall: 我記得基辛格從1972年回來時，和尼克松一起參加的第一個大型官方會議... 他召開了一個會議，向一些國家安全會議的人員匯報了情況。也許只有一些在準備工作中有所幫助的人參加了。我記得我做了一些小事。

--- 段落 531 (342 字元) ---
And he made this point about how good it was to deal with the Chinese,  who were, the way he put it, better than their word, as compared with the Soviets,  who are violating the treaty at the same moment they’re signing it.You know, I  mean [Marshall laughs].And also what a contrast…Not much…And also intellectually more interesting, better.

[翻譯]
他指出了與中國人打交道是多麼美好，他說中國人比起蘇聯來說更守信用，就像同時簽署條約卻又違反條約的蘇聯。你知道，我的意思是[馬歇爾笑了]。此外，這也是一個對比…沒有太多…而且在智識上更有趣，更好。

--- 段落 532 (492 字元) ---
- Q1: Who was the “AF gen” mentioned in the line “Tweedy/Helms reactions/role of  DCI/Intelligence Community staff, AF gen” from the notes for one of your talks on  this period?- Marshall: It may be a reference to Lew Allen, who was the first head of the Intelligence Community Staff and then later head of NSA.Both Schlesinger and I had  come to know him because he had been involved in the NRO space operations  and so on.92  
- Q1: How much contact did you have with Kissinger before 1969?

[翻譯]
問1：在你討論這個時期的一次演講筆記中提到的“AF gen”是指誰？“Tweedy/Helms reactions/role of DCI/Intelligence Community staff, AF gen”- 馬歇爾：這可能是指盧·艾倫，他是情報社區工作人員的首位負責人，後來成為NSA的負責人。舒萊辛格和我們都認識他，因為他曾參與NRO的太空行動等。92
- Q1：在1969年之前，你與基辛格有多少聯繫？

--- 段落 533 (489 字元) ---
- Marshall: Well, one that I—Well, very slim.I met him…He’d come to RAND…I forget  when it would be, probably the late ‘50s.I remember that he had been invited,  and there was a party for him up at the Wohlstetter’s and I remember being there,  shaking his hand and so on.But he’d also been at RAND, I mean that particular  visit, so I presume that would have been in… probably after this book of his in ‘57  [Nuclear Weapons and Foreign Policy] so it probably was the ‘58–’59 time period.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：嗯，有一個很瘦小的人。我遇到過他...他來過蘭德公司...我忘記是什麼時候，可能是50年代末。我記得他被邀請來參加Party，當時在沃爾斯特特家裡舉辦了一個Party，我記得當時在那兒，握了他的手等。但他也曾在蘭德公司，我指的是那次參訪，所以我推測那個時間應該是...可能在他的《核武器與外交政策》這本書出版後（1957年），所以應該是1958至1959年之間。

--- 段落 534 (247 字元) ---
But that’s the only two things I can remember.I mean—Right.But I mean I had no  real personal connection with him.- Q1: Can you think anything else about this period you’d like to…?- Marshall: [Laughs] No, I don’t think so.- Q1: I’ve asked enough.

[翻譯]
但這是我唯一能記得的兩件事。我的意思是—對。但是我和他沒有真正的個人聯繫。- Q1: 關於這段時間，你能想到其他任何事情嗎？- 馬歇爾：[笑] 不，我想沒有了。- Q1: 我問得夠了。

--- 段落 535 (5 字元) ---

1 Eds: This chapter includes four sections.The first two draw on consecutive interviews Guthe  conducted with Marshall in 1993 and 1994—the first covers 1969–1975, and is an interview  from 14 December 1993, the second covers 1973–1976, and is excerpted from an interview  from 8 April 1994.The first outline was prepared for the first interview, while the second outline is an excerpt of the relevant sections from the outline prepared for the second interview.

While on the staff of the Gaither Committee, Marshall was a member of a “small group  [of] people with systems analysis-analytical kinds of skills [that] worked as consultants and  experts to people in [the] other panels [and did] various kinds of tasks.” Transcript of interview  of Marshall by Goldberg and Matloff, 1 Jun 1992, 8.An organization chart for the committee  shows an “Evaluation Quantitative Assessments” group headed by Robert C.Prim (Bell Telephone Labs) and Stanley J.

[翻譯]
在蓋瑟委員會工作期間，馬歇爾是一個“一小群人，具有系統分析和分析技能，擔任其他小組的顧問和專家，從事各種工作。” 馬歇爾在1992年6月1日接受戈德堡和馬特洛夫的訪談中這樣說。委員會的組織圖顯示由羅伯特C.普瑞姆（貝爾電話實驗室）和斯坦利J.領導的“評估定量評估”小組。

56 In the SALT I negotiations, the United States hoped to prevent the replacement of the Soviet  SS-11 “light” (70 cubic meters in volume) ICBM with the SS-19 “heavy” (100 cubic meters in  volume) ICBM, a missile with substantially greater throw-weight.Toward this end, the U.S.

[翻譯]
在SALT I談判中，美國希望阻止蘇聯將SS-11「輕型」（體積70立方米）洲際彈道飛彈替換為SS-19「重型」（體積100立方米）洲際彈道飛彈，後者具有更大的有效載荷。為了達到這個目的，美國展開了努力。

--- 段落 584 (353 字元) ---
delegation made a statement (Unilateral Statement D) declaring that although “the Soviet  Delegation [had] not been willing to agree on a common definition of a heavy missile…[t]  he United States would consider any ICBM having a volume significantly greater than the  largest light ICBM [then] operational on either side [the SS-11] to be a heavy ICBM.

[翻譯]
代表團發表聲明（單方聲明D），宣布雖然「蘇聯代表團尚未同意就重型導彈的共同定義...美國將認為任何體積明顯大於兩邊當時最大輕型洲際彈道導彈（SS-11）的重型洲際彈道導彈為重型洲際彈道導彈。"

[翻譯]

officials were concerned that the  trawler might attempt to stop the unprotected ship from raising the submarine.Ford decided  the operation should proceed.Sections of the submarine were recovered and a “significant  amount of information was retrieved.” Gerald R.Ford, A Time to Heal: The Autobiography of  Gerald R.Ford (New York: Harper & Row Publishers, 1979), 135–136.
